## Curvature Agent 2 — Holonomy / Index Attack

### Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The curvature/holonomy pivot is not currently a viable replacement gate.}
}
\]

The obstruction
\[
\mathcal K(m)=C_{\rm geom}(m)\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)
\]
can be interpreted locally as the vertical defect of the \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C connection, but the current draft does **not** provide enough structure to promote
\[
\mathcal K(m)\,dm
\]
to a canonical global holonomy or index density. The failure is not just technical; it occurs at three levels:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no canonical cycle, no proved invariant density, and no theorem tying holonomy to off-line zeros.}
}
\]

This matches the strategic fork in the attached instruction: the current pointwise gate requires
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0,
\]
while a curvature/holonomy architecture would have to replace that gate with a genuinely global object. 

---

# 1. Local object under test

The local defect is

\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg},
\]

where

\[
C_{\rm geom}
=
a_1^2
\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi c(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}.
\]

The current Bottleneck-C gate is pointwise flatness:

\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

On a good patch,

\[
C_{\rm geom}\neq0,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}=0
\iff
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
}
\]

The proposed Branch B would replace this with something like

\[
\int_\Gamma \mathcal K(m)\,dm=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Hol}_T(\Gamma)=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Index}(\mathcal K)=0.
\]

That requires more than a local scalar coefficient. It requires a canonical path/cycle \(\Gamma\), a globally meaningful density, and a theorem connecting the resulting holonomy to RH-relevant zero geometry.

---

# 2. Candidate cycles and paths

## 2.1 Intervals between zero midpoints

Natural candidate:

\[
\Gamma=[m_i,m_{i+1}],
\]

where \(m_i\) are adjacent zero midpoints or Gram/core sampling centers.

Problem: this is not a cycle. The integral

\[
\int_{m_i}^{m_{i+1}} \mathcal K(m)\,dm
\]

depends on endpoint choice, core-window convention, and patch normalization. There is no current endpoint condition implying the boundary \(T\)-lift returns to itself. Therefore this is a **transport integral**, not a holonomy.

Possible use:

\[
T(m_{i+1})-T(m_i)
=
\int_{m_i}^{m_{i+1}}\mathcal K(m)\,dm
+
\text{lower-order transport terms}.
\]

But the draft does not establish a global transport equation of this form, and it does not identify canonical endpoint boundary values of \(T\).

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Intervals are natural, but they do not produce a canonical zero-holonomy condition.}
}
\]

---

## 2.2 Loops in phase/kernel parameter space

One might try to integrate around a closed loop in a space of parameters:

\[
(m,s,\kappa,\text{source window})
\]

or in the complexified \(m\)-plane.

Problem: the current object is a one-dimensional scalar density in \(m\), not a constructed curvature two-form on a parameter manifold. Also, the active row is symmetric in \(\eta_i,\eta_j\), so it is closer to a vertical second fundamental form than to an antisymmetric curvature form.

To get a genuine holonomy, one would need a connection one-form \(\omega_T\) on a bundle over a specified base \(\mathcal M\), then curvature

\[
F_T=d\omega_T+\omega_T\wedge\omega_T.
\]

The current coefficient is instead

\[
\partial_{\eta_i}\partial_{\eta_j}\omega_T(\partial_\kappa),
\]

a quadratic source-sector defect. This is not yet a two-form.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No loop holonomy exists until the base manifold and connection form are constructed.}
}
\]

---

## 2.3 Source-window deformation cycles

A tempting cycle is to move the core/source cutoff and return to the same window:

\[
R_0\to R_1\to R_0.
\]

If

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

is the full non-core zero complement, then this is the right place to look for a conservation law.

Problem: moving windows change the decomposition itself. The attached edits already record that if \(G_m(t)\) depends on \(m\), then

\[
A_4
=
\frac{1}{12}A_2''
-
\frac{1}{24}
\left(
\partial_m^2\partial_t^2
+
2\partial_m\partial_t^3
\right)G_m(t)\big|_{t=m}.
\]

Thus a moving-window cycle adds correction terms. These terms do not vanish automatically; they create an additional identity requirement.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-window cycles are possible only after proving covariance under moving-window corrections.}
}
\]

At present they do not provide a holonomy theorem.

---

## 2.4 Finite-core transport paths

The finite-core branch has natural sampled-vector transport paths. A curvature interpretation might try to identify

\[
\int \mathcal K\,dm
\]

with finite-core non-concentration or sampled-vector monodromy.

Problem: the finite-core data are downstream sampled vectors and determinant/non-concentration conditions. The current \(\mathcal K\) is a local Bottleneck-C vertical defect in the \(T\)-coordinate. No draft theorem identifies the finite-core connection with the \(T\)-connection.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-core paths are geometrically natural, but the draft does not tie their transport to }\mathcal K.
}
\]

---

## 2.5 Gram-block transport paths

Gram-block transport is closer to the local package geometry. One could imagine a loop in normalized Gram data and define \(T\)-holonomy.

Problem: the current obstruction is already after whitening and fixed-sector projection. A holonomy theorem would need to show that the whitening choices, \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-normalization, and \(S\)-basis are globally compatible.

This is exactly the transformation-law problem assigned to Curvature Agent 1. Without that, the integral

\[
\int \mathcal K(m)\,dm
\]

is gauge-dependent.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gram-block holonomy is the best conceptual candidate, but it requires a missing covariance theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Do known global zeta facts force holonomy zero?

No known fact in the current framework forces

\[
\int_\Gamma
C_{\rm geom}(m)\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)\,dm
=
0.
\]

The reason is structural.

The standard zeta global tools are mostly linear:

\[
\frac{\xi'}{\xi},\quad
\text{argument principle},\quad
\text{explicit formula},\quad
\text{zero-counting identities}.
\]

They control sums of zero contributions against test functions.

But

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]

is quadratic in the zero-complement moments:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

This is a quadratic pole-interaction density. Previous exactness and residue attacks were negative: it is not a natural midpoint derivative, and residue calculus at most gives global residue-sum cancellation, not pointwise or pathwise \(T\)-holonomy cancellation. 

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Known phase/argument-principle structure does not force zero holonomy for }\mathcal K.
}
\]

---

# 4. Do off-line zeros force nonzero holonomy?

Also no, not currently.

A useful RH proof gate would need something like:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{Hol}_T(\Gamma)\neq0,
\]

while global zeta consistency gives

\[
\operatorname{Hol}_T(\Gamma)=0.
\]

The present machinery does not establish the first implication.

Reasons:

1. **The defect is not off-line specific.**  
   The one-pair atom formula exists even on the critical-line subfamily. The far-pair asymptotic can still make
   \[
   A_4/A_2\approx0,
   \]
   while the required Bottleneck-C ratio is generally nonzero.

2. **Finite-tail models can produce local nonzero \(\mathcal K\)** without encoding a global RH obstruction.

3. **A signed integral can cancel even when the pointwise defect is nonzero.**  
   Nonzero local curvature does not imply nonzero total holonomy unless one proves a sign, positivity, or monotonicity theorem for \(\mathcal K\). No such sign theorem is present.

4. **Conversely, off-line zeros need not determine a unique sign or winding of \(\mathcal K\).**  
   The coefficient involves \(A_2A_4\), \(A_2^2\), \(q\), \(q''\), and normalization factors. There is no current index formula turning these into a zero-counting invariant.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is no proved implication from off-line zeros to nonzero }\mathcal K\text{-holonomy.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Relation to the quotient branch

The quotient branch uses the determinant coordinate

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]

or residual pairing

\[
ev_5-u_5f.
\]

This kills line shifts

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But the full transform branch sees

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2v_7.
\]

So the quotient branch is naturally interpreted as the **flat quotient connection**:

\[
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

while the full transform connection may have vertical \(T\)-curvature.

This is conceptually useful:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The curvature holonomy would measure exactly the lift ambiguity lost by quotienting.}
}
\]

However, this does not rescue the proof by itself. It only says:

- quotient data may be flat;
- full \(T\)-data may be curved;
- the difference is the lost vertical lift.

To make this a proof architecture, one must show either:

\[
\text{lost vertical lift is irrelevant to RH detection},
\]

or

\[
\text{lost vertical lift has a global holonomy/index contradiction}.
\]

Neither is currently proved.

---

# 6. Candidate replacement gate

The best possible Branch B gate would look like this.

Define, assuming covariance is later proved,

\[
\mathsf{Hol}_T(\Gamma)
:=
\int_\Gamma
C_{\rm geom}(m)\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)\,dm.
\]

Then replace pointwise Bottleneck-C flatness

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)=0
\]

with:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global }T\text{-holonomy gate: }
\mathsf{Hol}_T(\Gamma)=0.
}
\]

A full proof architecture would need two theorems:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global phase/finite-core consistency}
\Rightarrow
\mathsf{Hol}_T(\Gamma)=0.
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{existence of off-line zeros}
\Rightarrow
\mathsf{Hol}_T(\Gamma)\neq0.
}
\]

This is the clean replacement architecture.

But currently both theorems are missing, and even \(\Gamma\) is not canonical.

---

# 7. No-go for current holonomy replacement

Theorem-ready statement:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
Assume only the structures currently present in the draft: the local
Bottleneck-C defect
\[
\mathcal K=C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg},
\]
the fixed-sector \(T\)-coordinate, the quotient determinant branch, and the
standard zeta phase decomposition. Then \(\mathcal K(m)\,dm\) does not yet
define a canonical global holonomy density. No canonical cycle \(\Gamma\) is
specified, no transformation law proves gauge covariance under source-window,
core, whitening, or fixed-sector basis changes, and no global zeta theorem
forces
\[
\int_\Gamma \mathcal K\,dm=0.
\]
Nor is there a theorem that off-line zeros force nonzero \(\mathcal K\)-holonomy.
Therefore curvature/holonomy control cannot presently replace the pointwise
Bottleneck-C condition
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]
\end{minipage}
}
\]

---

# 8. What would make Branch B viable

Branch B becomes viable only if the next wave proves all four items:

## B1. Covariant density

\[
\mathcal K(m)\,dm
\]

must transform as a globally meaningful line-bundle-valued one-form under:

\[
m\mapsto \tilde m,
\]

core/source-window changes, whitening changes, and fixed-sector basis rescalings.

## B2. Canonical cycle

There must be a canonical \(\Gamma\), probably from one of:

\[
\text{Gram-block transport loop},
\quad
\text{finite-core sampling cycle},
\quad
\text{zero-counting contour},
\quad
\text{source-window deformation cycle}.
\]

## B3. Vanishing theorem

Global zeta/phase consistency must imply

\[
\int_\Gamma \mathcal K=0.
\]

## B4. Detection theorem

Off-line zeros must imply

\[
\int_\Gamma \mathcal K\neq0
\]

or a nonzero index.

Until these exist, Branch B is not an attack-ready proof path.

---

# 9. Final recommendation

Do not use curvature/holonomy as the next main branch yet.

The immediate priority is Curvature Agent 1’s transformation-law problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\,dm
\text{ even globally covariant?}
}
\]

If the answer is no, Branch B should be downgraded to a heuristic interpretation. If yes, then run a second wave on canonical cycles and vanishing/detection theorems.

For now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Curvature interpretation is useful diagnostically, but not yet a replacement for Bottleneck C.}
}
\]

The present architecture still requires the pointwise identity

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
}
\]

Understood: the attached instruction maps **Curvature Agent 2** to **Agent 2: Quotient Sampled Non-Concentration Agent**. I’ll execute that assignment. The prompt asks specifically for the quotient analogue of the finite-core sampled vector lower bound using quotient determinants \(D_{2r+1}\), not another attack on \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0\). 

# Agent 2 — Quotient Sampled Non-Concentration Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quotienting does not remove the sampled non-concentration problem.}
}
\]

It projects the old finite-core alignment branch
\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
\]
to the quotient branch
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

The quotient version is cleaner because it no longer asks for representative-level \(T\)-flatness, but it is **not easier in the decisive sense**. It still requires a new non-concentration theorem excluding small but nonzero quotient determinant vectors outside the quotient zero locus and quotient geometric incidence set.

The missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
}
\]

This is exactly the theorem assigned in the attached prompt. 

---

# 1. Quotient finite-core coefficients

Let

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S.
\]

Define the quotient determinant functional

\[
\omega_h(A,B)=u_Av_B-v_Au_B.
\]

Then

\[
D_{2r+1}
:=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

In particular,

\[
D_5=0,
\qquad
D_7=\Delta_7.
\]

The quotient finite-core vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1})(\theta).
\]

This is invariant under the representative shift

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

because

\[
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Thus \(C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\) is the correct no-\(T\) finite-core vector.

---

# 2. Quotient pair/interaction split

Assume the representative fixed-sector odd state splits as

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{2r+1}^{P,\mathfrak f}
+
A_{2r+1}^{J,\mathfrak f},
\]

where \(P\) is the pair-like or one-body part and \(J\) is the interaction part.

Define

\[
P_{2r+1}^{\quot}
:=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{P,\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

\[
J_{2r+1}^{\quot}
:=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{J,\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Then

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
P_{2r+1}^{\quot}
+
J_{2r+1}^{\quot}.
\]

So

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(P_7^{\quot},P_9^{\quot},\ldots,P_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\quot}),
\]

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(J_7^{\quot},J_9^{\quot},\ldots,J_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\quot}),
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
}
\]

This is the exact quotient analogue of the existing full-vector decomposition

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd},
\]

used in the finite-core sampled vector non-concentration section of the draft. The current full-vector branch already identifies calibrated interaction alignment \(J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}\) as the live obstruction. 

---

# 3. Quotient threshold

The natural quotient threshold should be calibrated from the same sampled transfer scale, with an additional fixed compact-patch norm factor for the quotient determinant map.

Let

\[
\Omega_5:\mathfrak f_h\to\mathbf C,
\qquad
\Omega_5(A)=\omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

On a compact good patch where \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq0\), define

\[
\|\Omega_5\|_{\Theta_k}
=
\sup_{\theta\in\Theta_k}\|\Omega_5(\theta)\|,
\]

and, if needed, a lower quotient-transverse scale

\[
\sigma_{\quot}(\Theta_k)
=
\inf_{\theta\in\Theta_k}
\|\Omega_5(\theta)|_{\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}}\|.
\]

Then the quotient threshold should be of the form

\[
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q)
=
C_{\quot,*}
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right),
\]

where \(C_{\quot,*}\) absorbs the quotient-transverse norm constants.

If quotient finite-core transfer is later proved with a different normalization, \(C_{\quot,*}\) changes, but the \(Q,m,N\)-scale is the same. Quotienting does not alter the sampled depth scale; it changes the coordinate in which the finite vector is measured.

---

# 4. Quotient zero locus and aligned branch

Define

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
:=
\{\theta\in\Theta_k:
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)=0\}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\theta\in\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
\iff
D_7=D_9=\cdots=D_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0.
\]

This means the finite odd fixed-sector states are projectively aligned with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) through the sampled finite-determinacy depth:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad
\text{for sampled odd orders}.
\]

Now define the quotient aligned branch:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q)
\right\}.
}
\]

The desired quotient sampled non-concentration theorem is exactly

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
}
\]

This is the quotient version of the old finite-core missing theorem. The attached background explicitly lists quotient sampled non-concentration as one of the main unresolved branches of the no-\(T\) architecture. 

---

# 5. Does quotienting make the problem easier?

## 5.1 What quotienting improves

Quotienting removes the representative-gauge direction

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So it correctly ignores variations that only change the discarded \(T\)-lift.

This is a genuine simplification: the quotient vector measures only projective failure of odd fixed-sector states to lie on the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line. It no longer tries to control \(v_{2r+1}\) itself.

Thus the no-\(T\) architecture avoids the specific \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C obstruction.

## 5.2 What quotienting does not improve

It does **not** remove finite-core cancellation. Since

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot},
\]

the same bad alignment pattern remains:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

This is the quotient projection of the old interaction-aligned branch. Nothing in the quotient determinant map prevents the pair-like determinant vector and interaction determinant vector from nearly cancelling.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quotienting removes the }T\text{-gauge direction but preserves the sampled cancellation problem.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Formal quotient good-patch small-vector model

Here is the formal obstruction model.

Let the quotient finite-core vector space be \(\mathbf R^M\), where

\[
M=R_{\Theta_k}.
\]

Choose a nonzero vector

\[
p\in\mathbf R^M,
\qquad
\|p\|_\infty\asymp 1.
\]

Let

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)=p,
\]

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)
=
-p+\varepsilon w,
\]

where

\[
0<\| \varepsilon w\|_\infty<\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q),
\]

and \(w\neq0\).

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
\varepsilon w.
\]

Hence

\[
0<
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]

So

\[
\theta_\varepsilon\notin\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
\]

but

\[
\theta_\varepsilon\in \mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q),
\]

unless an independent theorem forces this nearly cancelled configuration into

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]

This model is not claimed to be an actual zeta sample. It is the algebraic reason quotienting alone cannot prove the lower bound. The quotient determinant map does not forbid cancellation between \(P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\) and \(J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\).

Thus the missing theorem is not finite determinacy. It is an incidence or non-alignment theorem:

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\text{-smallness}
\Rightarrow
\theta\in\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Relation to existing finite-core branch

The draft’s full finite-core branch already states that projective detection and finite determinacy do not supply sampled size. The remaining obstruction is calibrated interaction alignment:

\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\approx -P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m)).
\]

The quotient version is the same statement after applying \(\Omega_5\):

\[
\Omega_5(J_{\rm fd})\approx -\Omega_5(P_{\rm fd}),
\]

i.e.

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

Therefore the quotient sampled non-concentration problem is not fundamentally easier. It is cleaner, but still open.

The previous finite-core audit already noted that compactness, finite determinacy, projective detection, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap control, and Łojasiewicz/Remez estimates do not by themselves eliminate the bad tube; they leave the aligned branch live. 

The quotient branch inherits that same weakness unless quotient geometry supplies a new incidence-containment theorem.

---

# 8. What theorem is actually needed?

The exact theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
For every compact nonsingular actual-source quotient stratum
\(\Theta_k^{\quot}\), there exist constants
\(Q_0(\Theta_k^{\quot})\), \(C_{\quot,*}>0\), and a controlled incidence set
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}\) such that for every actual zeta finite-core
sample \(\theta(m)\in\Theta_k^{\quot}\) and every \(Q\ge Q_0\),
\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
\end{minipage}
}
\]

A weaker but perhaps more attackable version is incidence containment:

\[
\boxed{
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

This would not prove raw non-concentration, but it would make smallness geometrically controlled.

---

# 9. Is quotient sampled non-concentration more plausible than the full version?

Only modestly.

## More plausible because

- It removes a false target: representative \(T\)-lift control.
- It measures projective determinant data, which is the natural no-\(T\) invariant.
- It may shrink the target space by quotienting line-gauge directions.
- It aligns with mixed four-point scalar exits, which are already quotient-level objects.

## Not more plausible because

- The determinant map is linear, so it preserves cancellation.
- Interaction alignment projects directly:
  \[
  J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
  \Rightarrow
  J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
  \]
- The quotient exceptional set must now absorb more geometry:
  line-gauge incidence, determinant degeneracy, and interaction-feature alignment.
- If quotient RH-detection is weaker, the lower bound may be easier to state but less useful.

So the quotient problem is cleaner but not solved.

---

# 10. Final result

\[
\boxed{
\text{The quotient sampled non-concentration theorem is a genuine new dependency.}
}
\]

I cannot prove the quotient lower bound from the current machinery. A formal quotient model shows that the same aligned branch persists:

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\approx0,
\qquad
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\neq0,
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\neq0.
\]

Therefore the quotient no-\(T\) architecture remains viable only if a new theorem controls this branch:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing
}
\]

or at least

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\subset
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

Until then, Branch C is coherent but blocked at quotient finite-core sampled non-concentration.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:42:09)

_Thought for 12s_

I’m Agent 2 here: **Quotient Sampled Non-Concentration Kill-Switch Agent**. The attached prompt asks whether the quotient aligned branch can be killed or forced into quotient incidence, not whether Bottleneck C can be repaired. 

# Agent 2 — Quotient Sampled Non-Concentration Kill-Switch

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\text{ is not killed by the current quotient machinery.}
}
\]

The no-\(T\) quotient architecture remains blocked by the same structural alignment problem:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

Quotienting removes the representative \(T\)-direction, but it does not create a mechanism forcing small quotient determinant vectors into

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]

Thus the required theorem remains missing:

\[
\boxed{
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

I do not find a proof of that containment from finite determinacy, quotient projection, Remez/Łojasiewicz bounds, or the current interaction geometry.

---

# 1. Quotient alignment has no automatic extra structure

The quotient finite-core vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1})
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot},
\]

where

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Since \(\omega_h(-,A_5^{\mathfrak f})\) is linear,

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
\omega_h(P_{\rm fd},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
\omega_h(J_{\rm fd},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Therefore the quotient alignment condition

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\]

is simply the projected version of the old alignment condition.

There is no new algebraic sign, positivity, or orthogonality constraint introduced by applying \(\omega_h(-,A_5^{\mathfrak f})\). It is a determinant projection. It kills the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line, but it does not prevent transverse cancellation.

So the quotient map removes one gauge direction but leaves the cancellation geometry intact.

---

# 2. Incidence containment is not currently available

The desired containment is

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

The current quotient incidence set should include at least:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
=
\{\text{endpoint collision, endpoint-gap failure, patch boundary, amplitude drop, whitening singularity, quotient determinant degeneracy, feature-rank drop, line-gauge degeneracy}\}.
\]

But smallness of

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\]

does not algebraically imply any of those incidence conditions.

It is an approximate cancellation condition between two nonzero quotient vectors. Unless the draft proves that the pair-vector and interaction-vector images lie in separated cones, transverse subspaces, or sign-definite sectors, the implication

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx0
\Rightarrow
\theta\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\]

does not follow.

No such cone separation is currently available.

---

# 3. Formal quotient good-patch model

A local formal model shows the obstruction.

Let the quotient finite-core target space be \(\mathbf R^M\), with

\[
M=R_{\Theta_k}^{\quot}.
\]

Choose generic nonzero vectors

\[
p,w\in\mathbf R^M,
\qquad
p\neq0,\quad w\neq0.
\]

Set

\[
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)=p,
\]

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)=-p+\varepsilon w,
\]

with

\[
0<\varepsilon\|w\|_\infty<\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]

Then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
\varepsilon w.
\]

Hence

\[
0<
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]

Also,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta_\varepsilon)\neq0,
\]

so

\[
\theta_\varepsilon\notin\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}.
\]

Now choose \(p,w\) generically so that no determinant degeneracy, feature-rank drop, endpoint collision, whitening singularity, or patch-boundary equation is satisfied. Since those incidences are algebraic or analytic closed conditions of positive codimension, a generic perturbation avoids them.

Thus, at the formal quotient-stratum level,

\[
\theta_\varepsilon
\in
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]

This is not a literal zeta-source counterexample. It is a **kill-switch formal model**: quotienting alone does not exclude the aligned branch. To close the branch, the proof needs a genuine actual-source incidence theorem.

---

# 4. Quotienting may make cancellation easier, not harder

The quotient map

\[
\Omega_5(A)=\omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]

reduces dimension by killing the line

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This has one benefit: it removes \(T\)-representative noise.

But it also has a cost: projected vectors have fewer coordinates, so accidental cancellation becomes **easier**, not harder.

A full-vector separation

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty\ge\Lambda
\]

could fail after projection even when the full vector is not small, because

\[
\Omega_5(P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd})
\]

can be small while

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]

has a large component in the discarded line.

Therefore quotienting does not strengthen non-concentration. It weakens the observable and demands a separate theorem that the discarded direction is RH-irrelevant.

So the quotient lower bound is not inherited from the old lower bound, even if the old lower bound were available.

---

# 5. Remez/Łojasiewicz does not close the branch

Finite determinacy gives an analytic quotient zero locus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
=
\{\theta:C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)=0\}.
\]

Łojasiewicz-type estimates can give a local inequality of the form

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge
c\,
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k^{\quot})^\mu
\]

on compact quotient strata.

But this does not imply an absolute lower bound

\[
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q)
\]

unless one also proves

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k^{\quot})
\ge
c'(m,Q).
\]

That distance lower bound is exactly the missing sampled non-concentration theorem in another form.

Similarly, Remez-type inequalities control analytic functions over intervals or sets of positive measure. They do not prevent a specific actual sample point from lying extremely close to \(\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\) unless the actual zeta sampling trajectory is known to avoid the corresponding bad tube.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remez/Łojasiewicz converts smallness into closeness to }
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot},
\text{ but does not exclude closeness.}
}
\]

At best it proves:

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\subset
\{\theta:
0<\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k^{\quot})
\lesssim
\Lambda_{\quot}^{1/\mu}
\}.
\]

It does not prove

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}=\varnothing.
\]

---

# 6. What would prove incidence containment?

The missing theorem must use actual quotient geometry, not formal analytic geometry alone.

A viable theorem would look like:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
For every compact good quotient stratum \(\Theta_k^{\quot}\), the actual zeta
sampling map \(\theta(m)\) cannot enter the calibrated aligned tube
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q)
\]
unless \(\theta(m)\) lies in the controlled quotient incidence set
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}\).
\end{minipage}
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
}
\]

To prove this, one of the following would be needed:

1. **Cone separation**
   \[
   P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
   \in \mathcal C_P,\qquad
   J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
   \in \mathcal C_J,\qquad
   \mathcal C_P\cap(-\mathcal C_J)=\{0\}
   \]
   outside incidence.

2. **Sign-definite determinant interaction**
   \[
   \langle P_{\rm fd}^{\quot},J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\rangle
   \ge0
   \]
   or an analogous non-cancellation inequality.

3. **Actual-source rigidity**
   forcing \(J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\) to be lower order or transverse to \(P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\).

4. **Incidence implication**
   \[
   J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
   \Rightarrow
   \text{feature-rank drop / determinant degeneracy / line-gauge incidence}.
   \]

None of these is currently in the draft.

---

# 7. Comparison with old full alignment

The quotient aligned branch is not identical to the old full aligned branch, but it is its direct projection.

Old branch:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}
=
\{0<\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|<\Lambda\}.
\]

Quotient branch:

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
=
\{0<\|\Omega_5(P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd})\|<\Lambda_{\quot}\}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}
\Rightarrow
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\]

is not automatic, and neither is the reverse. But the quotient branch is at least as dangerous because

\[
\Omega_5(P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd})
\]

can be small even if

\[
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}
\]

is not.

So quotienting does not eliminate the interaction-alignment mechanism. It moves it into a lower-dimensional determinant observable.

---

# 8. Kill-switch result

The no-\(T\) architecture requires quotient sampled non-concentration:

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Rightarrow
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{unproved and not implied by quotient finite determinacy.}
}
\]

Formal obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}=p,\qquad
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}=-p+\varepsilon w
}
\]

gives

\[
0<
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}
\]

outside the quotient zero locus, and generically outside incidence unless a new incidence theorem is proved.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The quotient architecture remains blocked by the aligned branch.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final theorem dependency

The exact dependency to record is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
The no-\(T\) quotient-determinant architecture requires a quotient sampled
non-concentration theorem. Namely, for actual zeta finite-core samples
\(\theta(m)\), one must prove
\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]
Equivalently, the calibrated quotient aligned branch
\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}
\]
must be empty or contained in
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]
At present, quotient finite determinacy and analytic Łojasiewicz/Remez
estimates only show that smallness places the sample near the quotient zero
locus; they do not exclude such closeness. A formal quotient model with
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
\]
shows the obstruction persists outside incidence unless a new actual-source
non-alignment theorem is supplied.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

## Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quotient sampled non-concentration is still a live kill switch.}
}
\]

The no-\(T\) quotient architecture should not be considered viable until either

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}=\varnothing
\]

or

\[
\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}\subseteq\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\]

is proved.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:54:38)

I’ll run **Agent 2: Split Scalar Analytic Pipeline Agent** from the attached prompt. I’ll treat canonicity of the whitening metric as a dependency from Agent 1, and focus on whether the split readout has the analytic/detection properties needed to replace the old scalar pipeline.

_Thought for 19s_

# Agent 2 — Split Scalar Analytic Pipeline Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right)
\]
is analytically viable as a **vector-valued fixed-sector readout**, provided the whitening inner product is canonical on the good patch. It fixes the pure-quotient detection failure because it sees both transverse determinant data and longitudinal \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line data.

But it is not a scalar miracle. It effectively restores the full two-dimensional fixed-sector state in a better coordinate system. Thus it also restores the burden of controlling the longitudinal component. Whether that longitudinal component avoids the old Bottleneck-C \(T\)-flatness obstruction is not decided by the analytic pipeline; that is the Agent 3/4 obstruction/connection question. The attached instruction frames this exact split-readout attack. 

---

## 1. Coefficient expansion

Let

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)
=
\sum_{r\ge 0} A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r+1}
+
\sum_{r\ge0} B_{2r}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r}
\]

on the fixed sector, where

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S.
\]

Let

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]

The quotient component is

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h\!\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right).
\]

Therefore its odd coefficients are

\[
H_{m,\odd}^{\quot}(s)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}D_{2r+1}s^{2r+1},
\]

with

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

In particular,

\[
D_5=0.
\]

The parallel component is

\[
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\frac{
\left\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\left\langle
A_5^{\mathfrak f},
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Its odd coefficients are

\[
H_{m,\odd}^{\parallel}(s)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}\lambda_{2r+1}s^{2r+1},
\]

where

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\left\langle
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\left\langle
A_5^{\mathfrak f},
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

In particular,

\[
\lambda_5=1.
\]

For anomaly tracking, the natural split finite-core vector begins after the normalizing order:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1},\lambda_{2R+1}).
\]

---

## 2. Holomorphy in \(s\)

Assume the original corrected fixed-sector object

\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)
\]

is holomorphic in \(s\) on the local sampling disk, as required by the existing finite-core pipeline.

Then both split components are holomorphic in \(s\), because they are obtained by applying fixed linear functionals in the fixed-sector fibre:

\[
A\mapsto \omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

and

\[
A\mapsto
\frac{\langle A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}.
\]

On a good patch,

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq0,
\qquad
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}\neq0,
\]

so the denominator is nonzero and independent of \(s\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
\text{ is vector-valued holomorphic in }s.
}
\]

The only caveat is not analytic but geometric: the whitening metric must be canonical enough in \(m\). That is Agent 1’s assignment.

---

## 3. Parity and odd projection

If the corrected fixed-sector object contains even leakage,

\[
\sum_{r\ge0}B_{2r}^{\mathfrak f}s^{2r},
\]

then both split components may also contain even terms.

The correct object for finite-core odd sampling is therefore

\[
\mathcal H_{m,\odd}^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\frac12
\left(
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
-
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(-s)
\right).
\]

This yields

\[
\mathcal H_{m,\odd}^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
\sum_rD_{2r+1}s^{2r+1},
\sum_r\lambda_{2r+1}s^{2r+1}
\right).
\]

So parity is not a blocker. At worst, one must explicitly pass to the odd part before applying the finite-core machinery.

---

## 4. Cauchy sampling and finite-core transfer

Cauchy estimates and sampling bounds apply componentwise.

If

\[
\mathcal H_{m,\odd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(H_{m,\odd}^{\quot},H_{m,\odd}^{\parallel}),
\]

then for any norm on \(\mathbf C^2\),

\[
\|\mathcal H_{m,\odd}^{\mathrm{split}}(s)\|
\]

is controlled by the two scalar holomorphic components. Standard Cauchy coefficient estimates apply to each coordinate:

\[
|D_{2r+1}|
\le
\frac{\sup_{|s|=\rho}|H_{m,\odd}^{\quot}(s)|}{\rho^{2r+1}},
\]

\[
|\lambda_{2r+1}|
\le
\frac{\sup_{|s|=\rho}|H_{m,\odd}^{\parallel}(s)|}{\rho^{2r+1}}.
\]

Thus the old finite-core sampling logic can be reused with a larger coefficient vector and adjusted constants.

The natural sampled vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots,D_{2R+1},\lambda_{2R+1}).
\]

This is analytically well-formed.

---

## 5. Detection: the split readout is complete on a good patch

The pure quotient scalar failed because

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

implies

\[
D_{2r+1}=0,
\]

even though

\[
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\lambda_{2r+1}v_5
\]

can be nonzero.

The split readout fixes this.

On a good patch, the map

\[
A\in\mathfrak f_h
\longmapsto
\left(
\omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\frac{\langle A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
\right)
\]

is injective, provided the whitening form is nondegenerate and \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\neq0\).

Reason: if both components vanish, then

\[
\langle A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}=0
\]

and

\[
\omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0.
\]

In a two-dimensional fixed-sector fibre, the first condition says \(A\) lies in the whitening-orthogonal line to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), while the second says \(A\) is symplectically dependent with \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), hence lies in \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). On a nondegenerate good patch, these two lines intersect only at \(0\). Therefore

\[
A=0.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
\text{ recovers }A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ on a good patch.}
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}\equiv0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_{\zeta,\odd}^{\corr}\equiv0
\]

on the fixed sector, modulo the same holomorphic finite-determinacy assumptions as the original vector-valued germ.

This is strictly stronger than pure quotient detection.

---

## 6. Relation to the old scalar \(H_m=\Phi_K(\cdots)\)

The old scalar

\[
H_m(s)
=
\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m))
\]

is a one-dimensional projection of the fixed-sector vector.

The split readout is not merely another scalar projection. It is a coordinate system for the full two-dimensional fixed-sector vector relative to

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}
\text{ detects every fixed-sector anomaly that }H_m\text{ can detect,}
}
\]

provided the anomaly lives in \(\mathfrak f_h\) and the split map is injective.

However, if the old proof used special one-variable scalar properties of \(H_m\)—for example a sign condition, scalar zero-counting, or a scalar argument-principle step—then those do not transfer automatically. One must replace them by a vector-valued finite-core statement or by scalarizing the vector norm:

\[
\|\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)\|^2
=
|H_m^{\quot}(s)|^2+|H_m^{\parallel}(s)|^2.
\]

That norm is not holomorphic, so it cannot be used directly in complex analytic zero-counting. But for finite-core coefficient sampling and non-concentration, componentwise holomorphy is enough.

So the replacement is viable for the finite-core analytic pipeline, but not automatically for any scalar argument-principle portion of the proof.

---

## 7. Finite determinacy for the split sequence

Because

\[
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
\]

recovers

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

the split zero locus is essentially the full fixed-sector zero locus:

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}
=
\{D_{2r+1}=0,\ \lambda_{2r+1}=0\ \forall r\}.
\]

Up to the normalization at order \(5\), the anomaly sequence should start at \(7\):

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}
=
\{D_{2r+1}=0,\ \lambda_{2r+1}=0\ \forall r\ge3\}.
\]

This is much smaller than the pure quotient zero locus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
=
\{D_{2r+1}=0\ \forall r\}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}
=
\mathcal Z_k
\]

at the level of fixed-sector odd anomalies, while

\[
\mathcal Z_k
\subsetneq
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
\]

generically.

Therefore finite determinacy for the split sequence follows from finite determinacy for the full fixed-sector vector, not from the weaker quotient-only determinacy.

The finite-depth theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
(D_7,\lambda_7,\ldots,D_{2R+1},\lambda_{2R+1})=0
\Longrightarrow
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad
\forall r\ge3.
}
\]

This is the correct split analogue.

---

## 8. Does the split scalar replace the failed pure quotient scalar?

Yes, for detection.

Pure quotient failure mode:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
\lambda_{2r+1}\neq0.
\]

Then

\[
D_{2r+1}=0,
\]

but

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}\neq0.
\]

Thus

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\]

can miss the anomaly, while

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}
\]

does not.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}
\text{ repairs the lost-}T\text{ detection failure of pure quotienting.}
}
\]

But this repair works by reintroducing the longitudinal line component. It does not prove that longitudinal motion is harmless.

---

## 9. Does it replace the old scalar pipeline?

Conditionally.

It can replace the old scalar pipeline if the proof only needs:

1. holomorphic coefficient extraction;
2. finite-order determinacy;
3. finite-core sampling;
4. detection of fixed-sector anomalies;
5. decomposition into pair and interaction pieces.

It does **not** automatically replace the old scalar pipeline if the proof needs:

1. scalar sign;
2. scalar argument-principle zero counting;
3. scalar positivity;
4. pointwise \(T\)-horizontal closure;
5. a scalar \(\Phi_K\)-visible contradiction.

For those, a new vector-valued or line-bundle argument is required.

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Analytic finite-core pipeline: viable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scalar contradiction pipeline: not automatically inherited.}
}
\]

---

## 10. Final answer

The split readout is the first replacement object that is analytically coherent and detection-complete:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
\omega_h(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
),
\frac{
\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
\right).
}
\]

It has odd coefficients

\[
\boxed{
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
}
\]

and, on a good patch with canonical nondegenerate whitening,

\[
\boxed{
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
\Longleftrightarrow
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

Therefore it fixes the pure quotient failure:

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\not\Rightarrow
H_m\equiv0.
\]

But it does so by restoring the longitudinal line component. Hence the remaining question is not analytic detection; it is geometric control:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the longitudinal component }\lambda_{2r+1}
\text{ be transported or controlled without reinstating the old }T\text{-flatness obstruction?}
}
\]

That is the next decisive attack.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:59:54)

_Thought for 11s_

I’ll execute this as **Agent 2: Bottleneck-C Longitudinal Transport Agent** from the attached line-bundle transport wave. The assigned question is whether the longitudinal split component \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) can be treated as transported line-bundle motion rather than a pointwise Bottleneck-C failure. 

# Agent 2 — Bottleneck-C Longitudinal Transport Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current data do not turn }\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ into harmless transport.}
}
\]

The line-bundle formulation is coherent as a coordinate system, but the Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) row enters the longitudinal component as an **inhomogeneous forcing term**. Unless a new global transport or boundary theorem is supplied, the current local gate still requires this forcing to vanish pointwise.

Thus the split readout currently **repackages** the old obstruction rather than eliminating it.

---

# 1. Longitudinal projection of the bad row

The active Bottleneck-C row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

The longitudinal projection along

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Let

\[
\Gamma_5
:=
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
}
\]

On a generic good patch,

\[
\Gamma_5\neq0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0
\]

unless the bad vector \(wI+uS\) is accidentally whitening-orthogonal to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). That orthogonality is an additional codimension-one incidence condition, not a structural cancellation.

---

# 2. Correct transport object

For a line section

\[
s=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

the candidate line connection is

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Thus

\[
\nabla^L s
=
(d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L)A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Along the exceptional collision direction \(\kappa\),

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
\partial_\kappa\lambda
+
\lambda\,\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa).
\]

So the correct candidate transport equation is not

\[
\partial_\kappa \lambda=0,
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda=0
}
\]

or, more generally,

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda=F_{\eta\eta}
}
\]

for some allowed forcing term.

---

# 3. Where the \(\eta\eta\) row enters

The bad row contributes to the split readout as an additive increment

\[
\delta\lambda_{\eta\eta}
=
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
\]

Therefore, at the level of the Bottleneck-C exceptional slope, the longitudinal transport equation has schematic form

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
+
\text{other lower-order / connection terms}.
\]

The key question is whether

\[
\lambda\,\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
\]

can cancel this forcing.

The answer is negative under the current local gate assumptions.

Reason: the connection term is **homogeneous in the existing line section** \(\lambda\), while the Bottleneck-C row is an **inhomogeneous new second-source forcing**. At the relevant residual order, the row is not generated by differentiating a pre-existing longitudinal component. It is produced by the promoted mixed-block second-\(\Delta\)-Hessian source.

Thus a connection correction can only cancel it if the draft proves a specific identity:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\,\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
=
+\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
}
\]

with matching source grade, scalar grade, endpoint symmetry, and fixed-sector profile.

No such identity is currently available.

---

# 4. Why lower-order gates do not supply the cancellation

Lower-order gates can ensure that earlier components merge or vanish in the appropriate quotient/fixed sector. But this does not automatically create a compensating connection term at the \(\eta\eta\), order-seven, Bottleneck-C row.

The needed compensation would have to satisfy all of the following:

\[
\text{same }\eta_i\eta_j\text{ source profile},
\]

\[
\text{same }Q^{-14}\text{ homogeneity},
\]

\[
\text{same fixed-sector vector }(wI+uS)\text{ projected along }A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

\[
\text{same exceptional }\kappa\text{-slope},
\]

and

\[
\text{opposite coefficient}.
\]

The previous frozen-row and endpoint/carrier audits found this row isolated in the local table. Recasting it in the \(\lambda\)-coordinate does not create a new physical row; it only projects the same row onto the line \(L\).

So the connection term

\[
-\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
\]

is not a free counterterm. It must be derived from the same finite-\(s\) package. In the current derivation, no such same-grade compensator exists.

---

# 5. Curvature versus forcing

The longitudinal defect is best classified as a **forcing / second fundamental form term**, not as harmless curvature.

A curvature term would arise from commutators of covariant derivatives:

\[
F_L(X,Y)
=
d\alpha_L(X,Y).
\]

But the active Bottleneck-C row is symmetric in the two source directions:

\[
\eta_i\eta_j.
\]

So it is not directly an antisymmetric curvature two-form. It is better written as a quadratic source-sector forcing:

\[
B_L(\eta_i,\eta_j;\partial_\kappa)
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
B_L(\eta_i,\eta_j;\partial_\kappa)
}
\]

at the bad row.

This is transportable only if the proof is rebuilt to allow a nonzero right-hand side and control its global accumulation. The current Bottleneck-C gate does not do that. It demands local closure.

---

# 6. If nonzero forcing is allowed, what theorem is needed?

A valid replacement gate would need to say:

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
B_L
\]

is not a failure, because \(B_L\) is globally controlled.

There are three possible forms.

## 6.1 Prescribed transport law

One could require

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
\]

and then show this equation is compatible with the global zero geometry.

But that only restates the forcing unless paired with boundary data.

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\text{ at the target boundary is determined by integrating }B_L
\text{ and gives the RH contradiction.}
}
\]

## 6.2 Zero holonomy / boundary cancellation

One could try:

\[
\int_\Gamma B_L\,d\kappa=0
\]

or

\[
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)=1.
\]

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global zeta phase consistency forces zero longitudinal holonomy,}
}
\]

while

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zeros force nonzero longitudinal holonomy.}
}
\]

No such theorem is currently present.

## 6.3 Exact covariant derivative

One could try to show

\[
B_L=\nabla^L_\kappa \Psi
\]

for some canonical potential \(\Psi\), so the forcing is a boundary term.

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
=
\nabla_\kappa^L\Psi
}
\]

with canonical \(\Psi\). Prior exactness attacks were negative for the scalar obstruction. The line-bundle version would need a genuinely new potential.

---

# 7. Pointwise closure reduces to the old obstruction

If the split architecture demands pointwise closure of the longitudinal component,

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\]

then generically

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

Since the split readout is locally complete, demanding both components vanish,

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\qquad
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\]

is equivalent to

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

That is stronger than the old scalar condition in coordinate form, but for the active row it hits the same obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise split closure requires killing the same Bottleneck-C row.}
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }\lambda\text{ must vanish pointwise, the split architecture fails for the same reason as Bottleneck C.}
}
\]

---

# 8. The exact replacement Bottleneck-C gate

The only viable replacement would be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Longitudinal Bottleneck-C transport gate}
}
\]

with the form

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda_{7}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\Gamma_5
}
\]

or, including the physical scalar,

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda_{7}
=
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}).
}
\]

Then the proof must replace local flatness by one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global endpoint constraint for }\lambda_7,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero holonomy of }(L,\nabla^L),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{index/winding theorem for the longitudinal forcing,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-core non-concentration theorem using }(D,\nabla^L\lambda)
\text{ rather than }(D,\lambda).
}
\]

Without one of these, the transport law is only a restatement of the obstruction.

---

# 9. Final theorem-ready statement

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
Let \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) and assume a canonical whitening
connection
\[
\alpha_L=
\frac{\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}.
\]
For a line coordinate
\[
\lambda(A)=
\frac{\langle A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}},
\]
the Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) residual
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
has longitudinal component
\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}.
\]
On a generic good patch this is nonzero whenever \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\neq0\).
The connection term
\(\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)\) is homogeneous in the existing line
section and does not, in the current derivation, supply a same-grade
inhomogeneous compensator. Therefore pointwise split closure is equivalent to
killing the same Bottleneck-C row. A genuine line-bundle architecture would
need to replace pointwise closure by a new global transport, boundary, or
holonomy theorem for \(\nabla^L\lambda\).
\end{minipage}
}
\]

## Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{The longitudinal Bottleneck-C defect is not currently transportable.}
}
\]

The split readout remains promising only if the next stage proves a global line-bundle theorem controlling

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
\]

or its holonomy. Without that theorem, the split architecture inherits the old Bottleneck-C obstruction.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:05:06)

_Thought for 5s_

I’m Agent 2 here: **Covariant Bottleneck-C Forcing Equation Agent**. The assigned task is to determine whether the Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) defect defines a covariant forcing term in \(\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda\), or whether pointwise vanishing is still required. 

# Agent 2 — Covariant Bottleneck-C Forcing Equation

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Bottleneck-C longitudinal defect is covariant only as a line-valued forcing term, not as a closed transport law.}
}
\]

More sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
\text{ can be packaged as a section of }L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\text{ but the current proof gives no equation allowing it to be nonzero.}
}
\]

Thus, inside the current local architecture, pointwise vanishing is still required. A line-bundle transport architecture would need a new theorem of the form

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta}
\]

together with global boundary, holonomy, or exactness control for \(F_{\eta\eta}\). That theorem is not currently present.

---

# 1. The longitudinal section

The bad Bottleneck-C row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

Define

\[
\Gamma_5
:=
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Then

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
\]

The associated line section is

\[
s_{\eta\eta}
:=
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So explicitly,

\[
\boxed{
s_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\Gamma_5
A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

This is the correct line-bundle form of the longitudinal Bottleneck-C defect.

---

# 2. Scaling covariance

Under a line-frame rescaling

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

assuming the whitening metric is conformally compatible, we have

\[
\Gamma_5\mapsto \mu^{-1}\Gamma_5,
\]

because the numerator scales by \(\mu\) and the denominator by \(\mu^2\), in the real-positive scaling case. Hence

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\mapsto \mu^{-1}\lambda(E_{\eta\eta}).
\]

Therefore

\[
s_{\eta\eta}
=
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is invariant:

\[
s_{\eta\eta}
\mapsto
(\mu^{-1}\lambda(E_{\eta\eta}))(\mu A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
s_{\eta\eta}.
\]

Thus the forcing is well-behaved **as a line-valued section**.

\[
\boxed{
s_{\eta\eta}\in\Gamma(L)
\text{ is the covariant object, not the scalar }\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ alone.}
}
\]

This is a useful positive result.

---

# 3. Covariant derivative of the defect section

The candidate connection is

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

For a line coordinate \(\lambda\),

\[
\nabla^L\lambda
=
d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L.
\]

Along \(\kappa\),

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
\partial_\kappa\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
+
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa).
\]

Substituting

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
\right)
-
\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5\,
\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa).
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi}
\left[
\partial_\kappa(q^{-3}\nu_{\eta\eta}\Gamma_5)
+
q^{-3}\nu_{\eta\eta}\Gamma_5\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
\right].
}
\]

This is a well-defined covariant derivative **if** the line connection itself is globally covariant.

But it does not vanish automatically.

---

# 4. Which local gate is correct?

There are three possible gates.

## Gate A: pointwise longitudinal vanishing

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0.
\]

Generically,

\[
\Gamma_5\neq0,
\]

so this gives

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

That is the old Bottleneck-C obstruction.

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\text{ is not a new architecture.}
}
\]

It just restates the old pointwise obstruction in split coordinates.

---

## Gate B: covariant flatness of the defect

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0.
\]

This is weaker than pointwise vanishing, but it is not currently justified as the Bottleneck-C closure condition.

It would mean the defect section is parallel along \(\kappa\). But the original Bottleneck-C gate did not ask for parallel transport of the residual; it asked for no residual vertical drift.

So this is a new gate. It requires a theorem explaining why parallel longitudinal residuals are harmless for RH detection.

No such theorem is currently in the draft.

---

## Gate C: forced transport equation

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta}.
\]

Here

\[
F_{\eta\eta}
=
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
\]

This is the only genuinely new line-bundle architecture:

\[
\boxed{
\text{allow the Bottleneck-C row as covariant forcing.}
}
\]

But then one needs a global theorem controlling the solution of

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta}.
\]

Without endpoint, holonomy, exactness, or sign/index control, this is just a restatement of the defect.

---

# 5. Does \(\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)\) cancel the forcing?

The connection term is

\[
\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa).
\]

To cancel the bad row, one would need

\[
\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
=
+\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
\]

There is no current mechanism forcing this.

The reason is structural:

\[
\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
\]

is homogeneous in the existing line coordinate \(\lambda\), while

\[
\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
\]

is an inhomogeneous second-source forcing from the promoted mixed-block \(\eta_i\eta_j\) row.

Thus cancellation would require a new identity matching:

\[
\text{same source grade},
\quad
\text{same scalar grade},
\quad
\text{same }\eta_i\eta_j\text{ profile},
\quad
\text{same fixed-sector projection},
\quad
\text{opposite coefficient}.
\]

That is precisely the kind of same-row cancellation already absent in the frozen Bottleneck-C table.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
\text{ does not currently supply a compensating Bottleneck-C term.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Is \(F_{\eta\eta}\) tensorial?

As a scalar,

\[
F_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5
\]

has weight \(\mu^{-1}\) under

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto\mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Therefore it is not an ordinary scalar. It is a coordinate of a line-valued section.

The invariant object is

\[
F_{\eta\eta}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
=
s_{\eta\eta}.
\]

So the correct forced equation is not

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa\lambda=F_{\eta\eta}
\]

as an equality of scalars unless both sides are understood in the same line-frame. The coordinate-free version is:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L_\kappa s
=
s_{\eta\eta}
}
\]

or, for the coordinate \(\lambda\),

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}\Gamma_5.
}
\]

This is covariant under line-frame rescaling.

Positive conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
F_{\eta\eta}\text{ is covariant as a line-bundle forcing coordinate.}
}
\]

Negative conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Covariance alone does not make the forcing harmless.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Does this replace Bottleneck C?

Not yet.

The original Bottleneck-C closure was a local condition:

\[
\partial_\kappa T=0.
\]

The forced line-bundle equation is a dynamical condition:

\[
\nabla^L_\kappa s=s_{\eta\eta}.
\]

For this to replace Bottleneck C, the proof must supply one of the following.

## 7.1 Boundary-value cancellation

A theorem of the form:

\[
s(b)-\operatorname{PT}_{a\to b}s(a)
=
\int_a^b \operatorname{PT}_{t\to b}s_{\eta\eta}(t)\,dt,
\]

with canonical boundary values forcing contradiction.

Missing: canonical endpoints and boundary conditions.

## 7.2 Holonomy control

A theorem of the form:

\[
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)=1
\]

but

\[
\int_\Gamma s_{\eta\eta}\neq0
\]

under off-line zeros.

Missing: canonical cycle \(\Gamma\) and off-line-zero holonomy theorem.

## 7.3 Exact forcing

A theorem of the form:

\[
s_{\eta\eta}
=
\nabla^L\Psi
\]

for canonical \(\Psi\), reducing the defect to boundary terms.

Missing: exactness identity.

## 7.4 Sign/index forcing

A theorem of the form:

\[
s_{\eta\eta}
\text{ has sign/index incompatible with global phase structure.}
\]

Missing: sign or index structure.

Without one of these, the forced equation is not a proof gate.

---

# 8. The no-go inside the current architecture

Inside the current local package, the only available closure condition is still pointwise vanishing.

If we require the residual line section to vanish,

\[
s_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

then, on a generic good patch,

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

Since prior ODE/exactness/residue/source attacks did not prove

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

the old obstruction remains.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The line-bundle formulation is a coordinate upgrade, not a closure proof.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Theorem-ready statement

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
Assume \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is equipped with the connection
\[
\alpha_L=
\frac{\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}.
\]
The Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) row
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
defines a line-valued forcing section
\[
s_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
This section is covariant under rescaling of the line frame
\(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto\mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). In coordinates it yields
the forced transport equation
\[
\partial_\kappa\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa)
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]
However, no current lower-order gate supplies an opposite same-grade connection
term, and no boundary, holonomy, exactness, or index theorem controls the
forcing. Therefore the present local architecture still requires
\(s_{\eta\eta}=0\), which generically reduces to
\(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\).
\end{minipage}
}
\]

## Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Bottleneck-C defect is covariant as line-bundle forcing, but not yet transport-controlled.}
}
\]

The line-bundle program remains viable only if a subsequent theorem proves that the forced transport equation has canonical global boundary, holonomy, exactness, or index control. Otherwise the architecture collapses back to pointwise Bottleneck-C vanishing.
