## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:05:34)

_Thought for 6s_

I’m Agent 2 here: **Fixed-Sector Projection Non-Annihilation Agent**. The assigned question is whether \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) can annihilate all off-line packet contributions to the fixed-sector odd germ, creating an open family with \(C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0\). 

# Agent 2 — Fixed-Sector Projection Non-Annihilation Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is no structural reason for }\pi_{\mathfrak f}\text{ to annihilate all nondegenerate off-line packet contributions.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(\text{off-line packet contribution})\not\equiv0
}
\]

is strongly supported by the existing Bottleneck-C row calculation, because the same class of source data produces a fixed-sector vector

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h
\]

with nonzero \(I\)- and \(S\)-components whenever \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\neq0\). Thus complete projection annihilation would contradict the already-derived existence of a fixed-sector source row unless the packet lies on an additional incidence locus.

However, I cannot upgrade this to a complete theorem without the exact draft formula for \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) and the full coefficient map

\[
\text{packet jets}\longmapsto A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed-sector invisibility is a proper analytic incidence condition, not a generic open phenomenon, conditional on the existing row formulas being source-realizable.}
}
\]

---

# 1. Projection target

The dangerous failure is

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\qquad
\forall r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\]

for a genuine off-line packet

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)=\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,
\qquad
\beta\neq\frac12.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
=0.
\]

The question is whether this could hold identically on an open off-line packet family, outside already controlled incidence.

---

# 2. Fixed-sector projection model

The fixed-sector projection has the schematic form

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z)
=
\text{fixed / transpose-invariant part of }Z.
\]

In a two-by-two local block, the fixed sector is spanned by

\[
I,\qquad S,
\]

so for a local matrix coefficient \(Z\),

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z)
=
z_I I+z_S S.
\]

In the simplest schematic form one expects something like

\[
z_I=\frac{Z_{11}+Z_{22}}2,
\]

and \(z_S\) is a fixed off-diagonal or symmetric off-diagonal coordinate, depending on the draft’s exact fixed-sector convention.

The key point is that \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) is a linear projection onto a two-dimensional sector. For it to annihilate every off-line packet contribution, the entire packet-induced odd germ would have to lie in

\[
\ker \pi_{\mathfrak f}
\]

to all sampled odd orders.

That is a strong analytic constraint, not a consequence of conjugation or functional-equation symmetry alone.

---

# 3. Evidence from the known Bottleneck-C row

The strongest available evidence is the active row itself.

The Bottleneck-C computation already produces a fixed-sector row

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

This is explicitly in

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

Thus

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(E_{\eta\eta})
=
E_{\eta\eta}.
\]

For a good patch where

\[
wI+uS\neq0
\]

and

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}\neq0,
\]

we have

\[
E_{\eta\eta}\neq0.
\]

Therefore the same source architecture that creates the off-line/source obstruction does produce nonzero fixed-sector projection.

The row coefficient is

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
\sim
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2
\right],
\]

or in the rebuilt source convention,

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
\]

Prior work found that actual exterior-pair source shapes can approximate the bad finite-jet germ \(r=u^2\). For such source jets, \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\) is generically nonzero. Hence the fixed-sector projection is not generically annihilated.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The existing Bottleneck-C row is itself a witness against generic fixed-sector invisibility.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Symmetry does not force \(\ker\pi_{\mathfrak f}\)

Functional-equation and conjugation symmetry package the off-line zero as

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)
=
\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\}.
\]

These symmetries impose reality, pairing, and parity relations on the local source atoms. They do **not** force the local packet contribution into the anti-fixed sector.

If they did, then every symmetry-closed packet contribution would satisfy

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(\text{packet contribution})=0.
\]

But the Bottleneck-C row is built from symmetry-compatible source data and still lands in

\[
\mathfrak f_h.
\]

Thus the symmetries can cancel some components, and they can force internal packet ties, but they do not annihilate the whole fixed-sector projection.

The only way symmetry could force invisibility is on special loci such as:

\[
\beta=\frac12,
\]

where the packet collapses onto the critical-line configuration, or on special midpoint/endpoint parity loci. Those are incidence boundaries, not open off-line families.

---

# 5. Analytic non-annihilation argument

Let local packet/core/sample parameters be

\[
(\beta,\gamma,m,s,\theta).
\]

Each fixed-sector coefficient

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is an analytic or meromorphic-analytic function of these parameters on a reduced good stratum, after excluding collision, endpoint collapse, and Gram singularity.

The invisibility condition is

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\qquad
(3\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}).
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]

is an analytic incidence locus.

To show it does not contain an open off-line family, it suffices to exhibit one point in the off-line parameter family where at least one coefficient is nonzero.

The existing Bottleneck-C row supplies a formal witness at order \(7\) or the corresponding finite sampled order, provided the bad source jets are realized or approximated by actual off-line packet jets. Prior one-pair/far-tail work supports this: actual exterior zero-pair source functions have free enough finite jets and can approximate the formal \(r=u^2\) germ.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

on the nondegenerate off-line packet stratum, conditional on the source-realization link between the packet jet expansion and the Bottleneck-C fixed-sector row.

---

# 6. Exceptional cases where projection may vanish

Projection non-annihilation is not unconditional. Vanishing can occur on controlled loci.

## 6.1 Critical-line collapse

If

\[
\beta=\frac12,
\]

then the off-line displacement vanishes and the symmetry packet collapses. This is not the off-line case.

Include it in the RH-boundary / critical-line incidence.

## 6.2 Special midpoint parity

At special midpoints, e.g.

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]

some odd or mixed packet jets may vanish by parity.

This does not imply all fixed-sector odd coefficients vanish for all nearby \(m\). It is a wall or subvariety in midpoint space.

Include it in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]

if it kills the finite sampled vector.

## 6.3 Endpoint symmetry

Certain endpoint choices

\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2
\]

may force cancellation in fixed-sector projection. Such conditions are analytic equations in \(s\) and \(m\), not generic identities.

## 6.4 Gram / whitening singularity

If whitening degenerates, the fixed-sector projection may become ill-defined or artificially zero. This is already in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}.
\]

## 6.5 Insufficient finite order

It is possible that a particular off-line packet first appears at an order above the chosen finite depth

\[
R_{\Theta_k}.
\]

This is the main finite-determinacy dependency. If finite determinacy is correctly calibrated, this should not occur outside incidence. But it must be proved by Agent 3’s first-nonzero finite-order analysis.

---

# 7. The actual theorem we can support

A theorem-ready conditional statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
On a reduced good stratum, the fixed-sector coefficient map
\[
(\beta,\gamma,m,s,\theta)
\longmapsto
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\]
is analytic. Functional-equation and conjugation symmetry do not force its image
to lie in \(\ker\pi_{\mathfrak f}\). The known Bottleneck-C fixed-sector row
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
provides a nonzero fixed-sector witness whenever \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\ne0\) and
\(wI+uS\ne0\). Therefore fixed-sector invisibility is a proper analytic
incidence condition, not an open condition on nondegenerate off-line packet
families, provided the off-line packet jets realize the same finite source
directions used in the Bottleneck-C row.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

---

# 8. What remains missing

The remaining missing piece is the exact realization theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line packet jets feed the Bottleneck-C/fixed-sector coefficient map in the same finite directions used by }E_{\eta\eta}.
}
\]

Equivalently, one needs a concrete formula showing that for

\[
\beta\neq\frac12
\]

there is some finite order \(2r+1\le 2R_{\Theta_k}+1\) such that

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\neq0
\]

outside controlled incidence.

Without that formula, this agent’s result is conditional.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-sector projection non-annihilation is strongly supported and should be treated as a proper-incidence theorem, not a generic failure.}
}
\]

But the fully rigorous statement still depends on two items:

1. the exact formula for \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) in the latest draft;
2. the first finite-order visibility theorem linking off-line packet jets to nonzero

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So Agent 2’s conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\text{ does not structurally annihilate off-line packets; any full invisibility belongs in }
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\text{ and should be a proper analytic incidence locus.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:09:59)

_Thought for 11s_

# Agent 2 — Clean Parameter Witness Evaluator

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is a clean order-7 nonzero witness in the local packet-jet model.}
}
\]

At

\[
x_m=0,\qquad \delta=\frac14,\qquad q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1,
\]

the source moments satisfy

\[
A_2\ne0,\qquad A_4\ne0,
\]

the septic locking equation fails, and therefore

\[
\nu\ne0.
\]

This gives a concrete analytic witness for nonzero order-7 fixed-sector visibility, subject to the standard caveat that \(q=1,q''=0,Q=1\) are good-patch/local-model normalizations unless separately realized by an actual zeta packet. The attached instruction asks specifically for such a clean parameter witness. 

---

## 1. Parameter choice

Take

\[
\delta=\frac14,
\qquad
\beta=\frac34.
\]

Then

\[
a=\frac12-\delta=\frac14,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta=\frac34.
\]

At the centered point

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]

use the packet source moments:

\[
A_2
=
-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
A_4
=
16(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

---

## 2. Compute \(A_2\)

\[
a^{-3}=4^3=64,
\]

\[
b^{-3}=\left(\frac43\right)^3=\frac{64}{27}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_2
=
-4\left(64+\frac{64}{27}\right)
=
-4\left(\frac{1792}{27}\right)
=
-\frac{7168}{27}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27}\ne0.
}
\]

---

## 3. Compute \(A_4\)

\[
a^{-5}=4^5=1024,
\]

\[
b^{-5}=\left(\frac43\right)^5=\frac{1024}{243}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_4
=
16\left(1024+\frac{1024}{243}\right)
=
16\cdot\frac{249856}{243}
=
\frac{3997696}{243}.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243}\ne0.
}
\]

---

## 4. Check septic locking

The locking condition is

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q''}{18q}.
\]

At

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,
\]

the right side is

\[
\frac{10}{9}.
\]

But

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{3997696/243}{-7168/27}
=
-\frac{3904}{63}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
-\frac{3904}{63}
\ne
\frac{10}{9}.
}
\]

So the septic locking condition fails.

---

## 5. Compute \(\nu\)

With

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1,
\]

the order-7 coefficient becomes

\[
\nu
=
\frac{1}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}\left(-\frac23\right)A_2^2
=
\frac{1}{240}A_2A_4
-
\frac{1}{216}A_2^2.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\nu
=
A_2^2
\left(
\frac{1}{240}\frac{A_4}{A_2}
-
\frac{1}{216}
\right).
\]

Substitute

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}=-\frac{3904}{63}.
\]

Then

\[
\nu
=
A_2^2
\left(
-\frac{3904}{15120}
-
\frac{1}{216}
\right).
\]

Both terms in the parenthesis are negative, and

\[
A_2^2>0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\nu<0,
}
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
\nu\ne0.
}
\]

---

## 6. Interpretation

This is a clean nonzero order-7 witness:

\[
\boxed{
\delta=\frac14,\quad x_m=0,\quad q=1,\quad q''=0,\quad Q=1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_2\ne0,\ A_4\ne0,\ \nu\ne0.
}
\]

The witness also fails the locking equation decisively:

\[
-\frac{3904}{63}
\ne
\frac{10}{9}.
\]

Therefore the order-7 fixed-sector coefficient is not identically zero in the corresponding analytic local model.

---

## 7. Caveat

The choice

\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1
\]

should be treated as a **good-patch local-model normalization** unless another agent verifies that these values are realized by an actual reduced off-line zeta packet. For the analytic non-identity argument, this is still useful: it shows that the coefficient formula itself is not algebraically identically zero.

To convert this into the full packet-visibility theorem, the remaining step is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{verify that this witness lies in, or is analytically connected to, the actual reduced off-line packet family.}
}
\]

---

## Final result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 2 produces a nonzero }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{-level witness.}
}
\]

The invisibility locus

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]

therefore cannot be an algebraic identity of the order-7 coefficient formula. It is at most a proper analytic incidence locus, conditional on actual-packet realization of the same local parameter regime.

# Agent 2 — Core/Source Comparison and Absorption Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The source-moment }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ witness does not automatically transfer to the actual reduced-core chart.}
}
\]

Moving the off-line packet from source to core changes the coefficient map, not merely its notation. The nonzero source-chart row is a valid analytic witness for the source-moment model, but it is **not yet certified** as a witness for the actual reduced-core coefficient

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The remaining bridge is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
+
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\neq -A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

At present, no theorem in the draft proves this non-cancellation. The attached coordinator prompt correctly identifies this as the realization gap between the source-moment witness and the actual reduced-core coefficient map. 

---

## 1. Two coefficient maps

There are two different local constructions.

### Source chart

\[
q=q_{\base}+G,
\qquad
\mathcal P(\rho)\subseteq G.
\]

The packet contributes through affine-subtracted source moments:

\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The order-7 fixed-sector source row is

\[
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
\supset
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]

with

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

For the clean witness

\[
\delta=\frac14,\quad x_m=0,\quad q=1,\quad q''=0,\quad Q=1,
\]

we have

\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243},
\]

and

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}\ne0.
\]

So

\[
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]

provided

\[
wI+uS\ne0.
\]

### Reduced-core chart

\[
q=q_{\core}+G_{\rm nc},
\qquad
\mathcal P(\rho)\subseteq q_{\core}.
\]

Now the same packet contributes to the **baseline/core finite-\(s\) model**, not to the non-core source variables. The coefficient is

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
\]

This is a different coefficient map unless the draft proves split-independence.

---

## 2. The comparison formula

The relevant difference is

\[
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
-
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This difference receives contributions from at least six places:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\Delta_{\rm base}
+
\Delta_{\rm aff}
+
\Delta_{\rm Gram}
+
\Delta_{\rm proj}
+
\Delta_{\rm norm}
+
\Delta_{\rm recenter}.
}
\]

More explicitly:

1. **Baseline jet change**
   \[
   q_{\base}\mapsto q_{\base}+q_\rho.
   \]

2. **Source moment removal**
   \[
   G\mapsto G-q_\rho,
   \]
   so the source moments change as
   \[
   A_2\mapsto A_2-\frac{q_\rho''(m)}2,
   \qquad
   A_4\mapsto A_4-\frac{q_\rho^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
   \]

3. **Affine subtraction change**
   The packet is no longer affine-subtracted as a source:
   \[
   r_\rho(t)
   =
   q_\rho(t)-q_\rho(m)-q_\rho'(m)(t-m)
   \]
   disappears from the non-core source variables.

4. **Gram / whitening change**
   The core model changes, so the Gram block and whitening matrix may change.

5. **Fixed-sector projection change**
   If the corrected local model changes, the projection
   \[
   \pi_{\mathfrak f}
   \]
   may act on a different fixed-sector decomposition.

6. **Core re-centering / normalization**
   The local baseline quantities
   \[
   q,\quad q'',\quad Q,\quad w,\quad u
   \]
   may change.

None of these terms is known to vanish.

---

## 3. Does the difference cancel \(E_{\eta\eta}\)?

To certify the source witness in the reduced-core chart, we need to rule out

\[
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-E_{\eta\eta}.
\]

At present, there is no structural reason this equality should hold. But there is also no theorem ruling it out.

The danger is real because moving a packet into the core changes precisely the variables appearing in the source-row coefficient:

\[
q,\quad q'',\quad A_2,\quad A_4.
\]

In the source chart, \(A_2,A_4\) are non-core source moments. In the core chart, those derivatives are absorbed into baseline/core geometry. Thus the row may be redistributed into baseline terms, connection terms, or normalization terms.

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No cancellation theorem, but also no survival theorem.}
}
\]

The nonzero source witness is not yet an actual reduced-core witness.

---

## 4. Gate A/B do not force equivalence

Gate A and Gate B are intra-chart local algebra statements under a fixed source/core convention.

They do not imply

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

They also do not imply

\[
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

Nor do they imply that moving a packet between source and core is a \(GL_2\)-frame transition.

Earlier source/core functoriality analysis already showed that such a move is at best affine:

\[
A_{2r+1,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G^{-1}A_{2r+1,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{\rho,2r+1}.
\]

Here

\[
B_{\rho,7}
=
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is exactly the term under audit.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B cannot certify the realization bridge.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Is core absorption harmless, incidence, or open invisibility?

Current evidence suggests **proper incidence**, but this is not yet proved.

### Why not obviously harmless

The coefficient map changes when the packet moves into the core. So core absorption is not merely notation.

### Why not obviously open invisibility

The source-row formula gives a nonzero analytic witness in a closely related chart. For an open-family invisibility mechanism to exist, the reduced-core construction would need a structural identity cancelling all such order-7 fixed-sector contributions for every nondegenerate off-line packet.

No such identity has been found.

### Best current classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{core absorption is a realization gap; any full cancellation should be treated as an analytic incidence condition unless a structural identity is proved.}
}
\]

But to make that rigorous, we need the direct reduced-core formula for

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

---

## 6. The theorem needed

The exact bridge theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
For a nondegenerate off-line packet \(\mathcal P(\rho)\subset q_{\core}\), the
actual reduced-core order-7 fixed-sector coefficient satisfies
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
+
R_{7,\core},
\]
where \(R_{7,\core}\) does not cancel the displayed term identically on the
reduced off-line packet family. In particular, for at least one reduced good
parameter choice,
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]
\end{minipage}
}
\]

A weaker but sufficient theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

on each nondegenerate reduced off-line packet component.

---

## 7. If \(A_7\) cancels

If a direct computation shows

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\equiv0
\]

for actual reduced-core packets, then we must test

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The reason is that the centered off-line packet has higher nonzero even moments:

\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})\ne0
\]

for

\[
0<|\delta|<\frac12.
\]

So a full invisibility theorem would need to cancel not just \(A_7\), but the entire finite odd fixed-sector sequence:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=A_9^{\mathfrak f}=\cdots=A_{2R+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

That is much stronger and should be treated as an analytic incidence unless forced by explicit symmetry.

---

## 8. Final result

\[
\boxed{
\text{The source witness does not yet prove actual reduced-core visibility.}
}
\]

The comparison gives:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
+
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
}
\]

and the unproved statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\neq
-A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ identically.}
}
\]

Therefore the next decisive computation remains Agent 1’s direct reduced-core derivation:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
}
\]

Until that computation is done, packet visibility is still **conditional**, not closed.

# Actual Reduced-Core \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) Derivation Agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered source-moment }A_2A_4\text{ witness is not yet certified as an actual reduced-core }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ witness.}
}
\]

The direct reduced-core septic analysis in the draft shows that the canonical order-\(7\) fixed-sector quotient is controlled by the **septic \(K_1\)-transport sector**, not by copying the source-chart \(\eta\eta\) Hessian row into the core chart. In particular, pure same-point septic terms vanish in the odd two-point germ, and normalization shadows only add a multiple of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). Thus the raw \(A_2A_4\) centered numerator computation is **not** the final \(A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\). This is exactly the realization bridge the attached prompt asks us to test. 

However, the actual reduced-core analysis does give a different positive witness: the draft’s septic \(K_1\)-transport formula has a nonzero direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven fixed-sector slice. Therefore an off-line packet with

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\neq 0
\]

has a certified actual reduced-core order-\(7\) visibility channel on the quintic-generic patch. The centered witness \(x_m=0\) has \(q^{(7)}(m)=0\) by parity, so it is the wrong point for this certified reduced-core channel.

So the best current result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual reduced-core visibility is certified generically via the }q^{(7)}\text{ septic }K_1\text{ channel, but not by the centered }A_2A_4\text{ source witness.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Reduced-core object

In the reduced-core convention,

\[
q=q_{\core}+G_{\rm nc},
\qquad
\mathcal P(\rho)\subseteq q_{\core}.
\]

The coefficient under test is

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_{\zeta}^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
\]

The draft decomposes the septic fixed-sector coefficient schematically as

\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

After fixed-sector projection,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

with

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The \(K_3\)-shadow vanishes after fixed-sector projection, and the pure same-point septic sector vanishes in the odd two-point germ. Therefore the canonical quotient-level septic data satisfy

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in }
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Thus the actual reduced-core order-\(7\) visibility test must pass through

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

not through the raw source-chart \(\eta\eta\) Hessian formula alone.

---

## 2. Centered core expansion

Let

\[
u=t-m.
\]

At a centered packet,

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]

the core phase derivative has an even expansion:

\[
q_{\core}(m+u)
=
q_0
+
\frac{q_2}{2}u^2
+
\frac{q_4}{24}u^4
+
\frac{q_6}{720}u^6
+
\frac{q_8}{40320}u^8+\cdots.
\]

For the paired atom,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}+\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
a=\frac12-\delta,\quad b=\frac12+\delta,
\]

with \(x=2t-\gamma\). At \(x_m=0\),

\[
A_2=\frac{q_2}{2}
=
-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3}),
\]

\[
A_4=\frac{q_4}{24}
=
16(a^{-5}+b^{-5}).
\]

For

\[
\delta=\frac14,\qquad a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\]

we get

\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\]

\[
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243}.
\]

Also,

\[
A_6=\frac{q_6}{720}
=
-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})
=
-\frac{2294284288}{2187}\neq0.
\]

These core jets are definitely nonzero. So core absorption does **not** erase the packet at the raw jet level.

---

## 3. Raw finite-\(s\) order-\(7\) numerator

For

\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\]

with

\[
\Delta
=
q_0s+\frac{q_2}{24}s^3+\frac{q_4}{1920}s^5+\frac{q_6}{322560}s^7+\cdots,
\]

\[
q_-
=
q_0+\frac{q_2}{8}s^2+\frac{q_4}{384}s^4+\frac{q_6}{46080}s^6+\cdots,
\]

the supplied raw coefficient is

\[
[s^7]\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
=
\frac{q_0^9}{36288}
-\frac{q_0^6q_2}{1728}
+\frac{q_0^4q_4}{4608}
+\frac{5q_0^3q_2^2}{3456}
-\frac{q_0^2q_6}{64512}
-\frac{q_0q_2q_4}{4608}
-\frac{5q_2^3}{41472}
+\frac{q_8}{9289728}.
\]

Substituting

\[
q_2=2A_2,\qquad q_4=24A_4,
\]

the visible \(A_2A_4\) and \(A_2^2\) channels inside this raw coefficient include

\[
-\frac{q_0A_2A_4}{96}
\]

and

\[
\frac{5q_0^3A_2^2}{864},
\]

along with additional channels

\[
\frac{q_0^4A_4}{192},
\qquad
-\frac{5A_2^3}{5184},
\qquad
-\frac{q_0^2q_6}{64512},
\qquad
\frac{q_8}{9289728},
\]

and lower pure \(q_0,q_2\)-dependent terms.

So the raw reduced-core finite-\(s\) numerator **does contain nonzero packet-jet channels**. But this raw coefficient is not yet the final

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

It still must pass through the corrected odd-germ construction, whitening, normalization, and fixed-sector projection.

---

## 4. Raw witness evaluation

There are two useful evaluations.

### 4.1 Packet-only centered value

For the packet alone at \(x_m=0\),

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1}
=
4+\frac43
=
\frac{16}{3}.
\]

Using the centered packet values for \(q_2,q_4,q_6,q_8\), the raw coefficient evaluates to

\[
[s^7]\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
=
\frac{20143144960}{19683}\neq0.
\]

Thus the raw reduced-core numerator is nonzero for the actual centered packet.

### 4.2 Normalized local-model value

If one instead uses the local-model normalization

\[
q_0=1,
\]

while retaining the packet’s nonzero higher jets, the same raw coefficient evaluates to

\[
\frac{262153916261603}{714256704}\neq0.
\]

This shows the raw coefficient is not algebraically zero. But it should be treated as a model normalization unless the draft’s normalization permits setting \(q_0=1\) independently of the packet contribution.

---

## 5. Why this does not yet certify final \(A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\)

The raw numerator computation is not the final reduced-core coefficient.

The draft’s septic fixed-sector analysis says:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
+
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

where

\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}
\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

and

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}].
\]

Moreover, pure same-point septic terms vanish in the odd germ:

\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

The centered raw \(A_2A_4\) calculation is a same-point even-core computation. Therefore it is not automatically part of the canonical quotient-level \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) after odd projection and whitening.

This is the key point:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The raw centered }A_2A_4\text{ coefficient is nonzero, but the draft’s actual septic package may project it away unless it enters through a transport channel.}
}
\]

So the centered \(A_2A_4\) source-moment witness is **not** by itself a certified actual reduced-core \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) witness.

---

## 6. Certified actual reduced-core visibility channel: \(q^{(7)}\)

The draft does provide a certified actual reduced-core order-\(7\) channel: the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven septic \(K_1\)-transport slice.

On the graded slice

\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(7)}),
\]

the fixed-sector septic contribution is \(I\)-directional:

\[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
\]

and

\[
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv0
\]

on the generic one-pair region.

The corresponding residual determinant satisfies

\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}
=
u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5,
\]

so if

\[
v_5\not\equiv0,
\]

then

\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv0.
\]

This is an actual reduced-core \(A_7\)-level visibility statement, not merely a source-moment statement.

---

## 7. Does an off-line packet have \(q^{(7)}(m)\neq0\)?

At the centered point

\[
x_m=0,
\]

the packet is even, so

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0.
\]

Thus the centered witness cannot use the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel.

But for a non-centered midpoint,

\[
x_m\neq0,
\]

the seventh derivative of

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
\]

is generically nonzero.

For example, with

\[
\delta=\frac14,
\qquad a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\qquad x_m=1,
\]

one gets

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
-\frac{78820552794808879146860544}
{212883222686767578125}
\neq0.
\]

So the actual reduced-core packet has a nonzero \(q^{(7)}\)-visibility channel at non-centered good midpoints.

This is enough to prove non-identity on any connected reduced packet family allowing \(x_m\neq0\), provided the point remains in the reduced good set and \(v_5\neq0\).

---

## 8. What happens to the centered witness?

For the centered packet,

\[
x_m=0,
\]

all odd derivatives of the even packet function vanish:

\[
q^{(1)}(m)=q^{(3)}(m)=q^{(5)}(m)=q^{(7)}(m)=\cdots=0.
\]

So the certified \(q^{(7)}\)-transport slice is unavailable.

The centered raw numerator still has nonzero \(A_2,A_4,A_6,A_8\) channels, but whether those survive the actual corrected odd fixed-sector package is not resolved by the current draft formulas quoted above. The prompt’s \(A_2A_4\) source-chart row cannot simply be copied into the reduced-core chart.

Thus for the centered witness:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\text{ remains unproved.}
}
\]

For a non-centered packet:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv0
\text{ is supported by the direct }q^{(7)}\text{ septic }K_1\text{ theorem.}
}
\]

---

## 9. \(A_9\) fallback

If one insists on the centered witness \(x_m=0\), then \(A_9\) or higher order remains the correct fallback.

At the centered packet,

\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})\neq0.
\]

For \(\delta=\frac14\),

\[
A_6=-\frac{2294284288}{2187}\neq0.
\]

If the actual order-\(9\) fixed-sector formula contains an \(A_6\)-channel that is not killed by odd projection or normalization, then centered-packet visibility can be certified at order \(9\).

But the actual \(A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\) formula is not present in the material used here. Therefore the centered \(A_9\) fallback remains a precise next computation, not a solved theorem.

---

# Final deliverable

## B. Visibility conditionally certified

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual reduced-core visibility is certified generically via the non-centered }q^{(7)}\text{ septic }K_1\text{ channel.}
}
\]

The certified statement is:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\neq0,\qquad v_5(m)\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
[A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}]\neq0
\]

on the generic one-pair/reduced-core region.

For an off-line packet, \(q^{(7)}(m)\) is generically nonzero when \(x_m\neq0\). Therefore

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
\]

on the corresponding reduced off-line packet family, assuming the reduced good-patch conditions allow a non-centered midpoint.

## But the centered \(A_2A_4\) witness is not certified

At

\[
x_m=0,
\]

the packet has strong nonzero even jets

\[
A_2,A_4,A_6,\ldots,
\]

and the raw finite-\(s\) numerator is nonzero. But the actual corrected order-\(7\) fixed-sector package may project pure same-point even-core septic terms away. The source-chart \(\eta\eta\) row is not automatically the reduced-core row.

So the centered witness remains conditional until either:

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is derived for the \(A_2A_4\)-channel, or

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is computed and shown to contain a surviving \(A_6\)-channel.

---

## Exact next step

If the rank-two route accepts non-centered reduced good patches, proceed: packet visibility is conditionally certified by the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel.

If the architecture requires centered packets, then compute:

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^9]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_{\zeta}^{\corr,\core}(s;m)
\]

and isolate the \(A_6\)-channel.

# Continued Attack — Centered \(A_9\) Fallback

## 1. Raw \(s^9\) coefficient

For the lower-left off-diagonal numerator,

\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2},

using the centered even expansion

\[

=

we have

\[
\Delta
=
q_0s+\frac{q_2}{24}s^3+\frac{q_4}{1920}s^5+\frac{q_6}{322560}s^7+\frac{q_8}{92897280}s^9+\frac{q_{10}}{40874803200}s^{11}+\cdots,

and

\[
q_-
=
q_0+\frac{q_2}{8}s^2+\frac{q_4}{384}s^4+\frac{q_6}{46080}s^6+\frac{q_8}{10321920}s^8+\frac{q_{10}}{3715891200}s^{10}+\cdots.

A direct expansion gives:

\begin{aligned}

={}&
-\frac{q_0^{11}}{3326400}
+\frac{q_0^8q_2}{80640}

-\frac{q_0q_4^2}{614400}
-\frac{q_2^2q_4}{184320}
+\frac{q_{10}}{3406233600}.

-

It also contains additional source-moment channels:

\frac{q_0^3A_2A_4}{480},

\frac{q_0^2A_2^3}{1728},

and

Thus order \(9\) is not controlled merely by the septic locking relation involving

\[
A_2,\quad A_4,\quad q,\quad q''.

It sees genuinely higher packet data.

## 3. Centered packet \(A_6\) is nonzero

=

So the centered off-line packet has a strong nonzero \(A_6\)-channel.

---

## 4. The \(A_6\)-channel is generically nonzero

The raw \(A_6\)-channel vanishes only if

\[
\frac{q_0^4}{896}-\frac{q_0A_2}{448}=0.
\]

Equivalently, assuming \(q_0\neq0\),

\[
q_0^3=2A_2.
\]

That is a single analytic locking condition.

For the clean packet-only centered value,

\[
q_0=a^{-1}+b^{-1}
=
4+\frac43
=
\frac{16}{3},
\]

and

\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27}.
\]

Then

\[
q_0^3
=
\left(\frac{16}{3}\right)^3
=
\frac{4096}{27},
\]

while

\[
2A_2
=
-\frac{14336}{27}.
\]

So

\[
q_0^3\neq 2A_2.
\]

Therefore the \(A_6\)-channel is nonzero at the clean packet-only centered point.

---

## 5. What this proves and does not prove

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The raw reduced-core }s^9\text{ expansion has a nonzero centered off-line packet channel.}
}
\]

More specifically, if the actual corrected \(A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\) retains any nonzero projection of the raw \(A_6\)-channel, centered packet visibility follows.

But this does **not** yet prove:

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\neq0.
\]

The missing operation is still:

\[
[s^9]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_{\zeta}^{\corr,\core}(s;m),
\]

including the actual order-\(9\) correction map, whitening, Gram normalization, and fixed-sector projection.

---

## 6. Strategic implication

We now have two visibility routes:

### Route A — non-centered order \(7\)

If the reduced architecture permits a non-centered midpoint

\[
x_m\neq0,
\]

then

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\neq0
\]

generically, and the draft’s septic \(K_1\)-transport channel gives actual reduced-core order-\(7\) visibility.

This is currently the cleaner route.

### Route B — centered order \(9\)

If centered packets are required, then

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0,
\]

but

\[
A_6\neq0.
\]

The raw \(s^9\) coefficient has a nonzero \(A_6\)-channel. The exact next computation is whether the corrected fixed-sector order-\(9\) map keeps that channel.

---

## Final conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered fallback attack succeeds at the raw finite-}s\text{ level.}
}
\]

The next precise theorem to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The actual corrected }A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\text{ contains a nonzero projection of }
A_6\left(\frac{q_0^4}{896}-\frac{q_0A_2}{448}\right).
}
\]

If yes, then centered packet visibility is certified. If no, the obstruction has moved one level higher and the next target is the first corrected odd order whose raw channel uses a packet moment not killed by centering and not removable by correction.

# Continued Attack — Non-Centered \(q^{(7)}\) Visibility Route

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{If non-centered reduced good patches are allowed, packet visibility is essentially certified at order }7.
}
\]

The centered packet \(x_m=0\) kills the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-channel by parity, forcing us toward the harder \(A_9\) fallback. But the reduced-base architecture does **not** intrinsically require \(x_m=0\). If we choose a nearby non-centered midpoint

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma\ne0,
\]

then the actual packet has

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0
\]

outside a finite analytic zero set. The draft’s actual reduced-core septic \(K_1\)-transport channel then gives a nonzero order-\(7\) fixed-sector witness, provided the standard good-patch conditions hold:

\[
v_5\ne0,\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,\qquad Q\ne0.
\]

So the visibility theorem should pivot from the centered \(A_2A_4\) witness to the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-witness. The attached derivation prompt identified \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) as the first target and \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) only as fallback. 

---

## 1. Exact seventh derivative channel

For a single packet component

\[
g_c(x)=\frac{c}{c^2+x^2},
\qquad x=2t-\gamma,
\]

we have

\[
\frac{d^7}{dt^7}g_c(x)
=
-5160960\,
\frac{
c\,x\,(x^2-c^2)(x^4-6c^2x^2+c^4)
}{
(c^2+x^2)^8
}.
\]

Therefore for the paired packet

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\]

with

\[
a=\frac12-\delta,\qquad b=\frac12+\delta,
\]

we get

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
-5160960x_m
\left[
\frac{
a(x_m^2-a^2)(x_m^4-6a^2x_m^2+a^4)
}{
(a^2+x_m^2)^8
}
+
\frac{
b(x_m^2-b^2)(x_m^4-6b^2x_m^2+b^4)
}{
(b^2+x_m^2)^8
}
\right].
\]

This is an analytic function of \((\delta,x_m)\). It is not identically zero for

\[
0<|\delta|<\frac12.
\]

---

## 2. Centering is the problem, not invisibility

At the centered midpoint

\[
x_m=0,
\]

the expression has the explicit factor \(x_m\), so

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0.
\]

That is a parity artifact of centering the packet, not a structural fixed-sector invisibility theorem.

For non-centered \(m\),

\[
x_m\ne0,
\]

the seventh derivative is generically nonzero. Its remaining zeros are the finite analytic set cut out by

\[
\frac{
a(x_m^2-a^2)(x_m^4-6a^2x_m^2+a^4)
}{
(a^2+x_m^2)^8
}
+
\frac{
b(x_m^2-b^2)(x_m^4-6b^2x_m^2+b^4)
}{
(b^2+x_m^2)^8
}
=0.
\]

This is another controlled incidence condition, not an open invisibility mechanism.

---

## 3. Explicit nonzero packet witness

For the clean off-line packet

\[
\delta=\frac14,
\qquad
a=\frac14,
\qquad
b=\frac34,
\]

choose

\[
x_m=1.
\]

Then

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
-\frac{
78820552794808879146860544
}{
212883222686767578125
}
\ne0.
\]

Thus the actual packet has a nonzero seventh core derivative at a non-centered midpoint.

This is a stronger reduced-core witness than the centered raw \(A_2A_4\) calculation, because it uses the actual reduced-core \(q^{(7)}\)-transport channel instead of importing the source-chart \(\eta\eta\) Hessian row.

---

## 4. Compatibility with reduced-good-patch conditions

The non-centered choice must still satisfy:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

same-scale packet bounds,

endpoint separation,

Gram/whitening nondegeneracy,

and fixed core stability.

Moving \(m\) slightly away from the centered value changes these conditions continuously. Therefore, if the centered packet lies in the interior of the same-scale and strict-gap region, then sufficiently small nonzero \(x_m\) remains in

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

If the centered point lies exactly on a wall, choose a nearby point away from the wall. The bad sets are analytic or semianalytic walls:

\[
x_m=0,
\]

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0,
\]

\[
d_k=d_{k+1},
\]

\[
\det G_{\core}=0,
\]

endpoint collision, and same-scale boundary.

A finite union of such walls cannot fill a two-parameter admissible \((m,s)\)-neighborhood unless one condition is identically forced. The \(q^{(7)}\) condition is not identically forced.

Thus the reduced-good-patch existence theorem should be amended:

\[
\boxed{
\text{choose }m\text{ non-centered unless the proof specifically needs centering.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Consequence for packet visibility

The draft’s actual reduced-core septic result says the \(q^{(7)}\)-driven \(K_1\) transport slice contributes to the order-\(7\) fixed-sector coefficient, with a nonzero quotient determinant when

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0
\]

and

\[
v_5\ne0.
\]

So the visibility implication is:

\[
\boxed{
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,\quad v_5(m)\ne0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0
}
\]

modulo the already accepted septic \(K_1\)-transport formula.

For the non-centered packet witness above, the left side is satisfied outside standard good-patch incidence.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

on the nondegenerate reduced off-line packet family.

---

## 6. What remains if centering is mandatory

If the architecture insists on

\[
x_m=0
\]

for every RH-relevant packet, then the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel is unavailable and we must continue the \(A_9\) fallback.

The raw \(s^9\) coefficient has a nonzero \(A_6\)-channel:

\[
A_6\left(\frac{q_0^4}{896}-\frac{q_0A_2}{448}\right),
\]

and for the clean centered packet,

\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})\ne0.
\]

But the corrected \(A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\) formula is still required to certify that channel after whitening and projection.

So the split is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{non-centered route: order }7\text{ visibility is available;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{centered-only route: order }9\text{ remains the next computation.}
}
\]

---

## Final conclusion

The strongest continuation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not center the packet. Use the actual }q^{(7)}\text{ septic }K_1\text{ channel.}
}
\]

Then packet visibility becomes conditionally certified under the reduced-good-patch assumptions:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ with }
x_m\ne0,\quad q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,\quad v_5\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
}
\]

The remaining theorem is now an avoidance statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant packets admit a reduced good patch avoiding the analytic walls }
x_m=0,\ q^{(7)}=0,\ v_5=0.
}
\]

That is much more tractable than deriving the centered \(A_9\) formula.

# Continued Attack — Non-Centered Visibility Avoidance Theorem

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The non-centered }q^{(7)}\text{ route is viable on any reduced packet stratum with genuine midpoint freedom.}
}
\]

The remaining visibility theorem reduces to an avoidance statement:

\[
\exists (m,s)\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\quad\text{such that}\quad
x_m\ne0,\quad q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,\quad A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0.
\]

This is now plausible because all failures are analytic or semianalytic walls. The key condition is that \(m\) is not rigidly forced to be the packet center. The previous prompt explicitly framed packet visibility as the remaining bridge before the rank-two connection theorem. 

---

## 1. The new exceptional walls

For the non-centered order-\(7\) route, enlarge the reduced exceptional set by

\[
\mathcal E_{7\text{-vis}}^{\core}
=
\{x_m=0\}
\cup
\{q^{(7)}(m)=0\}
\cup
\{A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}=0\}
\cup
\{v_5=0\}
\]

if the determinant/quotient witness uses \(v_5\), or more generally

\[
\{A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}=0\}
\]

if we use the full rank-two vector witness directly.

Then define

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,7}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{7\text{-vis}}^{\core}.
\]

The goal becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,7}.
}
\]

Equivalently, each nondegenerate off-line packet should admit a reduced good patch outside these walls.

---

## 2. \(q^{(7)}\) is not identically zero

For

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

we derived

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
-5160960x_m
\left[
\frac{
a(x_m^2-a^2)(x_m^4-6a^2x_m^2+a^4)
}{
(a^2+x_m^2)^8
}
+
\frac{
b(x_m^2-b^2)(x_m^4-6b^2x_m^2+b^4)
}{
(b^2+x_m^2)^8
}
\right].
\]

For the clean off-line packet

\[
\delta=\frac14,\qquad a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34,
\]

at

\[
x_m=1,
\]

we computed

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\neq0.
\]

Therefore

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
\]

is not the zero function on the off-line packet family. Its zero set is a proper analytic set, not an open obstruction.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\text{ is an avoidable analytic wall.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Non-centering is also avoidable

The centered wall is

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0.
\]

This is a single analytic hyperplane in the local midpoint parameter. If the proof permits \(m\) to vary in a neighborhood of the packet center, then

\[
x_m=0
\]

is trivially avoidable.

So the only dangerous case is:

\[
\boxed{
m\text{ is rigidly defined as }\gamma/2.
}
\]

If the architecture forces \(m=\gamma/2\), then the order-\(7\) \(q^{(7)}\)-channel is killed by parity and we must use the centered \(A_9\) fallback.

If \(m\) is a local sampling midpoint, not a rigid zero ordinate center, then non-centering is available.

---

## 4. Compatibility with the canonical core rule

Moving \(m\) slightly changes the packet distances

\[
D_P(m)
\]

continuously. If the centered point lies strictly inside the core selection region:

\[
D_{P_k}(m)<D_{P_{k+1}}(m),
\]

then this strict inequality persists for small nonzero \(x_m\).

Likewise, same-scale inequalities, endpoint separation, and Gram nondegeneracy persist under small perturbations as long as they are strict at the starting point.

Thus, on any reduced stratum where the packet is already in the interior of the good region, we can choose a nearby non-centered \(m\) with:

\[
x_m\ne0,
\qquad
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,
\qquad
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

and all other good-patch conditions preserved.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Non-centering does not destabilize the core unless the packet starts on a core-boundary wall.}
}
\]

Those boundary walls are already in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

---

## 5. The \(v_5\) issue

The septic \(q^{(7)}\)-transport slice gives an \(I\)-directional fixed-sector contribution:

\[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
\qquad
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv0.
\]

If one detects it through the quotient determinant

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]

then for this \(I\)-directional channel,

\[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}=u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5.
\]

Therefore quotient detection requires

\[
v_5\ne0.
\]

But the rank-two vector route does **not** require quotient detection. It only needs

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

If

\[
u_7^{(q^{(7)})}\ne0,
\]

then

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_7 I+v_7S
\ne0
\]

even if \(v_5=0\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
v_5\ne0
\text{ is needed only for quotient/determinant visibility, not for full rank-two visibility.}
}
\]

For the rank-two architecture, the essential wall is

\[
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
\]

not

\[
v_5=0.
\]

This is a meaningful improvement.

---

## 6. Refined visibility theorem

The theorem should now be stated in rank-two form:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
Let \(\mathcal P(\rho)\) be a nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet. Suppose
the reduced local construction permits a midpoint parameter \(m\) varying in a
neighborhood of the packet center, and suppose the packet lies in the interior
of the reduced-good-patch conditions. Then there exists a nearby non-centered
midpoint \(m\) such that
\[
x_m\ne0,\qquad q^{(7)}(m)\ne0.
\]
On the actual reduced-core septic \(K_1\)-transport slice, this gives
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0
\]
outside the analytic wall where the \(K_1\)-transport coefficient itself
vanishes. Hence fixed-sector invisibility is a proper analytic incidence
condition on the reduced off-line packet family.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

This theorem avoids reliance on the centered \(A_2A_4\) source-chart row.

---

## 7. Remaining risk: is the \(K_1\)-transport coefficient itself ever identically zero?

The draft result quoted earlier says the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven septic \(K_1\)-transport slice is nonzero on the generic one-pair region. Therefore the coefficient is not identically zero.

Still, for rigor, the incidence set should include:

\[
\mathcal E_{K_1}^{\core}
=
\{u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0\}.
\]

This is an analytic condition. It is proper if a single nonzero \(K_1\) witness exists.

So the full non-centered visibility exceptional set is:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
=
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\cup
\mathcal E_{K_1}^{\core}.
\]

Possibly also include

\[
\{A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\}
\]

if the local rank-two frame depends on the fifth-order reference.

---

## 8. What if midpoint freedom is not allowed?

If the architecture requires

\[
m=\gamma/2,
\]

then the non-centered theorem fails. In that case:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0
\]

by parity, and we return to the centered \(A_9\) fallback.

Then the next required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ contains a nonzero corrected }A_6\text{-channel.}
}
\]

The raw channel is already present:

\[
A_6\left(\frac{q_0^4}{896}-\frac{q_0A_2}{448}\right).
\]

But the corrected fixed-sector order-\(9\) formula remains missing.

---

# Final conclusion

The attack now strongly favors the non-centered route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use non-centered reduced good patches and certify visibility through }q^{(7)}.
}
\]

The remaining theorem is an avoidance theorem, not a coefficient-derivation theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant off-line packets admit reduced good patches with }
x_m\ne0,\quad q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,\quad u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\ne0.
}
\]

This is much weaker and more tractable than proving the centered \(A_9\) coefficient formula.

If that avoidance theorem is accepted, then packet visibility is conditionally closed and the rank-two route can proceed to the connection theorem on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

I’ll sharpen the avoidance theorem. The key improvement is that \(q^{(7)}\) has a *simple* zero at the centered midpoint, so an arbitrarily small non-centering activates the order-\(7\) channel while preserving any strict good-patch inequalities.

_Thought for 14s_

# Continued Attack — Simple-Zero Non-Centering Theorem

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The non-centered }q^{(7)}\text{ visibility channel is locally unavoidable near any nondegenerate centered packet.}
}
\]

More precisely, for an off-line packet with

\[
0<\beta<1,\qquad \beta\ne\frac12,
\]

the centered midpoint

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0
\]

is a **simple zero** of the seventh derivative channel. Hence every sufficiently small nonzero perturbation of \(m\) activates

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0.
\]

Thus, if the centered packet lies in the interior of the reduced-good-patch region, then the rank-two fixed-sector visibility witness can be activated without leaving

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

This strengthens the prior non-centered route from “generic” to “locally forced off the center.” The remaining issue is no longer coefficient visibility, but whether the proof architecture permits \(m\) to move off the exact packet center. The prior derivation prompt identified the actual reduced-core \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) realization bridge as the key obstacle; this continuation shows the \(q^{(7)}\) bridge is the cleaner way around the centered \(A_2A_4\) uncertainty. 

---

# 1. Seventh derivative near the packet center

For

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

where

\[
a=1-\beta=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\beta=\frac12+\delta,
\]

the seventh derivative at \(t=m\) has the form

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
-5160960x_m
\left[
\frac{
a(x_m^2-a^2)(x_m^4-6a^2x_m^2+a^4)
}{
(a^2+x_m^2)^8
}
+
\frac{
b(x_m^2-b^2)(x_m^4-6b^2x_m^2+b^4)
}{
(b^2+x_m^2)^8
}
\right].
\]

At

\[
x_m=0,
\]

the bracket equals

\[
-\frac{1}{a^9}-\frac{1}{b^9}.
\]

Indeed, for one term,

\[
\frac{a(0-a^2)(0-0+a^4)}{(a^2)^8}
=
\frac{-a^7}{a^{16}}
=
-\frac1{a^9}.
\]

Thus

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
-5160960x_m
\left[
-\frac1{a^9}-\frac1{b^9}
+O(x_m^2)
\right].
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960
\left(
a^{-9}+b^{-9}
\right)x_m
+
O(x_m^3).
}
\]

Since

\[
a,b>0
\]

for nontrivial zeros in the critical strip,

\[
a^{-9}+b^{-9}>0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
x_m=0
\text{ is a simple zero of }q^{(7)}(m).
}
\]

Consequently, for every sufficiently small

\[
x_m\ne0,
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0.
}
\]

---

# 2. Local perturbation preserves reduced-good-patch conditions

Let the centered point

\[
b_0=(m_0,s_0,\mathcal C_k(m_0))
\]

lie in the interior of

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

Then all defining inequalities are strict:

\[
d_k(m_0)<d_{k+1}(m_0),
\]

same-scale bounds are strict,

endpoint separation is strict,

Gram determinants are nonzero,

and the selected packet core is symmetry-stable.

All of these conditions are continuous or analytic in \((m,s)\). Therefore there exists an open neighborhood

\[
U\ni (m_0,s_0)
\]

such that for all \((m,s)\in U\), the same reduced-good-patch conditions remain true.

Since

\[
x_m=0
\]

is a hypersurface in \(U\), and since

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0
\]

has a simple zero along that hypersurface, there exist points in \(U\) such that

\[
x_m\ne0,
\qquad
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
b_0\in\operatorname{int}(\mathcal B_{\rm red})
\Longrightarrow
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ nearby with }q^{(7)}(m)\ne0.
}
\]

This removes the centered-parity obstruction.

---

# 3. Rank-two visibility implication

The reduced-core septic \(K_1\)-transport channel gives an actual fixed-sector order-\(7\) contribution of the form

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
\supset
q^{(7)}(m)\,\Xi_{K_1}(m),
\]

where

\[
\Xi_{K_1}(m)\in\mathfrak f_h
\]

is the nonzero fixed-sector transport vector on the generic \(K_1\) patch.

The prior septic analysis established that this channel is \(I\)-directional in the quotient determinant calculation:

\[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,
\qquad
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv0.
\]

For the full rank-two architecture, quotient determinant visibility is not required. It is enough that

\[
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\ne0.
\]

Hence on the open set where

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,
\qquad
\Xi_{K_1}(m)\ne0,
\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0.
}
\]

So the finite vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots)
\]

is nonzero.

---

# 4. The refined exceptional set

The reduced-base exceptional set should be enlarged by the order-\(7\) visibility walls:

\[
\mathcal E_{7}^{\core}
=
\{q^{(7)}(m)=0\}
\cup
\{\Xi_{K_1}(m)=0\}.
\]

If quotient determinant detection is used as a derived diagnostic, include

\[
\{v_5=0\}.
\]

But for the rank-two route, the \(v_5=0\) wall is not fatal if

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]

as a vector.

Thus the rank-two visibility exceptional set should be

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
=
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\cup
\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}
\]

is still an analytic or semianalytic controlled exceptional set.

---

# 5. The theorem now needed

The reduced-good-patch existence theorem should be restated as:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
For every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line symmetry packet, either the
configuration lies in the controlled exceptional set
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+},
\]
or there exists a nearby reduced good patch \(b=(m,s,\mathcal C_k(m))\) such
that
\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0
\]
and the septic \(K_1\)-transport vector is nonzero. Consequently,
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}(b)\ne0.
\]
\end{minipage}
}
\]

This is now a standard parameter-avoidance theorem, provided midpoint \(m\) is a genuine local parameter.

---

# 6. What if midpoint is fixed?

If the architecture forces

\[
m=\frac{\gamma}{2}
\]

or the corresponding exact packet center, then

\[
x_m=0
\]

and

\[
q^{(7)}(m)=0.
\]

Then the \(K_1\) order-\(7\) route is unavailable. The proof must instead use the centered even-jet route:

\[
A_2,A_4,A_6,\ldots
\]

and the next target is

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The raw \(s^9\) calculation already found an \(A_6\)-channel:

\[
A_6
\left(
\frac{q_0^4}{896}
-
\frac{q_0A_2}{448}
\right).
\]

But the corrected fixed-sector \(A_9\) formula remains unproved.

So the architecture has a clean fork:

\[
\boxed{
\text{midpoint movable}
\Rightarrow
\text{use }q^{(7)}\text{ and proceed;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{midpoint forced centered}
\Rightarrow
\text{compute corrected }A_9.
}
\]

---

# 7. Recommended strategic move

Do not continue with centered \(A_9\) unless centering is forced by the draft.

Instead, introduce a reduced-good-patch condition explicitly allowing non-centered midpoints:

\[
\boxed{
m\in U_{\rho}
\setminus
\{x_m=0,\ q^{(7)}(m)=0\}.
}
\]

Then packet visibility is handled at order \(7\).

The next theorem after this should be:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\text{ admits the canonical projected connection }
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}.
\]

---

## Final conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet visibility is now conditionally closed if non-centered midpoints are permitted.}
}
\]

The only remaining visibility obstruction is the architectural question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Must }m\text{ be the exact packet center?}
}
\]

If no, then the \(q^{(7)}\)-channel provides an actual reduced-core order-\(7\) witness, and the rank-two connection theorem is the next target.

If yes, then visibility remains centered and the required next computation is

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:27:25)

I’ll now attack the remaining objection: whether moving \(m\) off the packet center breaks the reduced-core local algebra or invalidates Gate A/B. This is the last visibility-side kill switch before the rank-two connection theorem.

_Thought for 33s_

# Continued Attack — Does Non-Centering Break the Reduced-Core Algebra?

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Non-centering is legitimate unless the draft explicitly fixes }m=\gamma/2.
}
\]

The local construction uses \(m\) as the midpoint of the two sample points

\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2,
\]

not intrinsically as the ordinate center of a zero packet. Therefore the centered choice

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0
\]

is a convenient symmetry point, not a structural requirement. The attached derivation prompt’s target was to certify actual reduced-core visibility, preferably at \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\); the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-channel is the cleanest way to do that. 

The main caveat is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If earlier Gate A/B formulas were proved only in an exactly centered/even-core gauge, they must be restated for non-centered core jets.}
}
\]

But I see no mathematical reason the rank-two route must stay centered. In fact, non-centering is better: it activates an actual reduced-core septic channel rather than relying on the unresolved centered \(A_2A_4\) transfer.

---

# 1. What changes when \(m\) is moved off center?

At the packet center,

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]

the packet contribution is even in \(u=t-m\). Hence all odd derivatives vanish:

\[
q_1=q_3=q_5=q_7=\cdots=0.
\]

Moving \(m\) slightly gives

\[
x_m\ne0,
\]

and odd derivatives appear:

\[
q_1,q_3,q_5,q_7,\ldots\ne0
\]

generically.

This is not a pathology. It simply means the core phase is no longer even around the sampling midpoint.

The rank-two reduced-core architecture should allow this because the fibre

\[
\mathfrak f_h(m)
\]

is defined for a general local midpoint \(m\), not only for parity-centered \(m\).

---

# 2. Does non-centering change the selected core?

Only if we cross a core boundary.

Let \(P\) be the RH-relevant packet and let \(D_P(m)\) be its packet-level distance score. Suppose at the centered point \(m_0\),

\[
D_{P_k}(m_0)<D_{P_{k+1}}(m_0)
\]

and the same-scale, symmetry, endpoint, and Gram conditions are strict.

Then by continuity, for all sufficiently small nonzero \(m-m_0\),

\[
D_{P_k}(m)<D_{P_{k+1}}(m),
\]

and the selected packet core remains unchanged:

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)=\mathcal C_k(m_0).
\]

Thus non-centering does not force a source/core transition. It stays inside the same reduced stratum.

The bad cases are already in the exceptional set:

\[
d_k=d_{k+1},
\qquad
\text{same-scale boundary},
\qquad
\text{endpoint collapse},
\qquad
\det G_{\core}=0,
\qquad
\text{patch boundary}.
\]

So the theorem should say:

\[
\boxed{
b_0\in\operatorname{int}(\mathcal B_{\rm red})
\Rightarrow
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ nearby with }x_m\ne0.
}
\]

---

# 3. Does non-centering break Gate A/B?

Not if Gate A/B are treated correctly.

Gate A/B are now local fixed-convention algebraic lemmas. They should not require the packet core to be centered. Their inputs are local finite-\(s\) jets, source labels, scalar grades, and symmetry/reflection tables under a fixed core/source convention.

Non-centering changes the numerical jet values:

\[
q_1,q_3,q_5,q_7,\ldots
\]

but does not change the source labels or the core membership as long as we remain in the same reduced stratum.

Thus Gate A/B should survive as local algebraic lemmas on the non-centered patch.

The only danger is if some previous cancellation proof used the evenness condition

\[
q_{2j+1}=0
\]

as a hidden hypothesis. If so, that proof was too narrow and must be restated. But that would be a limitation of the centered subcase, not a reason to forbid non-centering.

So the right audit statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B remain valid under non-centering if their hypotheses are jet-formal, not even-core-specific.}
}
\]

If any Gate A/B lemma explicitly assumes

\[
x_m=0
\]

or

\[
q_{2j+1}=0,
\]

then the non-centered route requires a local lemma extension.

---

# 4. Does non-centering create earlier obstructions?

Possibly, but that is not bad for visibility.

Non-centering may produce lower-order fixed-sector odd signals. For example, odd core jets can feed earlier rows than the centered even-jet mechanism.

If such lower-order terms produce

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]

for some \(r<3\) or \(r=3\), then packet visibility is even easier.

The only problem would be if the proof architecture required all lower-order odd core signals to vanish before order \(7\). But the rank-two visibility goal is not to kill local signals. It is to prove that off-line packets are detected by the fixed-sector germ:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\ne0.
\]

Thus non-centering does not create a visibility problem. It creates more possible visibility channels.

---

# 5. Nonzero \(q^{(7)}\) is locally forced off center

We established:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m
+
O(x_m^3)
\]

near

\[
x_m=0.
\]

Since

\[
a,b>0,
\]

the coefficient

\[
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})
\]

is nonzero.

Therefore

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0
\]

for every sufficiently small nonzero \(x_m\), outside possibly higher isolated zeros.

So the visibility wall

\[
q^{(7)}=0
\]

cannot swallow a reduced packet neighborhood. It intersects it as a proper analytic wall.

---

# 6. What must be true for \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0\)?

The reduced-core septic \(K_1\) channel gives

\[
A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}
\supset
q^{(7)}(m)\,\Xi_{K_1}(m),
\]

where

\[
\Xi_{K_1}(m)\in\mathfrak f_h
\]

is the fixed-sector transport vector for the \(q^{(7)}\) slice.

The visibility theorem needs:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,
\qquad
\Xi_{K_1}(m)\ne0.
\]

The second condition is the \(K_1\)-transport nondegeneracy condition. It should be placed into the exceptional set:

\[
\mathcal E_{K_1}^{\core}
=
\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
m\notin\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\mathcal E_{K_1}^{\core}
\Rightarrow
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
}
\]

This avoids any reliance on centered \(A_2A_4\) transfer.

---

# 7. Could other \(A_7\) terms cancel the \(q^{(7)}\) channel?

This is the last technical risk.

The safest answer is: in a graded row decomposition, the \(q^{(7)}\) channel is an independent jet monomial. It cannot be cancelled by \(A_2A_4\), \(A_2^2\), or lower even-jet channels because those live in different jet monomials.

When moving \(m\), lower odd derivatives \(q_1,q_3,q_5\) also become nonzero. Conceivably they could contribute to the same total order. But they are distinct jet coordinates. A cancellation of the \(q^{(7)}\)-slice would require another term linear in \(q^{(7)}\) with the opposite coefficient, or a structural identity relating \(q^{(7)}\) to lower jets along the actual packet family.

For the packet family, such a relation is not an identity: \(q^{(7)}\) has a simple zero at \(x_m=0\), while lower odd derivatives have different leading behavior in \(x_m\). A complete cancellation over an open set would be an analytic identity. The known \(K_1\)-transport coefficient says the \(q^{(7)}\) slice is nonzero.

Thus any cancellation belongs to a proper analytic incidence locus unless the draft contains an explicit identity killing the \(K_1\) slice.

---

# 8. Revised packet visibility theorem

The clean theorem should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
Let \(\mathcal P(\rho)\) be a nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet and let
\(b_0=(m_0,s_0,\mathcal C_k(m_0))\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}\) be a reduced good
patch with the packet in the canonical core. Suppose \(b_0\) lies in the
interior of the reduced-good-patch inequalities and the local midpoint \(m\)
is allowed to vary. Then there exists a nearby non-centered reduced good patch
\(b=(m,s,\mathcal C_k(m))\) such that
\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,
\qquad
\Xi_{K_1}(m)\ne0.
\]
At such a patch,
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}(b)\ne0.
\]
Hence the fixed-sector invisibility locus is a proper analytic incidence
condition on the nondegenerate reduced off-line packet family.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

The enlarged exceptional set is:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,7}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\cup
\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]

---

# 9. Strategic consequence

The rank-two route can proceed if we accept the following architectural rule:

\[
\boxed{
m\text{ is a local sampling midpoint, not fixed to the packet center.}
}
\]

Then packet visibility is no longer blocked by the centered \(A_2A_4\) realization gap.

If the draft insists that \(m\) must equal the packet center, then the \(q^{(7)}\) route fails and the required next computation is still:

\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

with the \(A_6\)-channel.

But if non-centered \(m\) is allowed, the right next theorem is no longer visibility. It is the rank-two connection theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
}
\]

on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}
\to
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\left(
\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}
\right).
\]

---

## Final conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{The attack succeeds if non-centered midpoints are permitted.}
}
\]

The packet visibility theorem becomes a controlled avoidance result, not a centered coefficient computation.

The next attack should therefore be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Verify explicitly from the draft that }m\text{ is a free sampling midpoint.}
}
\]

If yes, proceed to the rank-two connection theorem.

# Continued Attack — Midpoint Freedom / Non-Centered Patch Legitimacy

## Verdict

Therefore the non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-visibility route is legitimate **provided** the draft’s reduced-core construction is formulated for general sample points

\[

and not only for the special centered choice

\[
2m-\gamma=0.
\]

This is the strongest current route. It avoids the unresolved centered \(A_9\) computation and uses the already-available actual reduced-core septic \(K_1\)-transport channel. The prior attached derivation prompt identifies \(A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\) as the decisive visibility coefficient and says not to proceed to the rank-two connection theorem until reduced-core visibility is certified. 

---

## 1. What “midpoint” means in the local kernel

The local two-point construction uses

\[
t_+=m+\frac{s}{2},
\qquad
t_-=m-\frac{s}{2}.
\]

Thus \(m\) is the midpoint of the two **sample points**, not intrinsically the ordinate center of a zero packet.

The packet-centered condition

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0
\]

is an optional symmetry choice. It makes the packet contribution even around \(m\), which is useful for explicit even-jet computations, but it is not structurally required by the finite-\(s\) kernel.

So the right formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
m\in U_\rho
\text{ is a local midpoint parameter near the packet,}
\quad
\text{not fixed to }\gamma/2.
}
\]

---

## 2. Non-centering activates the certified order-7 channel

For the paired packet contribution

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad
x=2t-\gamma,
\]

with

\[
a=\frac12-\delta,
\qquad
b=\frac12+\delta,
\]

we have near \(x_m=0\):

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m
+
O(x_m^3).
\]

Since

\[
a,b>0,
\]

the coefficient is nonzero. Therefore

\[
\boxed{

\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0
}

outside a proper analytic wall.

The actual reduced-core septic \(K_1\)-transport channel then gives

\supset

\]

so, outside

\]

we obtain

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
}
\]

This proves fixed-sector visibility at order \(7\) on the non-centered reduced good patch.

---

## 3. Does moving \(m\) leave the reduced base?

If the centered packet is already inside the reduced good set, then small non-centering stays inside it.

The defining reduced-base conditions are strict:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

same-scale bounds,

endpoint separation,

Gram/whitening nondegeneracy,

fixed core membership,

and patch-interior conditions.

All of these vary continuously, indeed analytically or semianalytically, in \((m,s)\). Therefore, if they hold strictly at \(m_0\), they hold in some neighborhood of \(m_0\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
b_0\in \operatorname{int}(\mathcal B_{\rm red})
\Rightarrow
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ nearby with }x_m\ne0,\ q^{(7)}(m)\ne0.
}
\]

This is exactly the parameter-avoidance logic used in the reduced-good-patch existence wave: exceptional walls can be avoided unless they are identically forced. 

---

## 4. Does non-centering break the canonical core?

No, unless \(m\) crosses a core-boundary wall.

The canonical core is selected by packet distance scores. Let

\[
D_P(m)
\]

be the score of a symmetry packet \(P\). If

\[
D_{P_k}(m_0)<D_{P_{k+1}}(m_0),
\]

then for small perturbations of \(m\),

\[
D_{P_k}(m)<D_{P_{k+1}}(m)
\]

still holds.

Thus the selected packet core remains the same:

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)=\mathcal C_k(m_0).
\]

The only failures are already controlled:

\[
D_{P_k}=D_{P_{k+1}},
\]

same-scale boundary,

symmetry-closure boundary,

endpoint-gap collapse,

Gram singularity,

and patch-boundary failure.

So non-centering does not reintroduce arbitrary source/core transitions.

---

## 5. Does non-centering invalidate Gate A/B?

No, unless Gate A/B secretly require an even-core gauge.

Gate A/B are local fixed-convention algebraic lemmas. They are supposed to hold under a fixed source/core convention and stable labels. Non-centering changes jet values:

\[
q_1,q_3,q_5,q_7,\ldots
\]

but it does not change labels or the selected core if we remain in the same reduced stratum.

Thus the correct condition is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B survive non-centering if they are formal jet identities, not centered-even-core identities.}
}
\]

If a specific Gate A/B proof used

\[
q_{2j+1}=0
\]

as a hidden assumption, it must be restated. But that would be a limitation of the centered subcase, not of the rank-two route.

---

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}

as a vector.

because

# Continued Attack — Verifying Midpoint Freedom from the Draft

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The draft treats }m\text{ as a free admissible midpoint.}
}
\]

The finite-\(s\) local block section explicitly says:

\[
\text{“Fix a midpoint }m\text{ and a symmetric separation parameter }s,”
\qquad
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2}.
\]

It does **not** define \(m\) as the center of a zero packet. The corrected whitening section also says “fix an admissible midpoint \(m\),” then defines zero-source denominators using

\[
2m-\gamma_\rho,
\]

which is exactly the variable we have been calling \(x_m\). This confirms that \(x_m\) is allowed to vary with \(m\); it is not constrained to be zero.

Therefore the non-centered route is legitimate in the draft’s local setup.

---

## 1. Direct draft evidence

The finite-\(s\) construction begins with:

\[
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2}.
\]

The local mixed block then uses

\[
q_+(s)=q(t_+),
\qquad
q_-(s)=q(t_-),
\qquad
\Delta_m(s)=\Phi(t_-)-\Phi(t_+).
\]

This is a general two-point midpoint construction. There is no condition

\[
2m-\gamma_\rho=0.
\]

Later, in the corrected finite-\(s\) whitening section, the draft defines for each omitted zero:

\[
D_{\rho,\pm}(s)
=
\bigl((2m-\gamma_\rho)\pm s\bigr)^2+a_\rho^2.
\]

This explicitly uses

\[
2m-\gamma_\rho
\]

as a free local offset. If the architecture required centered packets, this term would be identically zero for the distinguished packet. It is not.

So:

\[
\boxed{
x_m=2m-\gamma_\rho
\text{ is a genuine local parameter.}
}
\]

---

## 2. Finite-core core selection also uses midpoint \(m\)

The draft defines a finite same-scale core around the midpoint:

\[
\mathcal C=\text{finite same-scale core of zero pairs around }m.
\]

This again treats \(m\) as the center of the local analysis window, not necessarily as the exact center of any single zero packet.

The canonical core condition is therefore:

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)\in\mathcal C_k(m),
\]

not

\[
m=\gamma_\rho/2.
\]

As long as the packet remains in the selected same-scale core and all strict reduced-base inequalities hold, \(m\) may be moved.

Thus the reduced base should include non-centered points:

\[
x_m\ne0.
\]

---

## 3. Odd two-point germ supports non-centering

The odd two-point germ is defined by the involution

\[
s\mapsto -s,
\qquad
t_+\leftrightarrow t_-.
\]

This parity is about exchanging the two sample points around the chosen midpoint \(m\). It does **not** impose that the core phase \(q(t)\) is even around \(m\).

The lemma on pure same-point septic terms says pure same-point septic contributions vanish in the odd two-point germ because they carry no transport factor from the ordered pair \((t_+,t_-)\). That is a statement about \(s\)-parity, not about zero-packet centering.

Therefore non-centering does not contradict the odd-germ construction.

In fact, non-centering helps: it creates odd core jets such as

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,
\]

which enter through the transport sector rather than through pure same-point even terms.

---

## 4. Consequence for visibility

The non-centered packet visibility theorem can now be stated cleanly:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
In the draft’s local finite-\(s\) construction, \(m\) is a free admissible
midpoint for the sample pair \(t_\pm=m\pm s/2\). For an off-line packet
\(\mathcal P(\rho)\), the offset
\[
x_m=2m-\gamma_\rho
\]
is not constrained to vanish. Therefore one may choose \(m\) in the same
reduced good stratum with
\[
x_m\ne0,\qquad q^{(7)}(m)\ne0,
\]
outside the controlled analytic walls. The actual reduced-core septic
\(K_1\)-transport channel then gives
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]
on the generic non-centered reduced patch.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

This closes the midpoint-freedom objection.

---

We should now define:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\left(
\{x_m=0\}
\cup
\{q^{(7)}(m)=0\}
\cup
\{\Xi_{K_1}(m)=0\}
\right).
\]

On this set:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\ne0.
}
\]

The fixed-sector invisibility locus is therefore a proper analytic incidence condition, not an open obstruction, provided the accepted septic \(K_1\)-transport result is used.

---
