# Agent 2 — \(N_7^{I,D}\) Companion-Row Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)\,N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

Here

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}
=
X_2N_7X_0-X_1N_7X_1+X_0N_7X_2
\]

is the centered-parity \(N_7\)-family order-9 companion row at \(g=h\), with

\[
X_0=pI,\qquad X_1=BS,\qquad X_2=aI+dD.
\]

So the \(N_7\)-family can contribute to the same **\(I\)-coordinate** as the order-9 survivor

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
-2yBd\,I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

But the \(N_7\)-family does **not** share the same channel label \(Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}\) unless the raw \(N_7^{I,D}\) carriers themselves contain the same \(yB\Gamma_{G,2}\) source/whitening structure. That would be a new analytic row identity, not a sector/parity necessity. The attached instruction identifies this exact \(N_7^{I,D}\) audit as Agent 2’s task in the order-9 row-table wave. 

---

## 1. Setup

At \(g=h\),

\[
X_0=pI,
\qquad
p=g^{-1/2}.
\]

Use

\[
X_1=BS,
\]

and

\[
X_2=aI+dD,
\]

where

\[
d=(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi}g^{-3/2}\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Write the raw \(N_7\)-carrier as

\[
N_7
=
N_7^I I+N_7^S S+N_7^D D+N_7^J J.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_1,
\qquad
X_{+,2}=X_2.
\]

Thus the \(N_7\)-family order-9 companion row is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{2,7}
=
X_2N_7X_0-X_1N_7X_1+X_0N_7X_2.
}
\]

Since \(X_0=pI\),

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}
=
p(X_2N_7+N_7X_2)-B^2SN_7S.
\]

---

## 2. Matrix products by \(N_7\)-sector

Use

\[
S^2=I,\qquad D^2=I,\qquad J^2=-I,
\]

\[
SJ=-D,\qquad JS=D,
\]

\[
DJ=S,\qquad JD=-S,
\]

and

\[
SDS=-D,\qquad SJS=-J.
\]

### 2.1 \(N_7=N_7^I I\)

\[
p(X_2I+IX_2)
=
p(2aI+2dD).
\]

Also

\[
-B^2SIS=-B^2I.
\]

So

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(I)}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I\,I
+
2pd\,N_7^I\,D.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(I)}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I.
}
\]

---

### 2.2 \(N_7=N_7^D D\)

\[
X_2D+DX_2
=
(aI+dD)D+D(aI+dD)
=
2aD+2dI.
\]

Thus

\[
p(X_2D+DX_2)
=
2paD+2pdI.
\]

Also

\[
SDS=-D,
\]

so

\[
-B^2SDS=+B^2D.
\]

Hence

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(D)}
=
2pd\,N_7^D\,I
+
(2pa+B^2)N_7^D\,D.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(D)}
=
2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

---

### 2.3 \(N_7=N_7^S S\)

\[
X_2S+SX_2
=
(aI+dD)S+S(aI+dD)
=
2aS+d(DS+SD).
\]

But

\[
DS=J,\qquad SD=-J,
\]

so

\[
DS+SD=0.
\]

Thus

\[
p(X_2S+SX_2)=2paS.
\]

Also

\[
SSS=S,
\]

so

\[
-B^2SSS=-B^2S.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(S)}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^S\,S,
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(S)}=0.
}
\]

---

### 2.4 \(N_7=N_7^J J\)

\[
X_2J+JX_2
=
(aI+dD)J+J(aI+dD)
=
2aJ+d(DJ+JD).
\]

But

\[
DJ=S,\qquad JD=-S,
\]

so

\[
DJ+JD=0.
\]

Thus

\[
p(X_2J+JX_2)=2paJ.
\]

Also

\[
SJS=-J,
\]

so

\[
-B^2SJS=+B^2J.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(J)}
=
(2pa+B^2)N_7^J\,J,
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(J)}=0.
}
\]

---

## 3. Total \(I\)-component

Combining the \(I\) and \(D\) carriers gives

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

The \(S\)-carrier contributes only \(S\), and the \(J\)-carrier contributes only \(J\). Thus neither contributes to the \(I\)-coordinate.

This verifies the preliminary expectation in the instruction.

---

## 4. Comparison with the order-9 candidate

The candidate order-9 survivor is

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
-2yBd\,I.
\]

Since

\[
d=-\frac{1}{32\pi}g^{-3/2}\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}},
\]

this is

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

The \(N_7\)-family companion has

\[
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D.
\]

So exact cancellation by the \(N_7\)-family would require

\[
\boxed{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
=
0.
}
\]

Equivalently, using \(d=(X_2)_D\),

\[
\boxed{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D-2yBd=0.
}
\]

---

## 5. Does this cancellation happen structurally?

I see no sector/parity reason it must.

The candidate row has channel label

\[
\boxed{
Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}.
}
\]

The \(N_7\)-family has labels

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I X_{2,I/D}X_0,
\qquad
N_7^D X_{2,I/D}X_0,
\qquad
N_7^{I/D}X_1X_1.
}
\]

These are different channels.

In particular:

- \(N_7^I\) contributes through the scalar combination \(2pa-B^2\). It need not contain \(d=\Gamma_{G,2}\).
- \(N_7^D\) contributes through \(2pd\), so it shares the \(d\)-factor but not the \(yB\) carrier unless \(N_7^D\) itself contains \(yB\).
- The \(X_1N_7X_1\) subrow contains \(B^2\), not the \(B d\) structure of the candidate.

Thus the \(N_7\)-family can only cancel \(C_9^{\rm cand}\) through a genuine analytic identity among row coefficients, not by automatic matrix algebra.

---

## 6. Risk classification

### Harmless by sector

\[
N_7^S,\qquad N_7^J
\]

are harmless for the \(I\)-component in this row.

### Potentially contributing

\[
N_7^I,\qquad N_7^D
\]

do contribute to the \(I\)-component.

### Cancellation risk

The cancellation risk is real enough that the full order-9 row table should include it:

\[
\boxed{
R_{2,7}^I
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D.
}
\]

But it is not a structural cancellation of the candidate. It defines part of the cross-channel incidence wall:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
=
\left\{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D
+\cdots
=
-\,\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
\right\}.
\]

Here “\(\cdots\)” denotes other order-9 \(I\)-sector companion families.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D.
}
\]

The \(N_7^S\) and \(N_7^J\) sectors do not contribute to the \(I\)-coordinate.

Therefore the \(N_7\)-family is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not structurally fatal, but cross-channel relevant.}
}
\]

It cannot cancel the order-9 survivor by sector/parity necessity. Exact cancellation would require the analytic identity

\[
\boxed{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pdN_7^D
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
=0
}
\]

after adding any remaining \(I\)-sector order-9 companions.

So the order-9 theorem should include an explicit cross-channel wall

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
}
\]

unless the full \(N_7^{I,D}\) coefficients are computed and shown to be incapable of same-row cancellation.

# Agent 2 — \(N_7^{I,D}\) Companion-Row Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

The \(N_7\)-family can contribute to the same \(I\)-coordinate as the order-9 survivor

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I,
\]

but it is a **different channel family**. It does not structurally cancel the survivor unless the raw carriers \(N_7^I,N_7^D\) satisfy a new analytic row identity. This is exactly the companion-row risk identified in the attached instruction. 

---

## 1. Setup

At \(g=h\), write

\[
X_0=pI,\qquad X_1=BS,\qquad X_2=aI+dD.
\]

The order-9 \(N_7\)-family row is

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}
=
X_2N_7X_0-X_1N_7X_1+X_0N_7X_2.
\]

Since \(X_0=pI\), this becomes

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}
=
p(X_2N_7+N_7X_2)-B^2SN_7S.
\]

Decompose

\[
N_7=N_7^I I+N_7^S S+N_7^D D+N_7^J J.
\]

Use

\[
S^2=I,\qquad D^2=I,\qquad J^2=-I,
\]

\[
SJ=-D,\qquad JS=D,
\]

\[
DJ=S,\qquad JD=-S,
\]

\[
SDS=-D,\qquad SJS=-J.
\]

---

## 2. Sector-by-sector computation

### \(N_7=N_7^I I\)

\[
p(X_2I+IX_2)
=
p(2aI+2dD).
\]

Also

\[
-B^2SIS=-B^2I.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(I)}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I\,I
+
2pd\,N_7^I\,D.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(I)}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I.
}
\]

---

### \(N_7=N_7^D D\)

\[
X_2D+DX_2
=
(aI+dD)D+D(aI+dD)
=
2aD+2dI.
\]

Thus

\[
p(X_2D+DX_2)
=
2paD+2pdI.
\]

Also

\[
-B^2SDS=+B^2D.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(D)}
=
2pd\,N_7^D\,I
+
(2pa+B^2)N_7^D\,D.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(D)}
=
2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

---

### \(N_7=N_7^S S\)

\[
X_2S+SX_2
=
(aI+dD)S+S(aI+dD)
=
2aS+d(DS+SD).
\]

Since

\[
DS=J,\qquad SD=-J,
\]

we get

\[
DS+SD=0.
\]

So

\[
p(X_2S+SX_2)=2paS.
\]

Also

\[
-B^2SSS=-B^2S.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(S)}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^S\,S.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(S)}=0.
}
\]

---

### \(N_7=N_7^J J\)

\[
X_2J+JX_2
=
(aI+dD)J+J(aI+dD)
=
2aJ+d(DJ+JD).
\]

Since

\[
DJ=S,\qquad JD=-S,
\]

we get

\[
DJ+JD=0.
\]

So

\[
p(X_2J+JX_2)=2paJ.
\]

Also

\[
-B^2SJS=+B^2J.
\]

Therefore

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(J)}
=
(2pa+B^2)N_7^J\,J.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I\mathcal R_{2,7}^{(J)}=0.
}
\]

---

## 3. Total \(I\)-component

Combining the only two \(I\)-visible sectors gives

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

The \(S\)-carrier contributes only \(S\). The \(J\)-carrier contributes only \(J\). Neither contributes to the \(I\)-coordinate.

---

## 4. Comparison with the order-9 survivor

The order-9 survivor is

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
-2yBd\,I.
\]

Using

\[
d=(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi}g^{-3/2}\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and

\[
B=\frac{q''}{8\pi g^{3/2}},
\]

we have

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

The \(N_7\)-family companion contributes

\[
R_{2,7}^{I}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
\]

Therefore cancellation by the \(N_7\)-family would require

\[
\boxed{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I
+
2pd\,N_7^D
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
=
0.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I
+
2pd\,N_7^D
-
2yBd
=
0.
}
\]

---

## 5. Structural cancellation status

The candidate row has channel label

\[
\boxed{
Y_JX_{1,S}X_{2,D}.
}
\]

The \(N_7\)-family has channel labels of the form

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I X_{2,I/D}X_0,\qquad
N_7^D X_{2,I/D}X_0,\qquad
N_7^{I/D}X_1X_1.
}
\]

These are not the same channel.

In particular:

\[
N_7^I
\]

would need to carry the same source scalar as \(yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\) and then satisfy the precise coefficient identity above.

Likewise,

\[
N_7^D
\]

shares the \(d\)-factor through \(2pd\,N_7^D\), but it still lacks the \(yB\) channel label unless \(N_7^D\) itself contains \(yB\).

Thus the \(N_7\)-family is **cross-channel relevant**, but it is not a sector-forced cancellation.

---

## 6. What remains unknown

This audit does **not** compute the raw coefficients

\[
N_7^I,\qquad N_7^D.
\]

It proves the exact form in which they would enter the order-9 \(I\)-coordinate. To remove them completely, one needs a raw-carrier computation showing either

\[
N_7^I=N_7^D=0,
\]

or that their source scalars are independent of

\[
yq''\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

and therefore cannot cancel identically except on a proper analytic wall.

Given the known centered raw off-diagonal order-7 carrier is skew,

\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\]

the \(J\)-part is harmless for the \(I\)-coordinate. The unresolved issue is whether diagonal or anti-fixed raw correction terms produce nonzero \(N_7^I\) or \(N_7^D\).

---

# Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(N_7\)-family: cross-channel relevant, not structurally fatal.}
}
\]

The precise contribution is

\[
\boxed{
R_{2,7}^{I}
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
}
\]

The exact cancellation identity would be

\[
\boxed{
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I
+
2pd\,N_7^D
+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
=
0.
}
\]

No parity or sector algebra forces this identity. Therefore the order-9 theorem may keep this row inside the cross-channel incidence wall

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
\]

unless a later raw \(N_7^{I,D}\) computation proves it vanishes or is harmless.

I’ll compute \(N_7\) under the centred raw finite-\(s\) convention. The main issue is whether any diagonal odd coefficient survives; if not, the raw \(N_7\) carrier is purely \(J\), which removes the \(N_7^{I,D}\) obstruction.

# Agent 2 — Raw \(N_7\) finite-\(s\) numerator expansion

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
N_7=F_7J
}
\]

under the centred raw finite-\(s\) numerator convention. In particular,

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I=N_7^D=0.
}
\]

Therefore the \(N_7\)-family companion row

\[
R_7^I[N_7]
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D
\]

vanishes:

\[
\boxed{
R_7^I[N_7]=0.
}
\]

So the \(N_7^{I,D}\) obstruction is removed at the raw numerator level, provided no later correction/normalization step reclassifies diagonal odd terms into the raw \(N_7\)-carrier. The attached instruction identifies \(N_7^I,N_7^D\) as the current main blocker for the order-9 theorem. 

---

## 1. Centred raw numerator setup

At a centred even packet, write

\[
t_\pm=m\pm\frac{s}{2}.
\]

The phase derivative satisfies

\[
q(t_+)=q(t_-),
\]

as a formal even expansion in \(s\). Write

\[
q_-(s)=q(t_-)
=
q_0+\frac{q_2}{8}s^2+\frac{q_4}{384}s^4+\frac{q_6}{46080}s^6+\frac{q_8}{10321920}s^8+\cdots,
\]

where

\[
q_{2j}=q^{(2j)}(m).
\]

The phase gap has odd expansion

\[
\Delta(s)
=
q_0s+\frac{q_2}{24}s^3+\frac{q_4}{1920}s^5+\frac{q_6}{322560}s^7+\frac{q_8}{92897280}s^9+\cdots.
\]

The raw off-diagonal numerator used in the previous expansion is

\[
F(s)
=
\frac{\sin\Delta(s)+q_-(s)s\cos\Delta(s)}{s^2}.
\]

Because \(\Delta(s)\) is odd, \(\sin\Delta(s)\) is odd and \(\cos\Delta(s)\) is even. Since \(q_-(s)\) is even, the product

\[
q_-(s)s\cos\Delta(s)
\]

is odd. Therefore \(F(s)\) has an odd-power expansion after the usual cancellation/normalization convention.

The raw off-diagonal block has the skew form

\[
N_7^{\rm off}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & F_7\\
-F_7 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
F_7J,
\]

up to the harmless global sign convention for \(J\).

Thus the off-diagonal raw \(N_7\) contributes only to the \(J\)-sector.

---

## 2. Explicit \(F_7\) coefficient

A direct expansion gives

\[
\begin{aligned}
F_7
={}&
\frac{q_0^9}{36288}
-\frac{q_0^6q_2}{1728}
+\frac{q_0^4q_4}{4608}
+\frac{5q_0^3q_2^2}{3456} \\
&-\frac{q_0^2q_6}{64512}
-\frac{q_0q_2q_4}{4608}
-\frac{5q_2^3}{41472}
+\frac{q_8}{9289728}.
\end{aligned}
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
N_7^J=F_7,
}
\]

up to sign convention.

But

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I=N_7^D=N_7^S=0
}
\]

for the raw off-diagonal numerator.

---

## 3. Diagonal raw entries

The diagonal raw entries are same-point / endpoint-local terms built from \(q(t_+)\), \(q(t_-)\), and even functions of the centred gap. At centred parity,

\[
q(t_+)=q(t_-)
\]

as even functions of \(s\). Thus the diagonal entries are even in \(s\). Hence

\[
[N_{11}(s)]_{s^7}=0,
\qquad
[N_{22}(s)]_{s^7}=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
N_7^I
=
\frac{N_{11,7}+N_{22,7}}2
=
0,
\]

and

\[
N_7^D
=
\frac{N_{11,7}-N_{22,7}}2
=
0.
\]

So the raw diagonal sector does not create \(I\)- or \(D\)-components at order \(7\).

---

## 4. Sector decomposition

Combining off-diagonal and diagonal parts:

\[
N_7
=
F_7J.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I=0,
\qquad
N_7^D=0,
\qquad
N_7^S=0,
\qquad
N_7^J=F_7.
}
\]

This is the strongest possible outcome for the order-9 companion audit.

---

## 5. Consequence for the order-9 \(N_7\)-family

Recall the \(N_7\)-family contribution:

\[
\mathcal R_{2,7}
=
X_2N_7X_0-X_1N_7X_1+X_0N_7X_2.
\]

The previous sector calculation gave

\[
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})
=
(2pa-B^2)N_7^I+2pd\,N_7^D.
\]

Since

\[
N_7^I=N_7^D=0,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\pi_I(\mathcal R_{2,7})=0.
}
\]

Thus the \(N_7\)-family cannot cancel the order-9 survivor

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

---

## 6. Caveat: corrected rows versus raw carrier

This conclusion is for the **raw \(N_7\)-carrier**. If the draft’s corrected normalization later moves diagonal odd terms into a row labelled \(N_7\), then those are not part of the raw finite-\(s\) numerator carrier computed here. They must be accounted for as correction, \(K_5\)-line, background/core, or cross-channel rows in \(R_9^I\).

Under the raw numerator convention requested in this agent instruction, however,

\[
\boxed{
N_7^{I,D}=0.
}
\]

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
N_7=F_7J
}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
N_7^I=N_7^D=0.
}
\]

The explicit skew coefficient is

\[
\begin{aligned}
F_7
={}&
\frac{q_0^9}{36288}
-\frac{q_0^6q_2}{1728}
+\frac{q_0^4q_4}{4608}
+\frac{5q_0^3q_2^2}{3456} \\
&-\frac{q_0^2q_6}{64512}
-\frac{q_0q_2q_4}{4608}
-\frac{5q_2^3}{41472}
+\frac{q_8}{9289728}.
\end{aligned}
\]

Therefore the \(N_7\)-family order-9 \(I\)-row vanishes:

\[
\boxed{
R_7^I[N_7]=0.
}
\]

This removes the main \(N_7^{I,D}\) blocker. The next obstruction in the order-9 row table is the \(N_5^D\) family and any lower-carrier correction rows.

# Agent 2 — Raw Lower-Carrier Parity Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
N_1,\ N_3\in \mathbf C J,
\qquad
N_0,\ N_2,\ N_4\in \mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S
}
\]

under the same centered raw finite-\(s\) convention used in the \(N_5,N_7,N_9\) audits.

More sharply:

\[
\boxed{
N_1^I=N_1^D=0,\qquad N_3^I=N_3^D=0.
}
\]

The lower even carriers

\[
N_0,\quad N_2,\quad N_4
\]

may have fixed-sector components \(I,S\). They can feed the order-9 \(I\)-coordinate after multiplication by high-order whitening terms. Thus the remaining lower-carrier risk is not \(N_1,N_3\), but the even-carrier families

\[
N_0,\quad N_2,\quad N_4
\]

together with high whitening coefficients \(X_5,\ldots,X_9\). The attached instruction identifies \(R_{\le4}^I\) as the current blocker after \(N_9,N_7,N_5\) were cleared. 

---

## 1. Parity rule

Use the endpoint-swap involution

\[
s\mapsto -s,\qquad t_+\leftrightarrow t_-.
\]

With swap matrix \(S\), the coefficient \(N_b\) obeys

\[
N_b=(-1)^bSN_bS.
\]

Therefore:

- if \(b\) is even, then \(SN_bS=N_b\), so \(N_b\) lies in the fixed sector;
- if \(b\) is odd, then \(SN_bS=-N_b\), so \(N_b\) lies in the anti-fixed sector.

Using

\[
SIS=I,\qquad SSS=S,
\]

\[
SDS=-D,\qquad SJS=-J,
\]

we get:

\[
\boxed{
b\text{ even}\Rightarrow N_b\in\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
b\text{ odd}\Rightarrow N_b\in\mathbf C D\oplus\mathbf C J.
}
\]

This is the parity-level classification.

---

## 2. Odd lower carriers \(N_1,N_3\)

Parity alone allows

\[
N_1,N_3\in \mathbf C D\oplus\mathbf C J.
\]

But the prior raw finite-\(s\) numerator audits show the odd raw carriers are off-diagonal skew. The diagonal entries are same-point centered quantities and are even in \(s\), so their odd coefficients vanish:

\[
N_{11,1}=N_{22,1}=0,
\qquad
N_{11,3}=N_{22,3}=0.
\]

Thus the diagonal anti-fixed part \(D\) is absent:

\[
N_1^D=N_3^D=0.
\]

The off-diagonal odd raw numerator has the skew form

\[
N_{21,b}=-N_{12,b}
\]

for odd \(b\), so

\[
N_b=F_bJ.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
N_1=F_1J,\qquad N_3=F_3J.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
N_1^I=N_1^D=0,\qquad N_3^I=N_3^D=0.
}
\]

These carriers do not directly contribute \(I\)-sector raw data. Any \(I\)-sector contribution involving them would have to be created by whitening products, not by \(N_1^{I,D}\) or \(N_3^{I,D}\).

---

## 3. Even lower carriers \(N_0,N_2,N_4\)

For even \(b\), parity gives

\[
N_b\in \mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
N_0,N_2,N_4
\text{ may have }I\text{- and }S\text{-components.}
}
\]

They cannot have \(D\) or \(J\)-components under centered raw parity:

\[
\boxed{
N_0^D=N_2^D=N_4^D=0,
\qquad
N_0^J=N_2^J=N_4^J=0.
}
\]

But unlike the odd carriers, the even carriers are not automatically harmless for the order-9 \(I\)-row. An even fixed-sector carrier can produce \(I\)-output after multiplication by high-order whitening coefficients.

Thus the dangerous lower-carrier families are:

\[
N_4^{I,S}\text{ with whitening degree }5,
\]

\[
N_2^{I,S}\text{ with whitening degree }7,
\]

\[
N_0^{I,S}\text{ with whitening degree }9.
\]

These are now the natural components of

\[
R_{\le4}^I.
\]

---

## 4. Classification table

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{carrier} & \text{parity sector} & \text{possible }I\text{-component?} \\ \hline
N_0 & \mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S & \text{yes} \\
N_1 & \mathbf C J\ \text{under raw skew audit} & \text{no raw }I/D \\
N_2 & \mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S & \text{yes} \\
N_3 & \mathbf C J\ \text{under raw skew audit} & \text{no raw }I/D \\
N_4 & \mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S & \text{yes}
\end{array}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
N_1,N_3\text{ are harmless as raw }I/D\text{ carriers.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
N_0,N_2,N_4\text{ remain possible lower-carrier contributors to }R_{\le4}^I.
}
\]

---

## 5. Consequence for \(R_{\le4}^I\)

The lower-carrier remainder is

\[
R_{\le4}^I
=
\sum_{b=0}^{4}
\pi_I
\sum_{a+c=9-b}
(-1)^cX_aN_bX_c
+
\text{correction rows}.
\]

The odd carriers \(N_1,N_3\) are skew \(J\)-type. Whether they contribute to \(I\) after high whitening depends on the whitening sector products, but they do not carry raw \(I\) or \(D\) components.

The even carriers \(N_0,N_2,N_4\) are fixed-sector carriers. These are the main lower-carrier rows to inventory next.

In particular, the next meaningful sector computations are:

\[
\pi_I\sum_{a+c=5}(-1)^cX_aN_4X_c,
\]

\[
\pi_I\sum_{a+c=7}(-1)^cX_aN_2X_c,
\]

\[
\pi_I\sum_{a+c=9}(-1)^cX_aN_0X_c.
\]

These require higher whitening coefficients:

\[
X_5,\quad X_6,\quad X_7,\quad X_8,\quad X_9,
\]

or structural identities showing these rows vanish, are line terms, or are connection/correction rows.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
N_1=F_1J,\qquad N_3=F_3J.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
N_0,N_2,N_4\in\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
}
\]

Therefore the raw lower-carrier parity audit gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{odd lower carriers }N_1,N_3\text{ have no raw }I/D\text{ components;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{even lower carriers }N_0,N_2,N_4\text{ remain possible contributors to }R_{\le4}^I.
}
\]

So \(R_{\le4}^I\) is **not cleared** by parity alone. The next exact target should be the even-carrier whitening rows:

\[
\boxed{
N_4\text{-family first, then }N_2,\text{ then }N_0.
}
\]

# Agent 2 — Gate A / Gate B Correction Audit

under the current fixed-convention Gate A/B hypotheses. Gate A/B correction rows do **not** contribute to

Thus they cannot structurally cancel the order-9 candidate

\[
C_9^{\rm cand}
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I.
\]

The remaining correction-row risk must come from non-Gate-A/B sectors: line terms, background/core, normalization/subtraction, or an explicitly unclassified correction row. The attached instruction asks Agent 2 to audit exactly the Gate A/B correction contribution to \(R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}\). 

---

## 1. Scope of this audit

The raw carrier table has been cleared:

\[
R_9^I[N_9]=R_7^I[N_7]=R_5^I[N_5]=R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{raw}}=0.
\]

So the order-9 \(I\)-row has the form

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}.
\]

This audit asks whether

\[
R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}
\]

contains Gate A or Gate B residue rows.

Gate A covers the aggregate homogeneous scalar-grade closure rows under the active fixed-convention grading.

On the reduced base, the following are fixed:

\]

\[
\text{endpoint orientation},
\]

\text{homogeneous scalar-grade convention}.

There is no residual Gate A \(I\)-component to include in \(R_{\le4}^{I,\mathrm{corr}}\).

All are retained in the current centered reduced-good-patch setup.

and cross-channel walls such as

=

These are restrictions on the base, not changes to the Gate A/B algebra. They do not modify source labels, source/core membership, endpoint orientation, or the scalar-grade convention.

Thus the Gate A/B closures are unaffected by the order-9 visibility refinement.

or any correction row not explicitly assigned to the Gate A/B ledger.

That row is a \(K_1\)-transport / whitening-anisotropy visibility channel, not a Gate A/B residue.

# Agent 2 — Quantitative Good-Patch Reach

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quantitative reach to the layered visibility base is not justified by the current local framework.}
}
\]

Qualitative reach is plausible: if \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) are not both identically zero on an admissible sampling interval, then there are points where the order-7/order-9 layered visibility mechanism is active. But the RH-scale theorem needs more:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The current machinery does not prove this. It would require a Remez/Cartan-type quantitative analytic non-concentration theorem with polynomial control of interval width, complex neighbourhood, function growth, and a non-tiny coefficient/witness. The attached instruction correctly frames this as the next global quantitative obstruction after the order-9 local theorem became conditionally available. 

---

## 1. Objects under test

Let the admissible sampling interval for an off-line packet \(\rho\) be

\[
I_\rho\subset \mathbb R_m,
\]

after imposing same-scale eligibility, strict packet core gap, endpoint separation, Gram positivity, and reduced-core stability.

Define

\[
G_1(m):=\Gamma_G(m)
=
q''(m)-6q_0(m)+2q_0(m)^3,
\]

and

\[
G_2(m):=\Gamma_{G,2}(m)
=
(1-q_0(m)^2)q''(m)-\frac16 q^{(4)}(m).
\]

The desired quantitative reach statement is

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
\max\{|G_1(m)|,|G_2(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is stronger than saying \(G_1\) and \(G_2\) are not both identically zero.

---

## 2. Local analytic avoidance is insufficient

If \(G_1,G_2\) are analytic and not both identically zero on \(I_\rho\), then

\[
I_\rho\setminus\{G_1=G_2=0\}
\]

is nonempty unless the zero set swallows the interval. This gives qualitative reach.

But RH-scale finite-core estimates require a lower bound. Analytic functions can be nonzero but extremely small at selected points. The bad pattern is

\[
0<\max\{|G_1(m_Q)|,|G_2(m_Q)|\}<e^{-Q}.
\]

This defeats every polynomial lower bound \(Q^{-A}\) while preserving qualitative nonvanishing.

Thus qualitative wall avoidance does not close the proof.

---

## 3. What Remez/Cartan would need

A Remez or Cartan argument could work only under quantitative hypotheses.

One needs:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}.
\]

One also needs analytic continuation to a complex neighbourhood

\[
\mathcal N_\rho
=
\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,I_\rho)\le Q^{-L'}\},
\]

with controlled growth

\[
\sup_{z\in\mathcal N_\rho}|G_j(z)|\le Q^M
\]

or at least \(e^{Q^M}\) with compatible constants.

Most importantly, one needs a non-tiny witness coefficient or value:

\[
\max_j |G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M}
\]

for some bounded \(r\), or a point \(m_0\in I_\rho\) with

\[
\max_j|G_j(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M}.
\]

Without this final input, Remez/Cartan only says that an analytic function cannot be small everywhere **relative to its maximum**. It does not provide a lower bound for the maximum itself.

So the missing theorem is not merely analytic. It is zeta-specific coefficient control.

---

## 4. Is \(I_\rho\) polynomially wide?

This is not established.

The admissible interval \(I_\rho\) is cut down by:

\[
\text{same-scale eligibility},
\]

\[
\text{strict packet core gap},
\]

\[
\text{endpoint separation},
\]

\[
\text{Gram positivity},
\]

and

\[
\text{visibility/correction incidence exclusions}.
\]

Qualitatively, if these inequalities are strict at one point, they persist in a neighbourhood. Quantitatively, the neighbourhood might be exponentially small if the packet sits exponentially close to a boundary wall.

Thus we need:

\[
\boxed{
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}
}
\]

or an equivalent polynomial interior-margin statement. The current reduced-base construction does not prove it.

---

## 5. Can both \(G_1\) and \(G_2\) be tiny on all of \(I_\rho\)?

The current local framework does not rule this out.

The simultaneous smallness conditions are

\[
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3\approx0,
\]

and

\[
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}\approx0.
\]

Equivalently, near the layered incidence set,

\[
q''\approx6q_0-2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
\approx
6(1-q_0^2)q''
\approx
12q_0(1-q_0^2)(3-q_0^2).
\]

These are two jet constraints. They are not contradictory with

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g>0,\qquad h>0.
\]

They are also not excluded by packet symmetry or same-scale structure alone. A finite-dimensional zeta-like jet model can plausibly tune \(q_0,q'',q^{(4)}\) close to these values unless additional arithmetic restrictions are imposed.

Therefore there is no current local reason preventing

\[
\max(|G_1|,|G_2|)<e^{-Q}
\]

on an actual sampled path.

---

## 6. Does the centered packet itself give a coefficient witness?

For an isolated centered packet, \(G_1\) and \(G_2\) are generically nonzero. In particular, earlier computations showed that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is not forced to vanish for the clean packet

\[
a=\frac14,\qquad b=\frac34.
\]

But actual \(G_1,G_2\) are full-core quantities:

\[
q_0=q_{0,P}+q_{0,R},
\]

\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=q^{(4)}_P+q^{(4)}_R.
\]

The rest/core contribution can cancel the distinguished packet jet contributions. Thus the isolated packet gives a non-identity witness, but not a quantitative lower bound for actual zeta data.

---

## 7. Same-scale/core-gap restrictions

Same-scale and strict core gap help by making the finite set of relevant packets stable. They do not by themselves impose lower bounds on

\[
G_1,\quad G_2.
\]

They restrict the geometry of selected packets, but the functions \(G_1,G_2\) are nonlinear sums of packet jets and background terms. Same-scale constraints can keep contributions comparable, but comparable terms are precisely capable of cancellation.

Thus same-scale structure may be useful in a future non-concentration theorem, but it is not itself such a theorem.

---

## 8. Conditional theorem that would suffice

A viable quantitative good-patch reach theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
For every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet \(\rho\), there exists an
admissible reduced sampling interval \(I_\rho\) such that:
\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]
\(G_1,G_2\) extend holomorphically to a \(Q^{-L'}\)-complex neighbourhood with
controlled growth, and
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max\{|G_1(m)|,|G_2(m)|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]
Consequently, there is \(m\in I_\rho\) with layered visibility at polynomial
scale.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

But the last line is essentially the desired result. Remez/Cartan can help only if one supplies a non-tiny coefficient or value.

---

## 9. Classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quantitative reach is conditionally reachable, but not justified.}
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need a Remez/Cartan lower bound for }(G_1,G_2)
\text{ on }I_\rho
\text{ with polynomial interval and coefficient control.}
}
\]

The missing input has two parts:

\[
\boxed{
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I_\rho}\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Neither follows from the current local rank-two algebra.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quantitative good-patch reach is not presently proved.}
}
\]

The local layered theorem improves qualitative visibility:

\[
\Gamma_G\ne0\Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

But the proof still needs a quantitative reach theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m\in I_\rho:\ 
\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

At present, this requires new zeta-specific analytic non-concentration input.

# Agent 2 — Remez/Cartan Quantitative Reach Attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{A Remez/Cartan route is viable only as a conditional analytic lemma; it does not supply the missing zeta-specific lower bound by itself.}
}
\]

For

\[
G_1(m)=\Gamma_G(m)=q''(m)-6q_0(m)+2q_0(m)^3,
\]

\[
G_2(m)=\Gamma_{G,2}(m)=(1-q_0(m)^2)q''(m)-\frac16q^{(4)}(m),
\]

the desired estimate is

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max\{|G_1(m)|,|G_2(m)|\}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Analyticity alone gives only qualitative avoidance. Remez/Cartan can promote **one non-tiny witness** to a polynomial lower bound across an interval, but it cannot create the witness. The attached coordinator prompt identifies this exact layered anisotropy non-concentration problem as the current proof-closing bottleneck. 

---

## 1. Target analytic setup

Let \(I_\rho\) be the admissible sampling interval for the off-line packet \(\rho\), after imposing:

\[
\text{same-scale eligibility},
\qquad
\text{strict packet core gap},
\qquad
\text{endpoint separation},
\qquad
\text{Gram positivity},
\qquad
\text{reduced-core stability}.
\]

Define the vector analytic function

\[
G(m):=(G_1(m),G_2(m)).
\]

The quantitative reach target is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\|G(m)\|_\infty\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This would give a point in the admissible interval where either the order-7 anisotropy or the order-9 anisotropy is polynomially visible.

---

## 2. What Remez/Cartan can prove

A useful Remez/Cartan lemma would have this form.

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
Let \(G_1,G_2\) be holomorphic on a complex neighbourhood
\[
\mathcal N(I_\rho,\rho_c)
=
\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,I_\rho)\le \rho_c\}
\]
with
\[
\rho_c\ge Q^{-L'},
\]
and suppose
\[
\sup_{\mathcal N(I_\rho,\rho_c)}\max(|G_1|,|G_2|)\le Q^M.
\]
If for some \(j\in\{1,2\}\), some \(r\le R\), and some \(m_0\in I_\rho\),
\[
|G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'},
\]
then
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max(|G_1(m)|,|G_2(m)|)\ge Q^{-A}
\]
for some \(A=A(L',M,M',R)\).
\end{minipage}
}
\]

In fact, the derivative witness alone already implies a lower bound on a small subinterval via Taylor/Cauchy estimates if the growth is controlled. Remez/Cartan becomes useful when the witness is not at the sample point and one must avoid exceptional small-value sets.

But the key is the non-tiny witness:

\[
\boxed{
|G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
}
\]

Without it, the analytic lemma has no scale.

---

## 3. Required hypotheses

The Remez/Cartan route requires four quantitative inputs.

### 3.1 Polynomial interval width

Need

\[
\boxed{
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}.
}
\]

The current local theory gives only openness if the inequalities are strict. It does not prove a polynomial interior margin from the same-scale/core-gap/endpoint/Gram walls.

If \(I_\rho\) has width \(e^{-Q}\), then even a nonzero analytic function may fail every \(Q^{-A}\) sampling lower bound on that interval.

### 3.2 Complex neighbourhood

Need holomorphic continuation to a strip/disc around \(I_\rho\):

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(z,I_\rho)\le Q^{-L'}.
}
\]

For \(q,q'',q^{(4)}\), this requires avoiding nearby zero/pole singularities of the log-derivative or phase kernel. Reduced good-patch conditions are real; they do not automatically give a polynomial complex margin.

### 3.3 Growth bound

Need a bound such as

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{\mathcal N}|G_j(z)|\le Q^M
}
\]

or at worst controlled exponential growth compatible with the final constants.

Since \(G_1,G_2\) include cubic and mixed terms in \(q\), this requires polynomial control of

\[
q,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

on the complex neighbourhood.

### 3.4 Non-tiny witness

Need some local coefficient or derivative lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{j=1,2}\max_{r\le R}|G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
}
\]

This is the actual missing input. It is equivalent to saying the actual zeta trajectory is not super-polynomially tangent to the layered anisotropy incidence set.

---

## 4. What the current framework already gives

The current framework gives the following qualitatively:

\[
G_1,G_2
\]

are analytic on a fixed reduced stratum.

The local order-7/order-9 theorem gives:

\[
G_1\ne0 \Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
G_1=0,\quad G_2\ne0 \Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]

modulo correction incidence.

But it does **not** give any of:

\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]

\[
\text{complex tube radius}\ge Q^{-L'},
\]

\[
\sup_{\mathcal N}|G_j|\le Q^M,
\]

or

\[
\max_{j,r}|G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
\]

Thus the Remez/Cartan strategy is not yet executable.

---

## 5. Why qualitative non-identity is insufficient

Suppose

\[
G_1(m)=e^{-Q}(m-m_0),
\qquad
G_2(m)=e^{-2Q}.
\]

This pair is analytic and not identically zero. But on an interval of \(O(1)\),

\[
\sup \max(|G_1|,|G_2|)
\]

can still be exponentially small if the coefficients are exponentially small. Remez cannot prevent that without a coefficient lower bound.

This mirrors the bad formal jet path:

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2,
\]

for which

\[
G_1=\varepsilon_1,\qquad G_2=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Taking

\[
\varepsilon_1=e^{-Q},\qquad \varepsilon_2=e^{-2Q}
\]

defeats every polynomial lower bound while keeping

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad q''\ne0,\qquad y_{\rm lead}\ne0.
\]

The analytic method must rule out such exponentially small coefficients for actual zeta data. That is not a formal analytic consequence.

---

## 6. Possible Remez/Cartan theorem template

A theorem worth targeting would be:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.9\linewidth}
For every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet \(\rho\), there exists an
admissible interval \(I_\rho\) such that:
\[
|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L},
\]
the functions \(G_1=\Gamma_G\) and \(G_2=\Gamma_{G,2}\) extend holomorphically
to a \(Q^{-L'}\)-neighbourhood of \(I_\rho\), satisfy
\[
\sup_{\mathcal N(I_\rho,Q^{-L'})}\max(|G_1|,|G_2|)\le Q^M,
\]
and have a non-tiny jet witness
\[
\max_{j=1,2}\max_{0\le r\le R}|G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'}
\]
for some \(m_0\in I_\rho\).  Then
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\max(|G_1(m)|,|G_2(m)|)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]
\end{minipage}
}
\]

This theorem is analytically plausible. But all of its quantitative hypotheses are nontrivial. The most important is the non-tiny jet witness.

---

## 7. Can the centered packet provide the witness?

For the isolated packet, yes: \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) are generically nonzero. But the actual full-core quantities are

\[
q=q_P+q_R,
\]

\[
q''=q_P''+q_R'',
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=q_P^{(4)}+q_R^{(4)}.
\]

The rest contribution \(q_R\) can, in the current local framework, tune the actual \(G_1,G_2\) close to zero. Therefore the isolated packet witness does not produce a non-tiny witness for actual zeta data.

To use it, one would need a theorem like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rest/core contributions cannot cancel the distinguished packet's }(G_1,G_2)
\text{ jets to super-polynomial precision.}
}
\]

That is exactly the global quantitative non-concentration problem.

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Remez/Cartan route: viable as a conditional analytic lemma, not a proof by itself.}
}
\]

It can turn polynomial input into polynomial output, but it cannot generate the polynomial input.

The precise missing assumptions are:

\[
\boxed{|I_\rho|\ge Q^{-L}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{holomorphic tube radius}\ge Q^{-L'}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\sup |G_j|\le Q^M},
\]

and most importantly,

\[
\boxed{
\max_{j,r}|G_j^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-M'}.
}
\]

The last condition is the core zeta-specific arithmetic separation theorem in another form.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quantitative layered reach is conditionally reachable, but not currently justified.}
}
\]

The Remez/Cartan mechanism is not blocked mathematically; it simply requires quantitative zeta-specific inputs that are not in the current framework.

The next exact theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta data provide a non-tiny witness for }
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\text{ on a polynomial-sized reduced sampling interval.}
}
\]

Without that witness, the local order-7/order-9 theorem remains qualitative and cannot close RH.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:21:41)

_Thought for 7s_

# Agent 2 — Distinguished packet versus rest cancellation

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The full source-weighted layered product is fully vulnerable to rest/core cancellation.}
}
\]

The distinguished off-line packet contributes nonzero source and anisotropy jets, but the actual quantities in the rows are **full-core** quantities:

\[
q_0=q_{0,P}+q_{0,R},
\qquad
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R},
\qquad
q''=q''_P+q''_R,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=q^{(4)}_P+q^{(4)}_R.
\]

At leading order,

\[
yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]

So if the rest/core term tunes

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P},
\]

then the source prefactor collapses. Independently, rest/core fourth-jet and curvature terms can tune

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

I find no monomial in the distinguished packet contribution that is protected against rest/core cancellation by the current local framework. This matches the attached instruction’s focus: the next gate is the full source-weighted non-concentration theorem, not more local row algebra. 

---

## 1. Full product under attack

The product is

\[
\mathcal P_{\rm sw}
:=
|yq''|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}.
\]

The leading source factor is

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

Since, in the centred convention,

\[
q''=2A_2,
\]

we have

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{\rm sw}
\sim
\left|\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}\right|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}.
}
\]

The source-weighted theorem would require a lower bound of the form

\[
\boxed{
\left|q_0A_2^3\right|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

## 2. Packet/rest variables

Decompose:

\[
q_0=q_{0,P}+q_{0,R},
\]

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R},
\]

\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=q^{(4)}_P+q^{(4)}_R.
\]

For the centred distinguished packet,

\[
q''_P=2A_{2,P},
\]

and

\[
A_{2,P}\ne0.
\]

Also,

\[
q^{(4)}_P\ne0
\]

for a nondegenerate off-line packet.

But the row sees the full

\[
A_2,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},
\]

not the distinguished packet pieces.

---

## 3. Source factor decomposition

Expand

\[
A_2^3
=
(A_{2,P}+A_{2,R})^3.
\]

This gives

\[
A_2^3
=
A_{2,P}^3
+
3A_{2,P}^2A_{2,R}
+
3A_{2,P}A_{2,R}^2
+
A_{2,R}^3.
\]

Therefore

\[
yq''
\sim
-\frac{(q_{0,P}+q_{0,R})}{36}
\left(
A_{2,P}^3
+
3A_{2,P}^2A_{2,R}
+
3A_{2,P}A_{2,R}^2
+
A_{2,R}^3
\right).
\]

The distinguished packet monomial is

\[
-\frac{q_{0,P}A_{2,P}^3}{36}.
\]

But the rest/mixed terms

\[
-\frac{q_{0,R}A_{2,P}^3}{36},
\]

\[
-\frac{q_0\,3A_{2,P}^2A_{2,R}}{36},
\]

\[
-\frac{q_0\,3A_{2,P}A_{2,R}^2}{36},
\]

\[
-\frac{q_0A_{2,R}^3}{36}
\]

are all same formal source order if the rest packet is same-scale.

In particular, if

\[
A_{2,R}=-A_{2,P}+\varepsilon,
\]

then

\[
A_2=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0\varepsilon^3}{36}.
\]

So choosing

\[
\varepsilon=e^{-Q}
\]

makes the source factor exponentially small while leaving the distinguished packet contribution nonzero.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-factor cancellation is completely possible at the formal packet/rest level.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Anisotropy decomposition

The first anisotropy is

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

Substitute the packet/rest decomposition:

\[
\Gamma_G
=
(q''_P+q''_R)
-
6(q_{0,P}+q_{0,R})
+
2(q_{0,P}+q_{0,R})^3.
\]

Expanding the cubic:

\[
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma_G
={}&
(q''_P-6q_{0,P}+2q_{0,P}^3)\\
&+
(q''_R-6q_{0,R}+2q_{0,R}^3)\\
&+
6q_{0,P}^2q_{0,R}
+
6q_{0,P}q_{0,R}^2.
\end{aligned}
\]

So even if the distinguished packet’s own anisotropy

\[
q''_P-6q_{0,P}+2q_{0,P}^3
\]

is nonzero, the rest/core can cancel it through

\[
q''_R,
\quad
q_{0,R},
\quad
q_{0,P}^2q_{0,R},
\quad
q_{0,P}q_{0,R}^2,
\quad
q_{0,R}^3.
\]

The second anisotropy is

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Substitute:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
\left(1-(q_{0,P}+q_{0,R})^2\right)(q''_P+q''_R)
-
\frac16(q^{(4)}_P+q^{(4)}_R).
\]

Expanding:

\[
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma_{G,2}
={}&
(1-q_{0,P}^2)q''_P-\frac16q^{(4)}_P\\
&+
(1-q_{0,R}^2)q''_R-\frac16q^{(4)}_R\\
&-
q_{0,P}^2q''_R
-
q_{0,R}^2q''_P
-
2q_{0,P}q_{0,R}(q''_P+q''_R)
\\
&\quad
+\text{terms already grouped depending on the chosen split convention}.
\end{aligned}
\]

The important point is that \(q^{(4)}_R\) enters linearly and can directly oppose the packet fourth-jet contribution. Thus if the rest/core can tune

\[
q^{(4)}_R
\]

independently enough, it can force

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

even if the packet’s own \(\Gamma_{G,2,P}\ne0\).

---

## 5. Independence of source and anisotropy cancellations

Source-factor cancellation requires mainly

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P}.
\]

Layered anisotropy cancellation requires two conditions:

\[
q''=6q_0-2q_0^3+\varepsilon_1,
\]

and

\[
q^{(4)}
=
6(1-q_0^2)q''
-
6\varepsilon_2
\]

or equivalently

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

Since

\[
q''=2A_2
\]

in the centred convention, source cancellation

\[
A_2\approx0
\]

sets

\[
q''\approx0.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
\approx
-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

This is not automatically small unless

\[
q_0^2\approx3.
\]

So source-factor cancellation and anisotropy cancellation are not completely independent if \(q''=2A_2\) is imposed.

However, this does not protect the product, because to make the full product small one only needs **one** factor small:

\[
|yq''|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

regardless of whether anisotropy is large.

Therefore the source-factor channel alone can defeat the product lower bound. Conversely, anisotropy can be made small while \(yq''\) remains \(O(1)\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source and anisotropy cancellations are distinct routes to failure.}
}
\]

They do not need to occur simultaneously.

---

## 6. Does same-scale/core-gap prevent source cancellation?

Not by itself.

Same-scale means the distinguished packet and rest packets have comparable geometric scale. Comparable scale makes cancellation easier, not harder, because the magnitudes of

\[
A_{2,P}
\]

and

\[
A_{2,R}
\]

can be comparable.

Strict core gap stabilizes packet membership. It does not impose sign separation or cone separation on the packet jet contributions.

Thus neither condition prevents

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P}
\]

unless a new zeta-specific sign/ordering theorem is supplied.

---

## 7. Is there a protected monomial?

The distinguished packet monomials include:

\[
q_{0,P}A_{2,P}^3,
\]

\[
q''_P-6q_{0,P}+2q_{0,P}^3,
\]

\[
(1-q_{0,P}^2)q''_P-\frac16q^{(4)}_P.
\]

None is protected in the full-core expressions, because the rest variables enter at the same algebraic level:

\[
A_{2,R}
\]

enters \(A_2^3\),

\[
q''_R,q_{0,R}
\]

enter \(\Gamma_G\),

and

\[
q^{(4)}_R,q''_R,q_{0,R}
\]

enter \(\Gamma_{G,2}\).

No monomial has a unique packet-only label after full-core aggregation.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is no protected distinguished-packet monomial in the current full-core scalar.}
}
\]

---

## 8. Final classification

The product is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fully vulnerable to rest/core cancellation.}
}
\]

More precisely:

- Source cancellation can make \(yq''\) super-polynomially small.
- Anisotropy cancellation can make \(\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\) super-polynomially small.
- These are independent failure modes.
- Same-scale/core-gap stability does not prevent either.
- No packet-only monomial is protected after aggregation.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{The source-weighted layered product is not protected by packet/rest structure.}
}
\]

The full-core decomposition shows that the rest contribution can cancel the distinguished packet through:

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P},
\]

\[
q''_R\approx -q''_P+\text{target},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}_R\approx -q^{(4)}_P+\text{target},
\]

and mixed \(q_{0,R}\)-terms.

Therefore the desired theorem

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''|
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

cannot follow from the current local packet/rest decomposition. It requires genuinely zeta-specific quantitative non-concentration or a new invariant that separates distinguished packet data from rest/core interference.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:26:46)

_Thought for 6s_

# Agent 2 — Regime B Source-Cancellation Adversary

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Regime B is formally constructible in the finite local packet model.}
}
\]

The source factor can be made exponentially small by tuning the full-core curvature

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}
\]

to

\[
A_2=\varepsilon,\qquad \varepsilon=e^{-Q},
\]

while keeping the layered anisotropy vector bounded away from zero. Thus

\[
0< |yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|) \ll e^{-3Q}
\]

is compatible with the present local algebra. This directly attacks the source-weighted lower bound identified in the prompt. 

---

## 1. Source factor collapse

At leading order,

\[
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\qquad
q''=2A_2.
\]

Therefore

\[
y_{\rm lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]

Choose

\[
A_2=\varepsilon=e^{-Q},
\qquad
q_0\asymp 1,\quad q_0>0.
\]

Then

\[
q''=2e^{-Q},
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|
\asymp
q_0e^{-3Q}.
}
\]

So the source prefactor alone violates every polynomial lower bound.

---

## 2. Packet/rest curvature cancellation

Let \(P\) be the distinguished centered off-line packet. Then

\[
A_{2,P}\ne0.
\]

Add rest/core packets so that

\[
A_{2,R}
=
-A_{2,P}+\varepsilon.
\]

Then

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}=\varepsilon.
\]

This does **not** remove the distinguished packet. It only cancels its second-jet contribution in the full core.

The current local framework has no sign rule preventing this. Same-scale packets can have comparable curvature magnitudes, and strict core gap stabilizes membership but does not impose a cone condition on jet sums.

Thus source cancellation is a genuine independent failure mode.

---

## 3. Keep anisotropy nonzero

Take, for example,

\[
q_0=2,
\qquad
q''=2\varepsilon,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=0.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
2\varepsilon-12+16
=
4+2\varepsilon.
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_G|\asymp 1.
}
\]

Also

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
(1-4)2\varepsilon
=
-6\varepsilon.
\]

Thus

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\asymp 1.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\asymp e^{-3Q}.
}
\]

This is exactly Regime B.

---

## 4. Gram positivity

For

\[
q_0=2,\qquad q''=2\varepsilon,
\]

we have

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi}=\frac2\pi>0.
\]

Also

\[
h
=
\frac1\pi
\left(
\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''
\right)
=
\frac1\pi
\left(
\frac83+\frac{\varepsilon}{3}
\right)
>0.
\]

So Gram positivity is preserved.

Endpoint separation and core-gap stability are open conditions; a sufficiently small perturbation of packet weights or positions used to tune \(A_2\) does not destroy them if the seed configuration had strict margins.

---

## 5. Are opposite-sign curvature contributions allowed?

For a centered packet,

\[
A_{2,P}=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3})<0
\]

for the basic positive kernel convention. If all rest packets are also centered with the same sign convention, their \(A_2\) contributions are also negative. Then they cannot cancel \(A_{2,P}\).

But the finite local model has two available cancellation sources:

1. **Background/gamma/core curvature.** A smooth background term can contribute positive second curvature while preserving \(q_0>0\).
2. **Off-center packet contributions.** Off-center derivatives of
   \[
   \frac{c}{c^2+x^2}
   \]
   change sign depending on \(x\). Indeed,
   \[
   \frac{d^2}{dt^2}\frac{c}{c^2+x^2}
   =
   -8c\,\frac{c^2-3x^2}{(c^2+x^2)^3},
   \qquad x=2t-\gamma.
   \]
   This is positive when
   \[
   x^2>\frac{c^2}{3}.
   \]

Thus same-scale off-center packets can supply positive curvature contributions. Therefore the sign-cone obstruction does not hold once off-center same-scale packets or background curvature are allowed.

---

## 6. Same-scale and core-gap compatibility

The tuning can be performed with packets at comparable distance scale. Same-scale does not require all packet offsets to be centered; it requires comparable local scale.

Strict core gap can be preserved by starting with a core whose selected packets are separated from the next packet, then varying packet parameters/weights within a small neighbourhood. The cancellation condition

\[
A_{2,R}=-A_{2,P}+\varepsilon
\]

is one scalar constraint, so it can be imposed without necessarily crossing the core-gap wall.

Thus the finite local model can preserve:

\[
\text{same-scale core},
\qquad
d_k<d_{k+1},
\qquad
\text{endpoint separation},
\qquad
g,h>0.
\]

---

## 7. What this proves against the framework

Regime B shows that even if the anisotropy vector is large,

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp 1,
\]

the source prefactor can collapse:

\[
|yq''|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

for every fixed \(A\). Therefore the lower bound

\[
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

cannot follow from layered anisotropy alone.

A proof needs an additional theorem excluding

\[
A_2=A_{2,P}+A_{2,R}
\]

from being super-polynomially small on actual zeta data, or it must use an invariant that does not multiply by the vulnerable full-core source factor.

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Regime B countermodel constructed at the finite local packet level.}
}
\]

Choose

\[
A_2=e^{-Q},\qquad q''=2e^{-Q},\qquad q_0=2,\qquad q^{(4)}=0.
\]

Then

\[
|yq''|\asymp e^{-3Q},
\]

while

\[
\Gamma_G=4+O(e^{-Q}),
\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\ll e^{-3Q}.
}
\]

This defeats the source-weighted polynomial lower bound in finite local models. The blocker would have to be a genuinely zeta-specific theorem preventing full-core curvature cancellation

\[
A_{2,R}\approx -A_{2,P},
\]

not anything in the current local rank-two architecture.
## User (2026-04-25 22:30:49)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:30:58)

_Thought for 6s_

# Agent 2 — Explicit-formula positivity / Weil-form attack

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{I do not find a coercive explicit-formula or Weil-form identity controlling }
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
}
\]

The explicit formula can represent the ingredients

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

as linear zero statistics plus arithmetic/background terms. But the source-weighted residual

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
:=
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\]

is a high-degree nonlinear jet polynomial. Tensorizing the explicit formula rewrites it as multi-zero / multi-prime sums, but no positivity, spectral gap, or prime-side coercivity emerges from the current structure. This matches the attached instruction: the finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel already defeats local Hadamard/quartet structure, so the only possible rescue here would be a genuinely arithmetic positive form. 

---

## 1. Object under test

The source-weighted residual is

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
(yq'')^2
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right),
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

At leading order,

\[
yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

so

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
\sim
\frac{q_0^2(q'')^6}{288^2}
\left[
(q''-6q_0+2q_0^3)^2
+
\left((1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}\right)^2
\right].
\]

This is nonnegative as a real algebraic expression. But nonnegativity is not enough. We need a lower bound:

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The finite countermodels make \(\Phi_{\rm sw}\) exponentially small while preserving the local constraints, so any lower bound must come from an actual-zeta arithmetic property not encoded in the local expression.

---

## 2. Explicit-formula visibility of ingredients

The ingredients

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

are accessible as local zero statistics / log-derivative phase jets. Schematically,

\[
q^{(2r)}(m)
=
B_{2r}(m)+\sum_\rho K_{2r}(m;\rho),
\]

where \(B_{2r}\) is the gamma/background term and \(K_{2r}\) are differentiated zero kernels.

Via the explicit formula, linear statistics of the form

\[
\sum_\rho K(m;\rho)
\]

can be related to prime-side sums against a test function. Thus:

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

are explicit-formula-visible at the linear level.

But

\[
q_0^3,\quad q_0^2q'',\quad (q'')^2,\quad q_0^6,\quad q_0^4(q'')^2,
\quad q^{(4)}q_0^2q''
\]

are nonlinear products of zero statistics. They require tensorized or multi-level explicit formulas.

---

## 3. Tensorization does not give coercivity

For example, if

\[
q_0=B_0+\sum_\rho K_0(\rho),
\]

then

\[
q_0^3
=
B_0^3
+
3B_0^2\sum_\rho K_0(\rho)
+
3B_0\sum_{\rho_1,\rho_2}K_0(\rho_1)K_0(\rho_2)
+
\sum_{\rho_1,\rho_2,\rho_3}K_0(\rho_1)K_0(\rho_2)K_0(\rho_3).
\]

The explicit formula can in principle represent these tensor sums using products/convolutions of test functions, but the resulting prime side is not a positive sum. It contains oscillatory terms, diagonal/off-diagonal decompositions, and mixed prime convolutions.

Thus tensorization gives a representation, not an inequality.

The obstruction is exactly the same as in the finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel: multi-packet contributions can cancel to high precision. Tensorized explicit formula does not prevent that unless it supplies a positive quadratic form or a spectral gap.

---

## 4. Weil positivity does not directly apply

Weil positivity gives nonnegativity of certain quadratic forms in test functions equivalent to RH-type positivity statements. But our desired quantity is not of the form

\[
\sum_{\rho,\rho'} \widehat f(\rho-\rho')\overline{c_\rho}c_{\rho'}
\]

for a fixed positive kernel in any obvious way.

Instead, \(\Phi_{\rm sw}\) is the square of a local nonlinear residual built from phase jets. Writing it as a square only gives tautological nonnegativity:

\[
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\ge0.
\]

The lower bound would require a statement that the residual vector cannot be close to zero. Weil positivity does not provide such a local pointwise separation from zero.

Moreover, if one tries to encode

\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

as orthogonality of a test function to all zeros, the finite countermodel shows that local zero configurations can satisfy the analogous moment constraints. Positivity would need to use arithmetic prime-side information beyond finite zero symmetry.

---

## 5. Positive-definite test kernels

A positive-definite test kernel could prove a lower bound if the residual were a norm of the form

\[
\|T f_m\|^2
\]

with a uniform spectral gap

\[
\|T f_m\|^2\ge cQ^{-A}\|f_m\|^2.
\]

But the residual

\[
(yq'')(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

is not currently identified as a linear operator applied to a test function. It is a product of nonlinear local jets. A norm representation would have to introduce a nonlinear lifting, and then the finite countermodel can make the lifted residual small unless the operator’s range excludes those finite configurations.

No such exclusion is known.

---

## 6. de Branges / Hermite-Biehler route

A de Branges structure could, in principle, give positivity or monotonicity for phase derivatives. But for the Riemann \(\xi\)-function, the required de Branges structure is essentially RH-level or stronger. If we invoked a positivity theorem strong enough to force pointwise lower bounds for

\[
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

and

\[
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)},
\]

we would likely be using an RH-equivalent mechanism, not a derived lemma within the current proof.

So this route appears circular unless a new unconditional de Branges-type input is found.

---

## 7. Could \(\Phi_{\rm sw}\) be a local ODE residual energy?

One might view

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

as an ODE residual:

\[
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Similarly,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

imposes a fourth-jet relation.

Then

\[
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\]

is an energy measuring failure to satisfy a local nonlinear ODE system.

But actual zeta has no known finite-order ODE of this form. A lower bound for this residual would require proving that the zeta phase derivative cannot shadow this ODE too closely. The finite countermodel shows that generic finite Hadamard data can shadow it. So any such energy estimate would again require actual arithmetic input.

---

## 8. Source weighting does not help coercivity

Including

\[
(yq'')^2
\]

makes the expression higher degree:

\[
(yq'')^2
\sim
q_0^2(q'')^6.
\]

This does not improve coercivity. It introduces an additional failure mode:

\[
q''\approx0
\]

or

\[
A_2\approx0,
\]

which can make the whole expression small even if the anisotropy vector is large.

Thus source weighting makes the row size more faithful to the local theorem, but less protected as a lower-bound object.

---

## 9. Explicit-formula route classification

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{object} & \text{explicit-formula status} & \text{lower-bound status}\\
\hline
q_0 & \text{linear statistic} & \text{no pointwise lower bound from EF alone}\\
q'' & \text{linear statistic} & \text{can cancel with rest/core}\\
q^{(4)} & \text{linear statistic} & \text{can be tuned against lower jets}\\
q_0^3 & \text{tensorized statistic} & \text{no positivity}\\
q_0^2q'' & \text{tensorized statistic} & \text{no positivity}\\
(yq'')^2 & \text{high-degree tensor statistic} & \text{extra small-source failure mode}\\
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2 & \text{nonnegative algebraic square} & \text{no spectral gap}
\end{array}
\]

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{No explicit-formula coercivity found.}
}
\]

The explicit formula can represent the ingredients of

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2),
\]

but the representation is nonlinear/tensorized and lacks a sign-definite prime-side or zero-side coercive form.

Thus source weighting does not rescue the lower bound. It merely changes the target from layered anisotropy separation to a higher-degree source-weighted separation, with an additional failure mode from \(yq''\approx0\).

The route would need a new theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for actual zeta data, derived from a genuinely arithmetic positivity/coercivity principle not present in finite \(\xi\)-like models. No such principle is currently identified.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:35:44)

_Thought for 6s_

# Agent 2 — Riemann–von Mangoldt density hardening agent

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Riemann--von Mangoldt density does not block the finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted countermodel.}
}
\]

A density-correct filler can be added around the bad local cluster while keeping its contribution to

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad A_2
\]

either negligible or absorbed as a smooth background. The density condition controls the **number** of zeros in windows; it does not impose the sign/coercivity needed to prevent

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}.
\]

So the countermodel survives this hardening. The missing obstruction must be more arithmetic than zero-counting density: probably Euler-product / prime-side coercivity, if it exists at all. This matches the current direction in the attached coordinator note: harden the finite countermodel and identify which actual-zeta feature, if any, blocks it. 

---

## 1. Density condition under test

The actual zeta zero-counting law is approximately

\[
N(T+H)-N(T)
\sim
\frac{H}{2\pi}\log T
\]

on mesoscopic windows where such an asymptotic is meaningful.

The hardening requirement is: embed the bad local packet cluster into a zero configuration whose local density near height \(T\) is Riemann–von Mangoldt-like, while preserving:

\[
F(z)=F(-z),\qquad \overline{F(z)}=F(\bar z),
\]

off-line quartet symmetry,

\[
q_0>0,\quad g>0,\quad h>0,
\]

same-scale selected core, strict core gap, endpoint separation, and

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}.
\]

---

## 2. Add density-correct filler zeros

Start with the bad local cluster \(C_{\rm bad}\), which realizes either:

### Regime A

\[
|yq''|\asymp1,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2,
\qquad
\max(|\varepsilon_1|,|\varepsilon_2|)<e^{-Q},
\]

or:

### Regime B

\[
|yq''|\ll e^{-Q},
\qquad
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

Now add a filler set \(C_{\rm fill}\) of simple quartet-symmetric zeros outside the selected same-scale core, with spacing chosen so that in a window of length \(H\),

\[
\# C_{\rm fill}\cap[T,T+H]
=
\frac{H}{2\pi}\log T
+
O(\text{acceptable error}).
\]

This can be done deterministically by placing filler ordinates on an approximate lattice with spacing

\[
\Delta_T\asymp \frac{2\pi}{\log T},
\]

then reflecting by conjugation and functional equation.

---

## 3. Keep the filler contribution smooth

Place the selected bad cluster inside a small local core window. Put the filler zeros either:

1. outside the selected core but within the larger density window; or  
2. symmetrically around the local midpoint so their low-order odd/even jet contributions cancel to high order; or  
3. far enough that their contribution to the local jets is a smooth background.

A zero packet at distance \(R\) from the sampling midpoint contributes to the local jets with decay of the schematic form

\[
K_{2r}(R)\sim R^{-(2r+1)}
\]

up to scale factors. Hence, by placing filler packets at controlled distances and in symmetric pairs, their local contribution to

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

can be made:

- negligible compared with the bad cluster contribution; or
- an adjustable smooth background already included in the construction.

Thus adding density-correct filler does not force the local jet vector away from the bad target.

---

## 4. Same-scale core and strict gap can coexist with density filler

The selected core only needs to contain the bad same-scale packets. The filler zeros can be placed outside the selected packet-score gap.

Let the bad core packets have packet scores in a compact annulus

\[
D_P(m)\in [R_0,2R_0].
\]

Choose filler packets either inside a separate outer annulus

\[
D_Q(m)\ge 4R_0
\]

or far enough away that

\[
D_{P_k}(m)<D_{P_{k+1}}(m)
\]

remains strict.

Then the canonical core is stable, while the ambient window still has the desired Riemann–von Mangoldt density after adding enough filler farther out.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{density matching does not force core-gap failure.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Endpoint separation is open

The bad cluster construction can be arranged with endpoints

\[
t_\pm=m\pm s/2
\]

away from all packet centers/singularities. Adding filler zeros outside the selected core does not change endpoint separation. Even if filler zeros lie in the larger density window, choose them away from \(t_\pm\).

Endpoint separation is an open condition, so it survives sufficiently small perturbations used to tune density.

---

## 6. Gram positivity survives

For the bad regimes, Gram positivity was already verified locally. For example, in the normalized Regime A path,

\[
q_0=2,\qquad q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

so

\[
g=\frac2\pi>0,
\]

and

\[
h
=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac83+\frac{-4+\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)
=
\frac1\pi\left(2+\frac{\varepsilon_1}{6}\right)>0.
\]

For Regime B,

\[
q_0=2,\qquad q''=2\varepsilon,
\]

so

\[
h
=
\frac1\pi\left(\frac83+\frac{\varepsilon}{3}\right)>0.
\]

Density filler can be made a small or smooth perturbation of these values, so \(g,h>0\) remain true.

---

## 7. Density gives no sign/cone constraint

Riemann–von Mangoldt density controls

\[
\sum 1
\]

over intervals. It does not control signed or weighted sums such as

\[
\sum_\rho K_2(m;\rho),
\qquad
\sum_\rho K_4(m;\rho),
\]

nor nonlinear expressions like

\[
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Two zero configurations can have the same local counting density and very different jet values. By symmetric placement of filler zeros, one can preserve density while nearly cancelling their low-order jet contributions.

So density alone cannot imply

\[
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

---

## 8. Does density force too many nearby zeros?

No. The selected core can be a subset of a denser ambient configuration. The canonical same-scale core rule chooses the nearest or same-scale packet cluster. The rest of the zeros needed for density can be placed outside the core boundary. If the density law demands zeros near the local region, we can choose the selected core size \(k\) to include the bad cluster and put filler beyond the strict core-gap boundary.

The only way density would block the construction is if the required density forces additional packets inside the same-scale annulus in a way that destroys the strict core gap or forces a sign/coercivity constraint. Riemann–von Mangoldt density does neither; it does not determine precise local positions.

---

## 9. Conclusion for the hardened countermodel

The density-hardened construction is:

\[
C=C_{\rm bad}\cup C_{\rm fill},
\]

where:

- \(C_{\rm bad}\) realizes Regime A or Regime B;
- \(C_{\rm fill}\) is quartet-symmetric, simple, density-correct, and placed outside the selected core or symmetrically enough to be a smooth background;
- the selected core and endpoint geometry remain stable.

Then:

\[
0<
|yq''|\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<e^{-Q}
\]

still holds after retuning the bad cluster by a perturbation of size \(O(e^{-Q})\) or smaller.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{density-hardened countermodel survives.}
}
\]

---

# Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Riemann--von Mangoldt density is too coarse to block the countermodel.}
}
\]

It controls zero counts, not the signed phase-jet combinations

\[
q'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad
\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2},\quad yq''.
\]

A density-correct filler can be added outside the selected core, or symmetrically so that it acts as a smooth adjustable background. Same-scale core, strict gap, endpoint separation, quartet symmetry, simple zeros, and Gram positivity can be preserved.

Therefore the finite \(\xi\)-like source-weighted countermodel survives Riemann–von Mangoldt density hardening. The missing obstruction must be more arithmetic than zero-counting density, most plausibly Euler-product / prime-side coercivity.
## User (2026-04-25 22:40:02)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 22:40:11)

_Thought for 6s_

# Agent 2 — Weil Positivity / RH-Equivalence Audit

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No non-circular Weil/de Branges positivity structure is currently identifiable for }
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
}
\]

The desired coercivity

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

would need to exclude a local off-line packet by proving that the source-weighted layered residual cannot be too small on actual zeta data. Existing positivity frameworks—Weil positivity, Li coefficients, de Branges/Hermite-Biehler positivity, and positive-definite explicit-formula kernels—either do not target this nonlinear local jet residual, or are RH-equivalent/circular if made strong enough to exclude off-line packets. The attached prompt asks exactly whether such coercivity can be obtained non-circularly from prime-side/positivity machinery. 

---

## 1. Target residual

The source-weighted residual is

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
=
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2),
\]

where

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

At leading order,

\[
yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

so

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}
\sim
\frac{q_0^2(q'')^6}{288^2}
\left[
(q''-6q_0+2q_0^3)^2
+
\left((1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}\right)^2
\right].
\]

This is a nonnegative local algebraic expression. But the issue is not nonnegativity; the issue is a **quantitative pointwise lower bound**:

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on admissible reduced good patches.

The finite \(\xi\)-like countermodels show that local Hadamard/quartet symmetry plus good-patch geometry does not imply such a lower bound. Thus any positivity route must use an actual-zeta arithmetic positivity principle not shared by those models.

---

## 2. Weil positivity

The Weil criterion concerns positivity of explicit-formula quadratic forms for suitable test functions. Schematically, one has a distributional identity pairing zeros and primes, and RH is equivalent to positivity of certain quadratic forms over test functions.

A possible hope would be to find a patch-dependent test function \(f_m\) such that

\[
W(f_m)
\asymp
\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)
\]

or at least

\[
W(f_m)
\le C\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)+\text{controlled error},
\]

with an unconditional lower bound

\[
W(f_m)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

I do not see such a construction.

The main obstructions are:

1. \(W(f)\) is a global quadratic form in a test function, while \(\Phi_{\rm sw}\) is a nonlinear pointwise polynomial in phase jets.

2. The terms \(q_0^3\), \(q_0^2q''\), and \((yq'')^2\) are high-degree products of local zero statistics, not a single quadratic zero statistic.

3. Weil positivity strong enough to rule out off-line zero packets is generally RH-equivalent. Using it to prove RH would risk assuming the conclusion.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Weil positivity does not presently give a non-circular coercive bound for }\Phi_{\rm sw}.
}
\]

---

## 3. Li coefficients

Li’s criterion gives RH-equivalent positivity of a sequence of global coefficients. These coefficients integrate information over all zeros with specific global weights. They are not local finite-core jet residuals.

To use Li positivity here, one would need a theorem of the form:

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)\text{ small near an off-line packet}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_n<0
\]

for some Li coefficient, or violates positivity of a finite set of Li coefficients.

No such implication is currently visible. The finite countermodels can satisfy many finite global-looking constraints while preserving local bad jets; any finite Li-like constraint is likely absorbable by far-tail degrees of freedom unless one uses the full infinite RH-equivalent Li positivity sequence.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Li positivity is either too global/indirect or RH-equivalent if strengthened enough.}
}
\]

---

## 4. de Branges / Hermite-Biehler positivity

A de Branges route would be attractive if the Riemann \(\xi\)-function were known to lie in a Hilbert space structure with a monotone phase or positive kernel that forces the needed local jet inequalities.

But that is essentially the kind of structure one hopes would imply RH. A theorem strong enough to say:

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\not\ll Q^{-A}
\]

near every admissible off-line packet would be a new de Branges-type positivity/rigidity theorem for \(\xi\). At present this is not available unconditionally. If one assumes a Hermite-Biehler/de Branges condition strong enough to rule out off-line zeros, the argument is circular.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{de Branges-type positivity is not currently a non-circular input for this proof.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Positive-definite kernels for zero distributions

One might try to build a positive-definite kernel \(K\) so that the local residual is a norm:

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)
=
\|T_m \xi\|^2
\]

or

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)
\ge c\|f_m\|^2.
\]

But the residual vanishes on an explicit finite-codimension jet incidence set:

\[
yq''=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

The finite \(\xi\)-like models can approach this incidence set exponentially closely while preserving local positivity and symmetry. Therefore a positive-definite kernel coercive enough to prevent this would need to use arithmetic constraints absent from finite Hadamard models.

No candidate kernel is currently known that distinguishes actual zeta arithmetic from the hardened finite model at this local jet level.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{positive-definite zero-kernel methods currently provide representation, not separation.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Can \(W(f_m)\) be chosen to detect the residual?

Suppose one tries to choose \(f_m\) so that

\[
W(f_m)
\approx
\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2.
\]

This would require \(f_m\) to encode nonlinear products of local zero statistics. But the explicit formula is linear in \(f\); a quadratic form \(W(f)\) is quadratic in the test function, not automatically equal to the square of a nonlinear zero-side residual.

One can tensorize, but then the prime side becomes a multilinear convolution with oscillatory signs. There is no automatic positivity after tensorization.

So the first obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the residual is nonlinear in local zero statistics, while standard explicit-formula positivity is linear/quadratic in test functions.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Circularity risk

If one did find a family of test functions \(f_m\) such that

\[
W(f_m)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
W(f_m)\lesssim \Phi_{\rm sw}(m),
\]

then

\[
\Phi_{\rm sw}(m)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This would exclude the source-weighted bad local configuration and could potentially close the RH proof. But because Weil positivity for broad test classes is equivalent to RH, the proof must show that this specific lower bound follows from an unconditional positive form, not from assuming the RH-equivalent positivity class.

At present, no such restricted non-circular positive form is identified.

Thus the status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any positivity strong enough to close the local off-line packet contradiction appears RH-level unless carefully restricted.}
}
\]

---

## 8. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{No identifiable non-circular positivity structure.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Weil positivity: RH-equivalent if strong enough; not targeted enough otherwise.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Li coefficients: global RH-equivalent positivity; no local jet implication known.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{de Branges/Hermite-Biehler: likely circular unless new unconditional structure is found.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{positive-definite kernels: no current kernel gives pointwise local jet coercivity.}
}
\]

---

# Final answer

The desired source-weighted coercivity

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

does not currently follow from any known non-circular Weil, Li, de Branges, or positive-kernel framework.

The most precise conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prime-side/positivity coercivity remains the only plausible differentiator, but no non-circular form has been found.}
}
\]

If the proof is to proceed through this route, the next theorem must be genuinely new:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Restricted prime-side coercivity for the source-weighted layered residual.}
}
\]

It must be weaker than full RH-equivalent Weil positivity, but strong enough to exclude the hardened finite \(\xi\)-like countermodels. No such theorem is currently available.
