**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Current source-divisibility obstruction]
\label{thm:current-source-divisibility-obstruction}
Within the established rank-two fixed-sector norm architecture, the local
order-seven/order-nine visibility theorem does not yield an RH-scale proof
gate without an additional source-jet nonflatness input.

More precisely, the known packet-visible fixed-sector rows satisfy
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H=yq''.
\]
Moreover the established tower
\[
X_1YX_{2k}-X_{2k}YX_1,
\qquad
X_1=BS,\quad B\propto q'',\quad Y=yJ,
\]
has fixed-sector projection
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_1YX_{2k}-X_{2k}YX_1
\right)
=
-2yB(X_{2k})_D I,
\]
and is therefore divisible by
\[
H=yq''.
\]
Thus higher anisotropy rows in this tower do not remove the source-collapse
wall
\[
H=0.
\]

There are local and AFE-style surrogate configurations compatible with
\[
q_0\asymp1,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}\asymp1,
\]
but with
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]
For such configurations
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ll Q^{-3C}.
\]
Therefore, taking \(C>A/3\), the desired lower bound
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}
\]
cannot be deduced from the existing local rank-two algebra, Gram positivity,
same-scale geometry, finite Hadamard symmetry, or the current AFE-style
surrogate tests.

Consequently, the present architecture requires at least one genuinely new
input:
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}
}
\]
or a stronger finite-source-jet nonflatness theorem,
\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B},
}
\]
or else a new packet-visible row not divisible by \(yq''\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Scope of Theorem~\ref{thm:current-source-divisibility-obstruction}]
\label{rem:scope-current-source-divisibility-obstruction}
Theorem~\ref{thm:current-source-divisibility-obstruction} is not a theorem
about actual zeta zeros.  It is a no-go statement for the present proof
architecture.  It says that the existing local package has reduced the
problem to a new arithmetic source-jet assertion.  A successful proof may still
supply such an assertion, but it is not contained in the current Gate~A/B,
Bottleneck-C, reduced-core, rank-two, or layered order-seven/order-nine
machinery.

Equivalently, the local theorem
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0\Rightarrow A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\Rightarrow A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]
is a qualitative visibility theorem.  It is not a calibrated lower-bound
theorem until source collapse is excluded.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 4 — Add projective-branch status after source-divisibility no-go

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 3.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Projectivization after the source-divisibility audit]
\label{rem:projectivization-after-source-divisibility-audit}
A natural response to the common source factor is to projectivize:
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}:A_9^{\mathfrak f}]
=
[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}]
\]
where the clean factorization
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]
is valid and \(H\ne0\).  Formally, the source derivative cancels in the
projective derivative:
\[
\nabla\left(\frac{A_9}{A_7}\right)
=
\frac{\Gamma_G\nabla\Gamma_{G,2}
-
\Gamma_{G,2}\nabla\Gamma_G}{\Gamma_G^2}.
\]
Thus projectivization is a coherent diagnostic for Regime~B source collapse.

It is not presently a proof gate for three reasons.

First, the raw projective point
\[
[A_7:A_9]
\]
is undefined at \(H=0\).  The correct object is the source-normalized or
blown-up coordinate
\[
[H^{-1}A_7:H^{-1}A_9]=[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}],
\]
which is a new object rather than the original norm vector.

Second, projectivization does not address Regime~A:
\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0,
\qquad
H\asymp1.
\]
At the base locus
\[
\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]
the two-coordinate projective invariant approaches \([0:0]\).  A higher
anisotropy projective tower
\[
[\Gamma_{G,1}:\Gamma_{G,2}:\cdots:\Gamma_{G,R}]
\]
could postpone this problem, but for each fixed \(R\) finite-prime and
finite-Hadamard models can in principle tune the corresponding finite jet
coordinates.

Third, correction rows are not yet proved to be either zero or \(H\)-divisible.
The actual corrected row may have the form
\[
A_9=H\Gamma_{G,2}+R_{\rm corr}^{(9)},
\]
where
\[
R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}
=
R_{\rm line}^{(9)}
+
R_{\rm bg/core}^{(9)}
+
R_{\rm norm/sub}^{(9)}.
\]
Unless these terms vanish, are absorbed, or lie in \(H\cdot\mathcal O\), the
limit near \(H=0\) is
\[
[A_7:A_9]\to [R_{\rm corr}^{(7)}:R_{\rm corr}^{(9)}],
\]
not
\[
[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}].
\]
Line, background/core, and normalization/subtraction rows have not been shown
to be source-robust off-line detectors.  They are currently best treated as
gauge, baseline, normalization, or nuisance coordinates.

Thus the projective branch remains diagnostic.  To become a proof route it
would require a corrected projective transport theorem plus a global endpoint,
index, winding, monodromy, or holonomy constraint.  None is presently
available.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current architecture ledger after the source-collapse audit]
\label{rem:current-architecture-ledger-after-source-collapse}
The current proof architecture has the following status.

\[
\boxed{\text{Gate A/B are retained as fixed-convention local algebraic lemmas.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Scalar \(T\)-flatness, endpoint symmetrization, exactness,
residue, quotient-only, split-readout, and line-bundle repairs do not close the
Bottleneck-C obstruction.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{The rank-two fixed-sector bundle is the best current local
language, but the \(\eta\eta\) row is affine forcing, not ordinary curvature.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{No global affine transport, holonomy, boundary, index, or endpoint
theorem currently converts the rank-two forcing into a contradiction.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Reduced-base packet visibility is locally layered:
order seven detects off \(\Gamma_G=0\), and order nine detects on
\(\Gamma_G=0\) unless \(\Gamma_{G,2}=0\).}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{The layered theorem is qualitative.  It does not supply the
RH-scale lower bound for }(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}).}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{The established fixed-sector tower is source-divisible:
all known packet-visible rows contain }H=yq''.}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{The source-collapse regime }q''\approx0,\ 
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1\text{ is fatal for the present
norm route.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Fixed-prime and AFE-style surrogate tests support the
interval-local source-collapse countermodel rather than blocking it.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Projectivization cancels }H\text{ formally but lacks correction
control, Regime-A control, and any global projective contradiction.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{The current missing theorem is an actual-zeta source-jet
nonflatness theorem, or a genuinely source-robust new row/invariant.}}
\]

In short: the current package is a strong local obstruction framework, not yet
a proof of RH.  The frontier is no longer the local order-seven/order-nine row
calculus; it is the arithmetic assertion that actual zeta data cannot realize
source-flat intervals on reduced good patches:
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 6 — Add a short “do not overclaim” theorem near the end of the proof-state section

**Where:** Immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}
```

or immediately before the end of the `Current proof state after the local package audits` section if you prefer to keep all global-gate remarks together.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Current non-closing theorem for the rank-two norm/projective package]
\label{thm:current-nonclosing-rank-two-package}
The current rank-two fixed-sector package does not, by itself, prove RH.

More precisely, after the local package audits one has:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a conditional rank-two fixed-sector bundle and local projected connection;
\item a vector-valued affine forcing interpretation of the Bottleneck-C
\(\eta\eta\) row;
\item a layered local visibility theorem through orders seven and nine;
\item a controlled reduced-core and visibility-positive local base, modulo
explicit incidence walls;
\item no source-robust packet-visible correction row;
\item no global affine, projective, energy, holonomy, or finite-core
non-concentration theorem;
\item and no actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness theorem excluding
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|\le Q^{-C}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Therefore the present architecture reduces the remaining proof obligation to
one of the following new inputs:
\[
\boxed{
\text{actual-zeta source-jet nonflatness;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{a source-robust fixed-sector or correction row not divisible by }yq'';
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{a global affine/projective transport theorem with endpoint or index data;}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{a quantitative transported finite-core non-concentration theorem.}
}
\]
Absent one of these inputs, the current architecture remains non-closing.
\end{theorem}
```

## Edit 7 — Strengthen the finite quadrature corollary to cover all derivatives

This is the most important technical cleanup.

**Where:** Replace the current corollary:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Finite same-scale source flattening to arbitrary finite order]
\label{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}
...
\end{corollary}
```

and its proof.

**Replace with:**

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Finite same-scale source flattening to arbitrary finite order]
\label{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}
For every \(M\ge1\), there exist finitely many angles
\[
0<\theta_1,\ldots,\theta_N<\pi
\]
and positive weights \(w_i>0\) such that, with
\[
c_i=d\sin\theta_i,\qquad x_i=d\cos\theta_i,
\]
one has
\[
x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2
\]
for every \(i\), and
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le r\le M,
\]
while
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}(0)>0.
\]
Equivalently, a finite positive same-distance packet cluster can satisfy
\[
q^{(1)}(0)=q^{(2)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(M)}(0)=0
\]
while retaining
\[
q_0=q(0)>0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Tchakaloff's theorem, or finite-dimensional Carath\'eodory reduction, to
the positive measure \(\mu\) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:continuous-same-scale-source-flattening-model} and the finite
list of continuous functions
\[
K_{\theta,d}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(1)}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(2)}(0),\ldots,K_{\theta,d}^{(M)}(0).
\]
The continuous measure has the prescribed moments because
\[
q_\mu(u)=\int K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)=\frac1d
\]
near \(u=0\).  A positive finite quadrature rule reproduces the same finite
list of moments.
\end{proof}
```

**Why this edit matters:** The interval-collapse proof later uses flattening of \((q'')^{(r)}\), which involves both even and odd derivatives of \(q\). The current corollary only states even moments. This replacement makes the proof chain consistent.

```latex
Symmetric placement also kills odd derivatives at \(m_0\).  Thus

\]
```

```latex
\]
Taking \(M\) large enough, this implies
\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)=0

for all \(r\) up to the required finite order.
```

## Edit 9 — Add a concise numerical-surrogate evidence remark

The paper currently records fixed-amplitude zonotope and recurrence-tube reductions, but not the staged numerical evidence. Since the Big Picture emphasizes these tests, include one short diagnostic remark; do not add long tables.

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
...

```

and before:

```latex

```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Numerical fixed-prime and AFE-surrogate evidence]
\label{rem:numerical-fixed-prime-afe-surrogate-evidence}
Numerical fixed-prime and AFE-style surrogate tests support the interval-local
source-collapse model.  In a normalized fixed-prime model, a representative
interval
\[
I=\left[m_0-\frac{0.25}{Q},\,m_0+\frac{0.25}{Q}\right]
\]
gave
\[
\sup_I |J_2|\approx 5.3\cdot 10^{-3},
\qquad
\inf_I\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)\approx4.49,
\]
and
\[
\sup_I |H_{\rm model}|\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)
\approx 4.7\cdot10^{-9}.
\]
Adding prime powers did not block the mechanism; a representative run gave an
interval product of order
\[
8.5\cdot10^{-8}.
\]
A smoothed \(\Lambda(n)\)-weighted main sum plus frozen dual term again
preserved source collapse, with interval product near
\[
8.8\cdot10^{-9}.
\]
Finally, replacing the frozen dual phase by the exact critical-line factor
\[
\chi\left(\frac12+it\right)
=
\pi^{it}
\frac{\Gamma\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)}
{\Gamma\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right)}
\]
and differentiating \(\chi(t)e^{it\log n}\) using the polygamma/Bell
recursion still left interval products of order
\[
10^{-7}.
\]

These computations are not theorems about actual zeta data.  They show that
fixed-prime, prime-power, smoothed-dual, and exact-\(\chi\) AFE-style
surrogates do not supply an evident source-jet nonflatness mechanism.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 10 — Add the exact-\(\chi\) derivative formula as a short technical note

This is useful “ammo” for the next numerical/AFE attack.

**Where:** Immediately after the numerical evidence remark above.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Exact \(\chi\)-derivatives used in AFE surrogates]
\label{rem:exact-chi-derivatives-used-in-afe-surrogates}
For the exact critical-line factor
\[
\chi(t):=\chi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)
=
\pi^{it}
\frac{\Gamma\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)}
{\Gamma\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right)},
\]
write
\[
g(t)=\log\chi(t).
\]
Then
\[
g(t)
=
it\log\pi+
\log\Gamma\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)
-
\log\Gamma\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]
and for \(n\ge1\),
\[
g^{(n)}(t)
=
\mathbf 1_{n=1}\,i\log\pi
+
\left(-\frac i2\right)^n
\psi^{(n-1)}\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)
-
\left(\frac i2\right)^n
\psi^{(n-1)}\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]
If
\[
E_0=1,\qquad
E_n=\sum_{k=0}^{n-1}\binom{n-1}{k}E_k\,g^{(n-k)},
\]
then
\[
\chi^{(n)}=\chi E_n.
\]
Consequently,
\[
\frac{d^k}{dt^k}
\left[
\chi(t)\sum_n b_ne^{it\log n}
\right]
=
\sum_{a=0}^k
\binom{k}{a}
\chi^{(a)}(t)
\sum_n b_n(i\log n)^{k-a}e^{it\log n}.
\]
Thus exact \(\chi\)-differentiation changes the AFE surrogate by explicit
lower-order phase and amplitude terms; in the staged tests it did not impose a
source-nonflatness obstruction.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 12 — Add one “next attack” remark after the source-nonflatness theorem remark

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What would be needed to save the norm route]
\label{rem:needed-source-jet-nonflatness-theorem}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Arithmetic form of the next attack]
\label{rem:arithmetic-form-next-attack}
The missing source-jet theorem should be attacked first in an \(L^2\) or
observability form, not as a pointwise inequality.  A natural target is
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
Equivalently, if
\[
q''(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)
\]
with \(B_2\) the gamma/far-tail/background contribution and \(P_2\) the
oscillatory prime/AFE contribution, one needs a theorem saying that the
fixed-coefficient AFE prime sum cannot approximate \(-B_2\) too well on every
admissible off-line packet interval \(I_\rho\).

A stronger packet-conditional version would decompose
\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R
\]
and prove
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_P(m)+q''_R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that such a result cannot
follow from local positive packet geometry alone; it must use actual zeta
arithmetic, zero-density information, Euler-product structure, or another
global constraint.
\end{remark}
```

This gives the paper enough “ammo” for the next attack and prevents future work from going back to local row algebra.

```latex
\boxed{\text{Scalar, quotient-only, split-pointwise, and line-bundle
Bottleneck-C repairs do not close the proof.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{The reduced-base rank-two fixed-sector bundle remains the best
local language for the obstruction.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{The active }\eta\eta\text{ row is tensorial affine forcing, not
ordinary curvature.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{The layered order-seven/order-nine theorem gives local
visibility, not an RH-scale lower bound.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{The established rank-two norm tower is source-divisible:
known packet-visible rows contain }H=yq''.}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{The source-collapse regime }q''\approx0\text{ with live
anisotropy is fatal for the present norm route.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{Projectivization cancels }H\text{ formally but lacks correction
control, Regime-A control, and a global projective contradiction.}}
\]
\[
\boxed{\text{The current missing theorem is actual-zeta source-jet
nonflatness, or a genuinely source-robust new row/invariant.}}
\]
For the final status summary, see
Remark~\ref{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 3 — Strengthen the finite same-scale source-flattening corollary

**Where:** Replace the current block:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Finite same-scale source flattening to arbitrary finite order]
\label{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}
...
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
...
\end{proof}
```

**with:**

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Finite same-scale source flattening to arbitrary finite order]
\label{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}
For every \(M\ge1\), there exist finitely many angles
\[
0<\theta_1,\ldots,\theta_N<\pi
\]
and positive weights \(w_i>0\) such that, with
\[
c_i=d\sin\theta_i,\qquad x_i=d\cos\theta_i,
\]
one has
\[
x_i^2+c_i^2=d^2
\]
for every \(i\), and
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le r\le M,
\]
while
\[
\sum_i w_iK_{\theta_i,d}(0)>0.
\]
Equivalently, a finite positive same-distance packet cluster can satisfy
\[
q^{(1)}(0)=q^{(2)}(0)=\cdots=q^{(M)}(0)=0
\]
while retaining
\[
q_0=q(0)>0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Tchakaloff's theorem, or finite-dimensional Carath\'eodory reduction, to
the positive measure \(\mu\) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:continuous-same-scale-source-flattening-model} and the finite
list of continuous functions
\[
K_{\theta,d}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(1)}(0),\quad
K_{\theta,d}^{(2)}(0),\ldots,K_{\theta,d}^{(M)}(0).
\]
The continuous measure has the prescribed moments because
\[
q_\mu(u)=\int K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)=\frac1d
\]
near \(u=0\).  A positive finite quadrature rule reproduces the same finite
list of moments.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** the current version only states even derivatives, but the interval-collapse proof uses \((q'')^{(r)}\), i.e. all sufficiently many derivatives. The stronger statement follows from the same continuous model and finite quadrature argument. The current draft’s even-only form is visible in the uploaded draft snippet.

```latex
By Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}, choose the packet
cluster so that
\[
q^{(2)}(m_0)=q^{(4)}(m_0)=\cdots=q^{(2M)}(m_0)=0.
\]
Symmetric placement also kills odd derivatives at \(m_0\).  Thus
\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)=0
\]
for all \(r\) up to the corresponding finite order.
```

**with:**

```latex
By Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-same-scale-source-flattening}, choose the packet
cluster so that
\[
q^{(1)}(m_0)=q^{(2)}(m_0)=\cdots=q^{(M)}(m_0)=0.
\]
Taking \(M\) large enough, this implies
\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)=0
\]
for all \(r\) up to the required finite order.
```

## Edit 6 — Replace the first paragraph of that subsection

**Where:** Immediately after the heading from Edit 5, replace the paragraph starting:

```latex
The local fixed-sector visibility result is now layered through order nine:
...
```

through the paragraph ending:

```latex
\left\|
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})
\right\|_\infty
\ge Q^{-B}.
```

**with:**

```latex
The local fixed-sector visibility result is layered through order nine:
\[
\Gamma_G\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0,
\]
while
\[
\Gamma_G=0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]
outside the named correction and cross-channel incidence walls.  This local
visibility theorem is not the remaining proof gate.  The remaining proof gate
is the source-weighted interval lower bound
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
H=yq''.
}
\]
A more invariant norm formulation is
\[
\left\|
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})
\right\|_\infty
\ge Q^{-B}
\]
on the sampled reduced packet interval.  The source-collapse analysis shows
that this lower bound is equivalent, for the present tower, to a new
source-jet nonflatness assertion for actual zeta data.
```

## Edit 7 — Add exact-\(\chi\) derivative note

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Numerical fixed-prime and AFE-style evidence]
\label{rem:numerical-fixed-prime-afe-source-collapse-evidence}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Exact \(\chi\)-derivatives in AFE-style source-collapse tests]
\label{rem:exact-chi-derivatives-used-in-afe-surrogates}
For the exact critical-line factor
\[
\chi(t):=\chi\!\left(\frac12+it\right)
=
\pi^{it}
\frac{\Gamma\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)}
{\Gamma\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right)},
\]
write
\[
g(t)=\log\chi(t).
\]
Then
\[
g(t)
=
it\log\pi+
\log\Gamma\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)
-
\log\Gamma\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right),
\]
and, for \(n\ge1\),
\[
g^{(n)}(t)
=
\mathbf 1_{n=1}\,i\log\pi
+
\left(-\frac i2\right)^n
\psi^{(n-1)}\left(\frac14-\frac{it}{2}\right)
-
\left(\frac i2\right)^n
\psi^{(n-1)}\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]
If
\[
E_0=1,\qquad
E_n=\sum_{k=0}^{n-1}\binom{n-1}{k}E_k\,g^{(n-k)},
\]
then
\[
\chi^{(n)}=\chi E_n.
\]
Consequently,
\[
\frac{d^k}{dt^k}
\left[
\chi(t)\sum_n b_ne^{it\log n}
\right]
=
\sum_{a=0}^k
\binom{k}{a}
\chi^{(a)}(t)
\sum_n b_n(i\log n)^{k-a}e^{it\log n}.
\]
In the staged AFE-style tests, replacing the leading asymptotic phase by this
exact \(\chi\)-derivative calculation did not remove interval-local source
collapse.  It changed the finite derivative target, but did not create a
source-jet nonflatness mechanism.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 8 — Add background-as-target-shift remark

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 7.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Gamma/background terms as shifted derivative targets]
\label{rem:gamma-background-shifted-derivative-targets}
Let
\[
J_2(t)=B_2(t)+P_2(t),
\]
where \(B_2\) is the gamma/Riemann--Siegel/far-tail background contribution and
\(P_2\) is the oscillatory prime/AFE contribution.  Interval source collapse
requires
\[
J_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
P_2^{(r)}(m_0)\approx -B_2^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]
Thus exact gamma/background terms shift the finite derivative-flat target.
They do not change the type of the problem unless one proves a range,
sign-cone, or arithmetic nonflatness theorem of the form
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|B_2^{(r)}(m_0)+P_2^{(r)}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
No such theorem is currently supplied by the local rank-two package.  On the
microscopic interval \( |t-m_0|\le c/Q \), the background is smooth and is
captured by finite Taylor data, so it behaves as a shifted target for the
oscillatory AFE part.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 9 — Add next-attack arithmetic observability remark

**Where:** Immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What would be needed to save the norm route]
\label{rem:needed-source-jet-nonflatness-theorem}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Arithmetic form of the next attack]
\label{rem:arithmetic-form-next-attack}
The missing source-jet theorem should be attacked first in an interval
\(L^2\)-or observability form, rather than as a pointwise inequality.  A natural
target is
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]
Equivalently, if
\[
q''(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m),
\]
with \(B_2\) the gamma/far-tail/background contribution and \(P_2\) the
oscillatory prime/AFE contribution, one needs a theorem saying that the
fixed-coefficient AFE prime sum cannot approximate \(-B_2\) too well on every
admissible off-line packet interval \(I_\rho\).

A packet-conditional version would decompose
\[
q''=q''_P+q''_R
\]
and prove
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_P(m)+q''_R(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that such a result cannot
follow from local positive packet geometry alone.  It must use actual zeta
arithmetic, zero-density information, Euler-product structure, or another
global constraint.
\end{remark}
```

after the item:

```latex
\item The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that finite
same-scale positive packet geometry does not itself prevent source collapse.
Consequently, an actual proof must use information not already present in the
local Hadamard/quartet packet geometry.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\item Fixed-prime and AFE-style surrogate tests support the same conclusion:
prime powers, smoothing, dual terms, moving \(\chi\), and exact
\(\chi(1/2+it)\)-derivatives do not by themselves impose source-jet
nonflatness.  These tests are diagnostic, not theorems about actual zeta data,
but they remove several easy objections to the source-collapse model.
```

## I would not change these parts

No changes to abstract, introduction, or conclusion.

I would also not add more local row-table, order-11, or projective material. The current paper already has enough. The remaining gap is sharply isolated as the source-curvature observability problem, and the edits above only clean up places where the draft is still stale or where the proof chain needs tightening.
